401 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



St. Vincent's Med. Ctr., Inc. v. Mem'l Healthcare Group, Inc.


No. SC06-1047


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 794; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1595; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 556



September 6, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case No. 1D05-1727. (Leon County).
St. Vincent's Med. Ctr. v. Mem'l Healthcare Group, 928 So. 2d 430, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6201 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee hospital sued the agency for health care administration, contending that former § 408.036(3)(l), Fla. Stat. (2004), concerning an exemption from a certificate of need (CON), was unconstitutional as a special law enacted in the guise of a general law. Appellant hospital intervened. The trial court ruled that former § 408.036(3)(l) was unconstitutional, and the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellee sought the agency's permission to establish a new hospital with an open-heart surgery program. State law required it to submit a CON as a condition for approval. Then, former § 408.036(3)(l), which had a four-year sunset date, was enacted. It created an exemption from the CON requirement for hospitals seeking to establish an open-heart surgery program that met certain very narrowly defined criteria. Appellees argued that as appellant was the only Florida hospital that could qualify for this exemption, former § 408.036(3)(l) was a special law that was invalid as it was not adopted pursuant to the notice requirements of art. III, § 10, Fla. Const., and § 11.02, Fla. Stat. (2004). The high court agreed. The evidence supported the trial court's finding that appellant was the only Florida hospital that could qualify for an exemption under former § 408.036(3)(l), Fla. Stat., and that the process contemplated by the statute would take so long to accomplish that there was no reasonable possibility that any other Florida facilities could use the exemption before the sunset date. Hence, former § 408.036(3)(l) was an unconstitutional special law enacted in the guise of a general law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

402 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Bus. & Prof'l Regulation v. Gulfstream Park Racing Ass'n


No. SC05-2130, No. SC05-2131


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 802; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1597; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 542



September 6, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case Nos. 1D04-3819 and 1D04-4094 (Leon County).
Dep't of Bus. & Profl Regulation, Div. of Pari-Mutuel Wagering v. Gulfstream Park Racing Ass'n, 912 So. 2d 616, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13663 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of business and professional regulation filed an administrative complaint against appellee racetrack, alleging it violated § 550.615(6), Fla. Stat. (1996). The racetrack filed suit, contending that § 550.615(6) was unconstitutional as a special law enacted in the guise of a general law. The trial court agreed, as did the First District Court of Appeal (Florida). The department and appellant intervenors sought review.


OVERVIEW: Section 550.615(6) prohibited thoroughbred permitholders from engaging in intertrack wagering in any area of Florida where there were three or more horserace permitholders within 25 miles of each other. The parties agreed that at the time § 550.615(6) was amended in 1996, these conditions existed only in the area where appellee racetrack was located. The trial court found that there was no reasonable possibility that these conditions would ever exist in another part of Florida. As a result, because the legislature, when enacting § 550.615(6), had not complied with the notice provisions mandated by art. III, § 10, Fla. Const., the statute was an unconstitutional special law enacted in the guise of a general law. Appellants argued that the trial court erred in applying a "reasonableness" condition to the evaluation of the possibility that § 550.615(6), Fla. Stat., might apply to others in the future. The high court disagreed. The proper standard to apply under art. III, § 10, Fla. Const., was whether there was a reasonable possibility that the class subject to the statute would include others in the future. It approved the findings and conclusions of the lower courts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

403 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Strand v. Escambia County


No. SC06-1894


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2007 Fla. LEXIS 1598; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 587



September 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 18, 2008.
As Revised September 28, 2007.
Modified by Strand v. Escambia County, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1745 (Fla., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County - Bond Validations. Michael G. Allen - Judge - Case No. 2006-CA-881.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Escambia County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a final judgment that validated tax-increment-financed bonds proposed for issuance by appellee county after concluding that the county had the authority to issue the subject bonds without first obtaining the approval by referendum mandated by Art. VII, § 12, Fla. Const. Appellant citizen, an intervenor, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted an ordinance and a resolution establishing an improvement district and authorizing the issuance of bonds to fund it. The bonds were to be used to finance a four-lane road-widening project in the improvement district and would reach maturity no later than the 35th year after revenues were first deposited into a trust fund. The ordinance defined the tax-increment-financing scheme that would be used to repay the obligations created by the bonds. The county filed a complaint seeking validation of the bond issuance. The citizen intervened. The trial court entered a judgment validating the bond issuance. It concluded that the county had the authority to issue the subject bonds without first obtaining approval from the electorate by referendum as mandated by Art. VII, § 12, Fla. Const. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the tax-increment-financing scheme to repay the bonds was an indirect attempt to pledge ad valorem taxes as a method of funding the project on a long-term basis and that the county could not do indirectly what it could not do directly, which meant obtaining approval from the electorate was required pursuant to Art. VII, § 12, Fla. Const.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.


 

404 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Kearse v. State


No. SC05-1876, No. SC06-942


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


969 So. 2d 976; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1534; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 525



August 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 30, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Kearse v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2379 (Fla., Nov. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St Lucie County, Marc A. Cianca, Senior Judge - Case No. 561991CF000136A; And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Kearse v. State, 770 So. 2d 1119, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1291 (Fla., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, in and for St. Lucie County (Florida), denied defendant's motion to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and sentence of death, which he filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, prompting his appeal and request for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Upon a review of defendant's evidence, the court first found that his claim that counsel did not sufficiently advocate for him was based largely statements defendant took out of context, and he failed to show prejudice by counsel's other alleged shortcomings. Second, the alleged newly discovered evidence did not exist at the time of the resentencing, and thus, would not have helped defendant's cause. Third, the police did not possess a videotape defendant sought, and his request for the personnel files of a state investigator and two assistant state attorneys were irrelevant and were not reasonably calculated to lead to helpful evidence. Also, a letter which contained the mental impressions of an assistant state attorney about the case qualified as work product, and thus, was privileged. Finally, defendant was not entitled to habeas relief. Specifically, none of a challenged juror's vague memories about the crime, nor her attenuated relationship to a testifying detective, either separately or cumulatively, raises a reasonable doubt about her ability to be fair and impartial. Also, defendant failed to show that the motion for co-counsel would have been meritorious on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying defendant relief was upheld, and his request for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

405 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Sims v. State


No. SC04-1879


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 148; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1226; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 477



July 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 11, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Sims v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1941 (Fla., Oct. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Thomas M. Carney, Judge - Case No. F91-22048.
Sims v. State, 681 So. 2d 1112, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1234 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and armed robbery. The trial court sentenced appellant to death. The convictions and sentence were upheld on direct appeal. Later, appellant filed a motion against appellee State, seeking postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) denied the motion. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with shooting an officer during a traffic stop, but claimed he did so in self-defense. At trial, evidence was introduced that a drug dog alerted to appellant's car, even though no drugs were found in the car. Appellant argued that his counsel were deficient for failing to properly challenge the canine-alert evidence. The trial court found, inter alia, that defense counsel believed any added attention would have placed emphasis where no emphasis was due. The appellate court found that the failure to properly challenge the canine-alert evidence did not represent a strategic choice. Neither of appellant's attorneys recalled any strategic reason for failing to challenge the canine-alert evidence. Indeed, one of the attorneys testified that he was surprised when he realized that there were no objections to this evidence in the record. Further, the defense was prejudiced by counsel's deficient performance, because it was essential to the State's argument that appellant's motive for shooting the officer was to avoid being found in violation of his conditional release by possessing drugs and returned to prison. The State's case was based on this motive theory.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.


 

406 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Jones v. State


No. SC04-2231


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


963 So. 2d 180; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1232; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 479



July 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 26, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Okeechobee County, Dan L. Vaughn, Judge - Case No. 01-CF-371.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Okeechobee County (Florida) convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised four issues on appeal: (1) the trial court erred in allowing hearsay testimony by defendant's girlfriend; (2) the trial court erred in finding the avoid arrest aggravator; (3) the death sentence was not proportional to other similar cases; and (4) Florida's death penalty statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed on issues 1 and 4. As to the first issue, it found that the witness's testimony constituted direct evidence of the group's activities and was properly admitted as relevant. Otherwise, testimony as to the statements of the others actually helped defendant, since it identified one of defendant's cohorts as the instigator of the plot. Further, defendant's statement that he hoped the victim had money, or else they would be "going on a blank trip" was admissible as an admission against interest. But, the court found that proof was lacking that the dominant or only motive for the killing was to avoid arrest in order to support the avoid arrest aggravator. Third, upon a proportionality review, the death sentence could not be upheld based on the single aggravator that remained. Thus, defendant's constitutionality argument was rendered moot.


OUTCOME: The conviction was upheld, but the death sentence was vacated, and defendant was ordered to spend life in prison without the possibility of parole.


 

407 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Heart of Adoptions, Inc. v. J.A.


No. SC07-738


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


963 So. 2d 189; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1236; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 455



July 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 27, 2007


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal -- Certified Great Public Importance. Second District -- Case No. 2D05-5058. (Hillsborough County).
J.A. v. Heart of Adoptions, Inc. (In the Interest of Baby H.), 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 4545 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Mar. 28, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed the trial court's judgment that terminated respondent father's parental rights. It then certified a question of great public importance to the state supreme court about whether in a proceeding on a petition for termination of parental rights pending adoption, the father's rights could be terminated for his failure to file a claim of paternity with the Florida Putative Father Registry.


OVERVIEW: The father, who was the alleged biological father of the baby at issue, became aware of the birth mother's pregnancy about three months before the baby's birth. About two weeks prior to the birth, petitioner adoption agency sent the father a certified letter, which he received, that requested that he contact the adoption agency. The letter did not inform the father that in order to preserve his rights regarding adoption, he had to timely file a claim of paternity with the Florida Putative Father Registry. The baby was then born. The same day as the child was born, the father filed a petition to determine paternity. The following day, the mother placed the baby with the adoption agency. The adoption agency then filed a petition to terminate the father's parental rights. The trial court ordered that his parental rights be terminated. On appeal, the appellate court reversed. On further review, the state supreme court found that his rights could only be terminated based on his failure to file a claim with the Florida Putative Father Registry if he was served with notice under § 63.062(3)(a), Fla. Stat. (2005) and failed to comply with its requirements within the 30-day period.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court found that the father's rights in relation to the child could only be terminated based on his failure to file a claim with the Florida Putative Father Registry only if the father was served with the applicable statutory notice and he failed to comply with requirements of the applicable statutory subsection within the 30-day period.

 

408 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Rubio


No. SC06-157


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 768; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1248; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 464



July 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised October 18, 2007.
Rehearing denied by State v. Rubio, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2116 (Fla., Oct. 10, 2007)
Rehearing denied by State v. Rubio, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1899 (Fla., Oct. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fifth District - Case No. 5D05-846 (Orange County).
State v. Rubio, 917 So. 2d 383, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 20575 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court dismissed racketeering, white collar crime, and all other charges against defendants, holding that §§ 409.920(2)(a) and 817.505, Fla. Stat., were unconstitutional and that patient brokering charges against defendants were multiplicitous. The State appealed; the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed the trial court's holding that § 817.505 was unconstitutional, but otherwise affirmed. The State and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two defendants provided dental care to Medicaid-eligible children who were solicited by the other two defendants. Defendants split the fees paid by Medicaid. A dentist examined five of the children and found no evidence to support the claims submitted on their behalf. Defendants were charged with (1) racketeering and conspiracy to commit racketeering (§§ 895.03(3), (4), Fla. Stat. (2002), respectively); (2) Medicaid provider fraud (§ 409.920(2)(a), Fla. Stat. (2002)); (3) split-fee patient brokering (§ 817.505(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2002)); and (4) white collar crime (§ 775.0844, Fla. Stat. (2002)). The high court saved the constitutionality of the "false statement" prohibition of § 409.920(2)(a) by severing the "should be aware" language from former § 409.920(1)(d) as it pertained to § 409.920(2)(a). The State had to prove defendants "were aware" of the nature of their conduct; State v. Wolland, 902 So. 2d 278 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2005), was disapproved to the extent it held to the contrary. The fee-splitting charges were not multiplicitous. Fee-splitting was not a proper predicate for the racketeering or white collar crime charges, as fraud was not one of its elements.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed the intermediate appellate court's determinations that § 409.920(2)(a), Fla. Stat., was unconstitutional and that the indictment was multiplicitous. It affirmed the remainder of that court's decision and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Darling v. State


No. SC04-2379, No. SC05-2020


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


966 So. 2d 366; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1233; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 486



July 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dismissed by State v. Darling, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1161 (Fla., May 25, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, John H. Adams, Sr., Judge - Case No. CR97-7497.
Darling v. State, 808 So. 2d 145, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 6 (Fla., Jan. 3, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Orange County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief, which he filed in an effort to get vacated his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. Defendant appealed that ruling and also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder of a woman, as well as armed sexual battery. Eventually, defendant was sentenced to death for the murder and to many months for armed sexual battery. His convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Thereafter, he filed a motion to vacate judgment of conviction and sentence pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The trial court found that only six of the claims merited an evidentiary hearing. His primary claim was that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The trial court found that he had not shown he received ineffective assistance of counsel and that he had not established any other ground for relief; as a result, it denied his postconviction relief motion. He appealed and also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus. The state supreme court found that he had not shown that he received ineffective assistance, especially in his primary claims regarding trial counsel's investigation and presentation of mitigation evidence, as well as trial counsel's decision not to challenge the DNA evidence since defendant had admitted being with the victim. Too, it found no ground for granting his habeas corpus petition.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed the denial of the motion for postconviction relief and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.

 

410 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Gore v. State


No. SC04-1458, No. SC05-733


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


964 So. 2d 1257; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1198; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 438



July 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 10, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Gore v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1794 (Fla., Sept. 10, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gore v. Florida, 552 U.S. 1197, 128 S. Ct. 1250, 170 L. Ed. 2d 89, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1551 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County, Dan L. Vaughn, Judge - Case No. 83-361-CF. And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Gore v. State, 706 So. 2d 1328, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1057 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Indian River County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 in a case where defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, the kidnapping of two people, and three counts of sexual battery, and his convictions and sentences, including a death sentence, were affirmed on direct appeal. He appealed and also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice picked up two teenage hitchhikers, took them to a residence, bound them, and forced at least one of them to perform sex acts on defendant. When one of the two hitchhikers escaped, defendant shot her to death. He was later convicted of first-degree murder, the kidnapping of both victims, and three counts of sexual battery. Eventually, defendant upon being resentenced received a death sentence for the murder and life sentences on the other convictions. The convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant then filed a motion for postconviction relief and the trial court denied all of his claims. Defendant appealed and he also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus in the state supreme court. The state supreme court then found that defendant had not preserved his Giglio claim, regarding the prosecutor's testimony that defendant could receive parole at "any time," as his counsel had not objected and that matter had already been decided adversely to defendant in his direct appeal. It also found that he had not shown that he received ineffective assistance of counsel or any ground for granting the petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed. Also, the state supreme court denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus.

Johnson v. State


No. SC04-1972


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


969 So. 2d 938; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1189; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 445



July 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 27, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Johnson v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2258 (Fla., Nov. 27, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. Florida, 553 U.S. 1007, 128 S. Ct. 2056, 170 L. Ed. 2d 799, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3517 (Apr. 21, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Johnson v. State, 135 So. 3d 1002, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 37 (Fla., Jan. 9, 2014)
Request denied by State v. Johnson, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1207 (Fla., May 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County, Burton C. Conner, Judge - Case No. 56 2001 CF 000793A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The St. Lucie County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment on a jury's verdict that found defendant guilty of first-degree murder, kidnapping, and sexual battery with great force. It then sentenced defendant to death for the first-degree murder and imposed other sentences on the other convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant met a woman and went back to his residence with her. An argument ensued between them. A neighbor then saw defendant carry the woman indoors. Other witnesses saw defendant force her into a bedroom. An hour later, the woman was dead; she had been strangled and had bruises about her. At trial, an accomplice testified that the woman had told defendant as she was being strangled that she wanted her children and that defendant had told him so. Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and related offenses. He was sentenced to death. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the trial court did not err in excusing a juror for cause who voiced doubt about recommending a death sentence, that no error occurred in admitting the victim's statement about wanting her children since the statement was an excited utterance, that defendant was properly indicted, that alleged error regarding cross-examination of him was waived, that the evidence was sufficient to prove felony murder, that the evidence sufficiently proved a heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator, that the death penalty was not disproportionate, and that the death sentence was not unconstitutionally imposed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments of conviction and sentence of death were affirmed.

Willacy v. State


Nos. SC05-189 & SC05-2021


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 131; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1141



June 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 11, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Willacy v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1940 (Fla., Oct. 10, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Willacy v. Florida, 552 U.S. 1265, 128 S. Ct. 1665, 170 L. Ed. 2d 368, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2501 (2008)
Related proceeding at Willacy v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 817 (Fla., Apr. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, J. Preston Silvernail, Judge -- Case No. 05-1990-CFA-16062-XX And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Willacy v. State, 696 So. 2d 693, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 558 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Brevard County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's postconviction relief motion where defendant was convicted of first-degree premeditated murder, burglary, robbery, and arson arising out of the killing of his neighbor during an interrupted burglary at the neighbor's house, and, eventually, defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed and also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: A woman returned home unexpectedly to find defendant, her next-door neighbor burglarizing her house. Defendant bludgeoned her, bound her, choked and strangled her, and eventually set her on fire. He then took property to his house from her house. Police uncovered a large amount of evidence linking defendant to the murder. His fingerprints were found on property at her home; some of her property was found at his home. He was charged with first-degree premeditated murder, burglary, robbery, and arson. Eventually, he was sentenced to death. His convictions and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant later filed a motion for postconviction relief. The trial court summarily denied several postconviction relief claims and denied the remaining claims following an evidentiary hearing. On appeal, the state supreme court found that summary denial of certain claims was not error because the claims were not shown to be facially invalid or were conclusively refuted by the record. It also found that denial of the claims was supported by competent, substantial in the record and that he had not shown that he was entitled to relief regarding the habeas corpus petition he filed.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief. It also denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus.

Guardado v. State


No. SC05-2035


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


965 So. 2d 108; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1145; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 382



June 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 19, 2007. Released for Publication September 10, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Guardado v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1839 (Fla., Sept. 10, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Guardado v. Florida, 552 U.S. 1197, 128 S. Ct. 1250, 170 L. Ed. 2d 90, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1518 (Feb. 19, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Guardado v. State, 176 So. 3d 886, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 801 (Fla., 2015)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Guardado v. Jones, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 69976 (N.D. Fla., May 27, 2016)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Related proceeding at Guardado v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1056 (Fla., May 11, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Walton County, Kevin C. Wells, Judge - Case No. 6604-CC-000903A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and robbery with a weapon; the Walton County Circuit Court (Florida) imposed a death sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to killing a 75-year-old woman by beating her with a metal bar, slashing her throat, and repeatedly stabbing her. She had defensive wounds and was conscious at least until she was stabbed in the heart. The jury recommended execution; the trial court held a Spencer hearing (though defendant had waived one) and received additional mitigation evidence. Defendant did not seek to discharge counsel until completion of evidence at the penalty phase. The high court held his complaints amounted to dissatisfaction with counsel's trial strategies and a request for immediate sentencing--complaints that did not require a Nelson hearing. The brutal nature of the crime established the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator under § 921.141(5)(h), Fla. Stat. (2004). That he planned to kill the victim to get money for drugs supported the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator; there was no evidence his drug use robbed him of the ability to plan the murder. As he had a prior violent felony conviction, he could not challenge Florida's death penalty statute under Ring. The death sentence was proportional to other cases with similar aggravators and mitigators.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

414 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Franklin v. State


No. SC04-1267


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


965 So. 2d 79; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1107; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 359



June 21, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 10, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Franklin v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1793 (Fla., Sept. 10, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Franklin v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 140 (Fla., Jan. 16, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, Mark J. Hill, Judge - Case No. 2002-CF-217-A-02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder and attempted armed robbery with a firearm. The Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida) sentenced defendant to death for the murder and a consecutive life sentence for the attempted robbery. Defendant appealed the murder conviction and sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's claims of error, the supreme court concluded, inter alia, that: (1) defendant's hearsay objections to the guilt phase testimony regarding the victim's statements to others did not preserve any Crawford claim; (2) any error in the admission of defendant's statements to a newspaper reporter was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because, even without those statements, the jury heard defendant's confessions to the police, the victim's description of the events and his assailant, and the forensic evidence that tied defendant to the shooting; (3) although defendant stipulated to the aggravating factor of prior violent felony convictions, the admission of testimony recounting those crimes was not error where, inter alia, there was no indication of any kind of emotional display by the witnesses; (4) the testimony of the victim's family members and coworker did not exceed the proper bounds of victim impact evidence as provided in § 921.141(7), Fla. Stat. (2005) and Payne v. Tennessee; and (5) the jury's finding of the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator and the pecuniary gain aggravator was supported by sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


 

415 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Williams v. State


No. SC04-857


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 735; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1106; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 347



June 21, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised October 18, 2007.
Rehearing denied by, En banc Williams v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1900 (Fla., Oct. 18, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Williams v. Florida, 552 U.S. 1283, 128 S. Ct. 1709, 170 L. Ed. 2d 519, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2755 (Mar. 24, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by Williams v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1432 (Fla., June 29, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Sheldon Shapiro, Judge - Case No. 93-3005CF10A.
Williams v. State, 792 So. 2d 1207, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1393 (Fla., July 12, 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder and felony murder and sentenced him to death. The trial court found the existence of four statutory aggravating factors, including the cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) aggravator under § 921.141(5)(i), Fla. Stat.; two statutory mitigating factors; and five nonstatutory mitigating factors.


OVERVIEW: The teenage victim died 19 days after being stabbed multiple times. She told a 911 dispatcher and paramedics that her roommate's boyfriend "Rodney" raped and stabbed her and gave them his phone number. After surgery, she picked defendant out of a photo lineup. On appeal, the court held that her identifications were admissible as excited utterances, § 90.803(2), Fla. Stat., or dying declarations, § 90.804(2)(b), Fla. Stat. The trial court properly allowed the jury access to the State's transcript of the 911 call with a proper limiting instruction. Evidence of the victim's pregnancy was relevant to the issue of consent, an element of aggravated battery, § 784.045(1)(b), Fla. Stat., or attempted sexual battery, § 794.011(3), Fla. Stat., offenses underlying the requested lesser included offense of third-degree felony murder. Although the victim did not die during the crime, the first-degree felony murder conviction, § 782.04(1)(a), Fla. Stat., was proper because she died of medical complications caused by a felonious act. Although the CCP aggravator was error, it was harmless because the court stated that it had not considered that aggravator in deciding to impose the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

Belcher v. State


No. SC05-1732, No. SC06-866


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


961 So. 2d 239; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1050; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 334



June 14, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Belcher v. Florida, 552 U.S. 1026, 128 S. Ct. 621, 169 L. Ed. 2d 400, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12274 (Nov. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Peter L. Dearing, Judge - Case No. 16-1999-CF-1156-AXXX. And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Belcher v. State, 851 So. 2d 678, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1161 (Fla., July 10, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) denied defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence. Defendant appealed from said order and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The instant court first reviewed the denial of defendant's postconviction relief claims, finding that trial counsel were not ineffective in: (1) failing to object to the alleged improper prosecutorial misconduct; (2) making opening statement comments regarding the sexual battery suffered by the victim; (3) failing to object to numerous statements made by the victim's brother, gruesome photographs admitted, and the prosecutor's appeals to the emotions of the jury; (4) failure to call a gynecologist to rebut the State's expert; (5) failing to object to the State's presentation of non-statutory aggravating circumstances; and (6) failing to call additional mitigation witnesses. Moreover, defendant failed to demonstrate any prejudice thereby. Second, defendant was not entitled to habeas relief. The court initially found that his Ring challenge was procedurally barred. Further, counsel's alleged failures to object, move for an acquittal or a mistrial, and the fact that defendant could not demonstrate that his claims would have merit on direct appeal, did not support his request. Finally, the State properly presented victim impact evidence.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's post-conviction relief motion was affirmed and his petition for habeas corpus was denied.

 

417 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Bell v. State


No. SC02-1765, No. SC05-610


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


965 So. 2d 48; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1045; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 307



June 7, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 29, 2007.
Rehearing dismissed by Bell v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1593 (Fla., Aug. 29, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bell v. Florida, 552 U.S. 1011, 128 S. Ct. 535, 169 L. Ed. 2d 375, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11997 (2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Bell v. Fla. AG, 614 F.3d 1230, 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 17112 (11th Cir. Fla., 2010)
Decision reached on appeal by Bell v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 806 (Fla., Apr. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Charles W. Arnold, Jr., Judge - Case No. 94-9776-CF. And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Bell v. State, 699 So. 2d 674, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1060 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) denying his motion to vacate his two convictions of first-degree murder and two sentences of death filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, and petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to discover a tape which allegedly would have demonstrated that the testimony of a key State witness (appellant's girlfriend) was false and coerced. Appellant failed to show that the evidence ever existed, and the girlfriend maintained that she was not coerced. Trial counsel was also not ineffective for not cross-examining a witness to bring testimony before the jury that the witness touched the victim's body after the subject shooting. The witness testified at a hearing and at trial that he saw no other guns at the crime scene besides the masked shooter's gun; therefore, there was no support for appellant's claim that the witness's testimony that he touched the victim's body after the shooting somehow would indicate that the witness took a gun from the body. Appellate counsel did not render ineffective assistance in failing to raise on direct appeal the trial court's alleged error in excusing a prospective juror for cause. The juror seemed confused about several of the questions asked during voir dire, and also reported that he had trouble remembering his previous place of employment because of a stroke.


OUTCOME: The denial of the postconviction motion was affirmed and the petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Dailey v. State


No. SC05-1512, No. SC06-576


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


965 So. 2d 38; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 955; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 293



May 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 10, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Dailey v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1800 (Fla., Sept. 10, 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Dailey v. Sec'y, Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 86800 (M.D. Fla., Sept. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Jack Espinosa, Jr., Judge - Case No. CR 85-07084-CFANO-D And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Dailey v. State, 659 So. 2d 246, 1995 Fla. LEXIS 797 (Fla., 1995)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. He sought postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel, prosecutorial misconduct, and newly discovered evidence. After conducting an evidentiary hearing, the Pinellas County Circuit Court (Florida) denied his petition. He appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Three prisoners testified the inmate confessed to murdering a teenaged girl. The high court held that as the prosecutor merely stated her belief that the State satisfied its burden of proof, defense counsel's failure to object was not deficient. The prosecutor's alleged improper vouching for a witness was in fact a fair comment in response to defense counsel's attack on the witness's credibility. As documents signed by a witness did not prove he testified falsely at trial, the prosecutor testified that she believed the witness's testimony was truthful, and the documents contained unsubstantiated allegations written a year after the trial, the inmate's Giglio and newly discovered evidence claims were properly denied. A statement was properly excluded as uncorroborated hearsay which failed to qualify as a statement against interest under § 90.804(2)(c), Fla. Stat. (1991), because the declarant never admitted to committing the murder or any other crimes. The trial court properly refused to credit a witness's recantation of his trial testimony. Regarding the habeas petition, as the inmate's conviction was final before Ring v. Arizona was decided, his claim based on Ring lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The high court affirmed the trial court's denial of the inmate's postconviction claims and denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Preston v. State


No. SC05-781, No. SC06-351


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


970 So. 2d 789; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 961; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 296



May 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 10, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Preston v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2396 (Fla., Dec. 10, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Preston v. Sec'y, Dep't of Corr., 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60586 (M.D. Fla., May 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, Kenneth R. Lester, J., Judge - Case No. 78-41-CFA.
Preston v. State, 444 So. 2d 939, 1984 Fla. LEXIS 2549 (Fla., 1984)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Seminole County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. Defendant appealed that ruling and also petitioned the state supreme court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the robbery, kidnapping, and murder of a convenience store clerk and was sentenced to death. His convictions were upheld on direct appeal. After numerous proceedings, his death sentence was also eventually upheld. He later filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 postconviction relief motion and ultimately raised 42 claims. Following an evidentiary hearing on some claims, the trial court denied all of them. On appeal, he raised eight issues. The state supreme court found only three claims merited review: (1) involving newly-discovered evidence, (2) that resentencing counsel provided ineffective assistance, and (3) that the trial court erred in denying his cumulative error claim. The state supreme court rejected each of those claims. It found as to the newly-discovered evidence, DNA evidence showing that a pubic hair recovered from his belt buckle did not match the victim, that such evidence would not likely result in an acquittal at a retrial. It found as to ineffective assistance of counsel that he did not show he was prejudiced, and that as to cumulative error, he did not show error as to any individual claim at all and, thus, could not show cumulative error.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief, as well as his petition for writ of habeas corpus.

Jones v. State


No. SC04-726


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


966 So. 2d 319; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 950; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 272



May 24, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Jones v. McNeil, 776 F. Supp. 2d 1323, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29294 (S.D. Fla., Mar. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Victoria Platzer, Judge - Case No. 90-50143.
Jones v. State, 855 So. 2d 611, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1532 (Fla., Sept. 11, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Dade County Circuit Court (Florida) entered judgments that denied defendant's successive motion for postconviction relief and determined that defendant was not mentally retarded in a case where defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder and two counts of armed robbery for killing his two employers in their office. Defendant appealed both judgments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his two employers in their office. Before he died, one of the two victims shot defendant in the head. Defendant was convicted of four crimes, including murder. A competency hearing was held before the penalty phase; several doctors testified. No one testified that defendant was mentally retarded. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for both murders. The state supreme court affirmed. Eventually, defendant filed a successive postconviction relief motion alleging that he was mentally retarded. The trial court, in denying the successive motion, concluded that he was not mentally retarded. Defendant raised two claims on appeal: (1) that the court erred in concluding that the second prong of the definition of mental retardation requires a current assessment of adaptive functioning, and (2) that the trial court erred in concluding that he was not mentally retarded. The state supreme court found that the language of the relevant law, § 921.137(1), Fla. Stat. (2005) and Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203(b), showed that a current assessment of adaptive functioning was required and substantial, competent evidence supported a finding that he was not mentally retarded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments were affirmed.


 

421 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Dillbeck v. State


No. SC05-1561


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


964 So. 2d 95; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 845; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 228



May 10, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 27, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Dillbeck v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1590 (Fla., Aug. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, Charles A. Francis, Chief Judge - Case No. 90-2795-AF.
Dillbeck v. State, 882 So. 2d 969, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1366 (Fla., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and other crimes and was sentenced to death. The Leon County Circuit Court (Florida) denied his motion to vacate the judgment of conviction. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, serving a life sentence for killing a policeman, escaped, hijacked a car, and killed its driver. The appellate court rejected his claim that the trial court erred in adopting virtually verbatim the State's proposed findings of fact and conclusions of law, as the trial court directed both parties to submit proposed orders, and the inmate did not claim he was not served with the State's proposed order or denied an opportunity to object. His counsel was not ineffective for conceding the heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC) aggravating factor; referring to the murder as "brutal" and "terrible" was not a concession of the HAC aggravator, and counsel argued that the murder was not heinous, atrocious, or cruel. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge jurors for cause, as their exposure to pretrial publicity or their views on the death penalty were not sufficient grounds for such a challenge. Counsel made a reasonable tactical decision not to file a motion for change of venue. He made a reasonable strategic decision to present evidence of defendant's prior crimes, as he wanted to soften the negative impact of prejudicial evidence he knew the State would present.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

422 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Fla. Bar v. St. Louis


No. SC04-49


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


967 So. 2d 108; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 762; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 191



May 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 11, 2007.
Clarified by Fla. Bar v. St. Louis, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1943 (Fla., Oct. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Fla. Bar v. Rodriguez, 959 So. 2d 150, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 761 (Fla., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court had for review a referee's report recommending that respondent attorney be found guilty of professional misconduct and that he receive a sixty day suspension and serve a three-year period of probation. The referee also recommended forfeiture of $ 2,277,663 to The Florida Bar's Clients' Security Fund. Complainant Florida Bar sought, inter alia, disbarment.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was engaged in a secret "engagement agreement" with a corporation which he was suing on behalf of 20 clients. The corporation agreed to pay the attorney's law firm $ 6,445,000 in exchange for the firm's agreement not to pursue future claims against it and for the firm to possibly perform future work for the corporation on an hourly basis. Thus, the $ 59,000,000 offered to the law firm's clients and the $ 6,445,000 offered to the firm through the engagement agreement constituted separate funds. They created a conflict of interest when they executed the engagement agreement with DuPont, placing their financial interests above those of their Benlate clients. The attorney made false statements to a judge, made a false representation and committed an omission to two Florida Bar representatives, and deliberately did not tell his clients about the engagement agreement. The court held that it was clear that the attorney engaged in an extensive pattern of intentional deceit. Thus, disbarment was the appropriate sanction. Pursuant to R. Regulating Fla. Bar 3-5.1(h), the referee appropriately recommended forfeiture of the prohibited fees to the Florida Clients' Security Fund.


OUTCOME: The court imposed the sanction of disbarment. In addition to disgorgement of $ 2,277,663, the court ordered the attorney to pay interest on that amount.

Walker v. State


No. SC04-2381


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


957 So. 2d 560; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 765; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 201



May 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part Walker v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 753 (Fla., Apr. 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Charles M. Holcomb, Judge - Case No. 05-2003-CF-32520.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida) of assault, kidnapping, and first-degree murder. Following the penalty phase, the jury recommended death by a vote of seven to five. After conducting a hearing, the trial court found three aggravating factors, no statutory mitigators, and four nonstatutory mitigators. The trial court then sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplices assaulted the victim, drove the bound victim in the trunk of a car to a remote location, and shot and killed the victim. Upon his arrest, defendant gave a confession after signing a waiver of his Miranda rights. On appeal, the court found that (1) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress his statement because the statement was voluntary; (2) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to declare Florida's capital sentencing scheme, § 921.141, Fla. Stat. (2004), unconstitutional because the course of a felony aggravator was based on the unanimous kidnapping conviction by the jury, and the jury found defendant guilty of murder solely on a premeditation theory, precluding any overlap between the elements of the murder conviction and the aggravator; (3) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal because the State of Florida's circumstantial evidence case was sufficient to rebut defendant's hypothesis of innocence as to the murder count; (4) the trial court did not err in weighing the aggravating and mitigating factors; and (5) the death sentence was proportionate.


OUTCOME: The convictions and the death sentence were affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's motion to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and sentence of death, filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to litigate the motion to suppress his confession, failing to present mental health mitigation and evidence of coercion at resentencing, and for conduct during voir dire regarding two potential jurors. OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate relief was affirmed, and his request for habeas corpus was denied.

Post-conviction relief denied at Hoskins v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2636 (Fla., Nov. 3, 2011)

Hoskins v. State, 735 So. 2d 1281, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 801 (Fla., 1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which imposed a sentence of death on him upon resentencing. Defendant had been previously convicted of first-degree murder, burglary of a dwelling, sexual battery with physical force, kidnapping, and robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from his rape, beating, and fatal strangulation of his elderly neighbor, as well his theft of her car. Defendant was sentenced to death for the first-degree murder. Thereafter, the trial court set aside the original penalty phase proceeding (PPP) and a second PPP again resulted in a death sentence. On appeal, the convictions and sentences were all affirmed except as to the death sentence. A remand for a PET scan was ordered, which showed an abnormality. On appeal once more, the court found no basis to reverse the trial court's rulings. The State's use of a peremptory challenge for an African-American juror and a limitation as to voir dire examination regarding "gory photographs" were proper. There was no error in jury instructions on issues that were preserved for review, and the mitigating and aggravating circumstances under § 921.141, Fla. Stat. 2004), were properly considered and balanced by the trial court. The capital sentencing process was constitutional, and the sentence was proportional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Brown v. State


No. SC05-1018


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


959 So. 2d 146; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 659; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 144



April 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication June 7, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Brown v. State, 961 So. 2d 932, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1057 (Fla., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Brown v. State, 14 So. 3d 241, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1207 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Rex Barbas, Judge - Case No. 86-4084.
Brown v. State, 565 So. 2d 304, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 421 (Fla., 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) which denied a motion to vacate a sentence of death under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The prisoner essentially argued that the trial court should have weighed his expert's testimony more heavily and discounted the testimony of appellee State's expert and the trial court's expert based on the testimony of the prisoner's expert.


OVERVIEW: After confessing to the police, the prisoner was convicted of first-degree murder, as well as other crimes. The trial court followed the jury's recommendation of death. The prisoner later asserted that he was mentally retarded based on § 921.137, Fla. Stat. The State and the prisoner presented conflicting expert opinions. The trial court appointed its own expert. The trial court determined that based on the experts' evaluations, the prisoner was not mentally retarded. The prisoner had seen numerous mental health experts since he was 10. Several IQ tests placed him in the mildly mentally retarded range, and there were references as to some deficits in his adaptive functioning skills. On the other hand, some of his IQ scores were higher than what a mentally retarded person would have, particularly as to his performance IQ. The trial court clearly found that the prisoner's expert was not as credible as the other expert witnesses. The appellate court held that after all conflicts in the evidence and all reasonable inferences were resolved in favor of the trial court's decision, there was competent, substantial evidence to support the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Rogers v. State


No. SC05-732, No. SC05-1730


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


957 So. 2d 538; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 13; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 263



January 18, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised May 24, 2007.

Released for Publication May 24, 2007.
Rehearing denied by, Motion granted by Rogers v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 949 (Fla., May 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Rex M. Barbas, Judge -- Case No. 95-15314. And an Original Proceeding -- Habeas Corpus.
Rogers v. State, 783 So. 2d 980, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 407 (Fla., 2001)



DISPOSITION: The trial court's judgment was affirmed. Additionally, the state supreme court denied defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief requesting that defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death be vacated. Defendant appealed and also petitioned the state supreme court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The victim and defendant met at a bar. They then left when defendant asked for a ride. Defendant was later seen at a motel packing the victim's car. He then made an effort to keep anyone from going into the room he was staying in. He left the motel alone in the victim's auto. The next day, a cleaning person went into the room defendant had rented and found the victim dead from two stab wounds. The victim's wallet was found at a highway rest area with defendant's fingerprints on it. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed robbery, and grand theft of a motor vehicle. The jury unanimously recommended the death penalty and the trial court sentenced him to death. His convictions and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. On his amended motion for postconviction relief, the trial court denied his request for relief. On review of that ruling, the state supreme court found that he had not shown that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, he had not shown that newly-discovered evidence would lead to his acquittal on retrial, he had not shown any other error, and the petition he filed for habeas corpus relief did not show any viable claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed. Additionally, the state supreme court denied defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


 

429 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Ratner


Nos. SC05-1007 & SC05-1009


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


948 So. 2d 700; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 23



January 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
On remand at, Transferred by, Certificate for question declined at State v. Ratner, 953 So. 2d 36, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 4589 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. And an Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fourth District - Case No. 4D04-2513. (Palm Beach County).
State v. Ratner, 902 So. 2d 267, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 7401 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which declared invalid portions of § 924.07(1), Fla. Stat. (2003), as applied to appeals to the district courts. The State had sought review in the district court of a county court's denial of a motion in limine based on a hearsay issue. The county court had certified that issue as a question of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: The county court denied the State's motion to admit as an excited utterance a statement by a domestic battery victim. Its ruling was based on the U.S. Supreme Court decision in Crawford. After briefing, the district court dismissed the appeal and transferred the case to a circuit court, holding that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the matter under Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(c). In doing so, the district court declared unconstitutional the provisions of § 924.07(1), Fla. Stat. (2003) that the State relied on for jurisdiction because they had not been adopted in the appellate rule. The supreme court reversed. Section 924.07 constituted the general law enacted by the state legislature that, pursuant to Art. V, § 5(b), Fla. Const., governed appeals by the State to circuit courts. The State could appeal the county court's limine order to a circuit court under § 924.07(1)(h), (l), Fla. Stat. and Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(c)(2). Thus, because the order was "otherwise appealable to the circuit court" under Rule 9.140(c)(2), and because it had been certified as a question of great public importance, the district court had jurisdiction to consider the appeal under Fla. R. App. P. 9.030(b)(4)(B).


OUTCOME: The district court's decision regarding its jurisdiction was reversed and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings consistent with the supreme court's opinion.

Peede v. State


No. SC04-2094, No. SC05-1885


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


955 So. 2d 480; 2007 Fla. LEXIS 4; 32 Fla. L. Weekly S 33



January 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 23, 2007.
As Corrected April 26, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Peede v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 799 (Fla., Apr. 23, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Peede v. Florida, 552 U.S. 1044, 128 S. Ct. 656, 169 L. Ed. 2d 518, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12683 (2007)
Subsequent appeal at Peede v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 825 (Fla., Apr. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, C. Alan Lawson, Judge - Case No. CR83-001682.
Peede v. State, 748 So. 2d 253, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1368 (Fla., 1999)



DISPOSITION: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's postconviction motion and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which denied defendant's postconviction motion to vacate his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death. Defendant also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. The court had upheld defendant's conviction and sentence on direct appeal, and the United States Supreme Court denied defendant's petition for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from the killing of his wife. Defendant asserted that he was not competent to stand trial, but the court determined that the trial court entertained multiple motions from the defense regarding defendant's competency, ordered defendant to a psychiatric facility to be observed even after finding him competent, held multiple hearings during which the issue was discussed, and considered various experts' testimony and written reports. Further, the court held that the record supported the trial court's ruling that defendant was competent to proceed in postconviction proceedings, and that any difficulties in communicating with counsel were of defendant's own choosing rather than due to any mental defects. Because defendant would not assist his counsel in providing any mitigating evidence or circumstances, defendant was precluded from complaining of the same. Ultimately, the trial court concluded that defendant counsel's performance, although not perfect, was adequate to meet the demands of Strickland. With regard to the petition for a writ of habeas corpus, the court found no merit in any challenge raised by defendant as no prejudice was shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's postconviction motion and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.
