PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case Nos. 3D00-3206, 3D00-3207, 3D00-3208, 3D00-3210, 3D00-3212, 3D00-3215, and 3D00-3400 (Dade County).
Engle v. Liggett Group, Inc., 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1480 (Fla., July 6, 2006)
Liggett Group Inc. v. Engle, 853 So. 2d 434, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7500 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., May 21, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant class representatives filed a class action against appellees, major domestic cigarette companies and two industry organizations (tobacco), for compensatory and punitive damages for injuries allegedly caused by smoking. The trial court awarded compensatory damages and punitive damages. The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed the final judgment with instructions that the class be decertified. The representatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that (1) res judicata did not bar the class action punitive damages claim due to a Florida Settlement Agreement as the class relied on legal theories that were based on injuries personal to the class members to support the punitive damages claim; (2) due process was violated by the jury determining a lump sum punitive damages amount before the total compensatory damages amount for the class was determined; (3) the trial court erred by allowing the jury to consider entitlement to punitive damages before finding that the representatives had established causation and reliance; (4) the district court erred in nullifying its previous affirmance of the certification order as Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(d)(1) did not authorize the subsequent (and different) appellate panel to substitute its judgment for that of the prior panel and reverse the trial court's certification order after the trial court entered its final judgment after Phase II of the trial plan; and (5) continued class action treatment for Phase III of the trial plan was not feasible under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(3) as individualized issues of legal causation, comparative fault, and damages predominated.


OUTCOME: The district court's reversal of the class action punitive damages award was affirmed, but the remainder of the court's decision was quashed. The compensatory damages award for two of the representatives was reinstated, the compensatory damages award for the third representative was vacated, the compensatory damages award was reversed as two companies, findings were affirmed, and the case was remanded for decertification and further proceedings.

 

432 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Roach


No. SC04-2313


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


945 So. 2d 1160; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2877; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 840



December 14, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case No. 2D03-201. (Polk County).
Roach v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 892 So. 2d 1107, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17036 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee accident victim sued appellant insurer for underinsured motorist benefits under an insurance policy. The trial court granted summary judgment to the insurer. On review, the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) invalidated an exclusion contained in the policy that, although permitted in the state where the policy was executed, was not permissible under Florida law. The court then certified a question of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: The insureds lived in their homesteaded residence in another state, where they purchased from their local insurance agent an automobile policy covering their cars. The insureds purchased a second home in Florida, and began spending several months there each year. The accident victims, who were winter neighbors of the insureds in Florida, were passengers in the insureds' car when it crashed with another car. The accident victims then sought underinsured motorist benefits under the insureds' policy. The state supreme court found that the district court erroneously applied a significant connection test to determine whether Florida bore a significant connection to the insurance coverage. However, the supreme court, in applying the lex loci rule instead of the significant connection test, found that the public policy exception to the lex loci rule required both the involvement of a Florida citizen in need of protection and the existence of a paramount Florida public policy. Thus, because the insureds were not permanent residents of Florida, the public policy exception to the lex loci rule did not apply. Accordingly, the exclusion contained in the policy was valid.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court answered the certified question in the negative and quashed the decision below.


 

433 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Golphin v. State


No. SC03-554


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


945 So. 2d 1174; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2878; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 845



December 14, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for certiorari filed at, 03/09/2007
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Golphin v. Fla., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10155 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Fifth District - Case No. 5D02-1848 (Volusia County).
Golphin v. State, 838 So. 2d 705, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 2850 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Up for review was a decision from the Fifth District Court of Appeal, which certified a direct conflict with a decision in the Fourth District, and affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress drug evidence discovered on his person, entered by the Circuit Court of Volusia County's (Florida), during the course of a search incident to his arrest on an outstanding warrant.


OVERVIEW: The legal question presented herein was whether defendant had been "seized" at any point, as that term was defined under the Fourth Amendment, considering the totality of circumstances surrounding his contact with law enforcement. The instant court held that, upon such consideration, defendant was not seized when a police officer held defendant's identification, which he consensually and voluntarily provided, and viewed the same, as she conducted a computerized check for warrants in his presence. Second, neither defendant nor the officer moved away from the location where defendant produced said identification. Further, even if a seizure had occurred, the evidence discovered during a subsequent search of defendant's person was not subject to suppression, as the existence of a valid arrest warrant removed any illegality, and, absent any evidence of bad faith on the part of the officers, the search was incident to defendant's lawful arrest. Finally, retention of defendant's identification would not have constrained his ability to either request the return of the identification or simply end the encounter by walking away.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Fifth District below, which affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress, was approved.


 

434 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Jones v. State


No. SC04-2217, No. SC05-1612


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


949 So. 2d 1021; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2881; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 862



December 14, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 15, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Jones v. McDonough, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 394 (Fla., Feb. 15, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Jones v. McNeil, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 37635 (M.D. Fla., Mar. 9, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, William Arthur Wilkes, Judge - Case No. 95-1632 And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Jones v. State, 748 So. 2d 1012, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1987 (Fla., 1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner, who was convicted of first-degree murder, robbery and kidnapping, and was given the death penalty, sought review of the denial by the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) of his motion for postconviction relief. He also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The prisoner made several claims asserting ineffective assistance of trial counsel and appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: The victim was abducted from a parking lot. Her body was found abandoned in a wooded area. Two days later, the prisoner stole $ 600 from the victim's ATM account. The prisoner, who had scratches on his face was apprehended driving the victim's car. He had bloody scratches on his face and was almost conclusively the victim's blood. The prisoner confessed to a detective that he committed the murder and took the police to her body. The appellate court held the prisoner failed to demonstrate that trial counsel was ineffective. Because the prosecutor's comments were not improper, the lack of an objection by trial counsel did not constitute ineffective assistance. Trial counsel was not deficient in failing to object to the State's opening statements and closing arguments because they were fair comments on the evidence. Because the trial court correctly denied the claims of ineffective assistance of counsel, there was no cumulative error. As to appellate counsel, there was no failure to conduct any meaningful investigation into mitigation. Mental health mitigation was vigorously pursued, the jury was instructed on statutory mitigation, and the trial court found mitigation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

435 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Diaz v. State


Nos. SC06-2259 & SC06-2305, No. SC06-2313, No. SC06-2325


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


945 So. 2d 1136; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2810; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 833



December 8, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 11, 2006. As Corrected December 14, 2006.
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Stay denied by Diaz v. McDonough, 472 F.3d 849, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 30533 (11th Cir. Fla., Dec. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Four Cases: Two Appeals from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Amy Steele Donner, Judge - Case No. 83-18931-B.

An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.

And an Original Proceeding - All Writs.
Diaz v. Dugger, 719 So. 2d 865, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1043 (Fla., 1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Dade County Circuit Court (Florida), in a death penalty case, denied petitioner's motions for postconviction relief and requests for public records. Petitioner appealed and also filed petitions with the state supreme court pursuant to the state supreme court's authority to issue writs of habeas corpus and all writs necessary to the complete exercise of the state supreme court's jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder, four counts of kidnapping, two counts of armed robbery, one count of attempted robbery, and one count of possessing a firearm during the commission of a felony based on his participation in the holdup of a bar many years earlier. The holdup was by three men. No one witnessed who actually shot and killed the victim. The jury found petitioner guilty. The trial court followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced petitioner to death. On direct appeal, the state supreme court affirmed the death sentence. In post-conviction proceedings, the trial court denied his postconviction relief request made pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 and his public records request made under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.852. Petitioner appealed those rulings and also petitioned the state supreme court for habeas corpus and all writs relief. The state supreme court found that petitioner had not established a ground under which post-conviction relief was warranted and none of the public records that he requested would help his case. It also found that he had not shown entitlement to relief pursuant to his habeas corpus and all writs petitions.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief, as well as petitioner's public records request. The state supreme court also denied the petitions of petitioner for habeas corpus relief and all writs relief.


 

436 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Inquiry Concerning a Judge (Holder)


No. SC03-1171


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


945 So. 2d 1130; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2808; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 828



December 7, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 14, 2006.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Florida Judicial Qualifications Commission (JQC) filed formal charges against respondent judge, who had been accused of plagiarism. After a JQC hearing panel voted unanimously to dismiss the charges, it recommended that the present court award costs to the judge. The judge filed a motion for attorney's fees, which the JQC challenged.


OVERVIEW: The judge argued that he was entitled to receive attorney's fees under the Thornber doctrine, which stated that for public officials to be entitled to representation at public expense, the litigation had to arise out of or in connection with the performance of their official duties and serve a public purpose. The court stated that the doctrine did not apply to JQC proceedings. Under Art. V, § 12(c), Fla. Const., the court could award costs to a prevailing party in JQC proceedings, but the constitution was silent with regard to the court's authority to award attorney's fees in such proceedings. The express constitutional vesting of authority in the court to grant costs in JQC proceedings implied that the court was without similar authority to grant attorney's fees in JQC proceedings. This did not violate the principle that the court should avoid constitutional questions when possible; rather, it acknowledged that before the court could take action, the Florida Constitution had to give it the power to do so. This was consistent with the concept of judicial restraint.


OUTCOME: The court denied the judge's motion for attorney's fees.


 

437 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Simmons v. State


No. SC04-2375


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


944 So. 2d 317; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2684; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 794



November 16, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Invalidity First District - Case No. 1D02-4977 (Columbia County).
Simmons v. State, 886 So. 2d 399, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17297 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest in the trial court to luring or enticing a child by use of an online service in violation of § 847.0135, Fla. Stat. (2002), and to transmission of material harmful to a minor in violation of § 847.0138, Fla. Stat. (2002). The Florida First District Court of Appeal denied defendant's constitutional challenges to §§ 847.0135 and 847.0138, Fla. Stat, and declared the statutes to be valid. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the transmission statute, § 847.0138, Fla. Stat., violated free speech principles, was overbroad under U.S. Const. amend. I and Fla. Const. art. I, § 4, and was vague under the Due Process Clause in U.S. Const. amend. V and Fla. Const. art. I, § 9. He further contended that both the transmission statute and the luring statute, § 847.0135, Fla. Stat., violated the Dormant Commerce Clause under U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The state supreme court found that, because the transmission statute only applied to electronic mail sent to a specific individual that a defendant actually knew was a minor or believed was a minor, the transmission statute did not suppress adult-to-adult speech. Further, the scope of the statute was sufficiently limited by its terms, thereby negating defendant's vagueness and overbreadth challenges. Finally, neither statute violated the Dormant Commerce Clause because the Florida dissemination statute at issue here applied only to electronic mail which was harmful to minors that the sender knew or believed was a minor located in Florida, and any burden that the luring statute placed on interstate commerce was incidental.


OUTCOME: The decision reached by the district court was approved.


 

438 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Sliney v. State


No. SC05-13, No. SC05-1462


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


944 So. 2d 270; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2608; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 776



November 9, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Charlotte County, Donald E. Pellecchia, Judge - Case No. 92-451CFA-DEP And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Sliney v. State, 699 So. 2d 662, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1055 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner sentenced to death, appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Charlotte County, Florida, denying his pro se motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner's claim of ineffective assistance in his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion based on counsel's previous representation of a State witness as constituting a conflict of interest was unavailing because the prisoner did not show how the prior representation adversely affected his own case. As for his claim that counsel was ineffective for not presenting expert testimony or evidence of the prisoner's substance abuse in mitigation during the penalty phase did not merit relief because both decisions were strategic. In support of his habeas petition, the prisoner alleged that appellate counsel was ineffective. But counsel was not ineffective by not raising on direct appeal the State's introduction of collateral crime evidence because the evidence was admissible under § 90.404(2)(a), Fla. Stat. (1996), and provided no meritorious claim for appeal. Counsel was justified by not appealing the admission of alleged hearsay testimony because the challenged testimony was not hearsay, and the statements were not prejudicial to the prisoner's case. A mistake by the prosecutor in his closing argument was not intended to impugn defense counsel and provided no basis for habeas relief.


OUTCOME: The denial of the prisoner's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed, and the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

439 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Vosilla v. Rosado


No. SC05-1778


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


944 So. 2d 289; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2612; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 757



November 9, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Fifth District - Case No. 5D04-2617 (Seminole County).
Rosado v. Vosilla, 909 So. 2d 505, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13384 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tax sale purchasers filed a quiet title action against respondent property owners. The trial court entered judgment for the purchasers. The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed, finding that the notice of the tax sale sent to the owners pursuant to § 197.522(1), Fla. Stat. (2000), did not satisfy due process because it was sent to their former address. The purchasers appealed.


OVERVIEW: Although the owners notified both the tax collector and the clerk of court of their change of address, their address was not updated in the tax assessment roll, and the clerk sent the notice required by § 197.522(1) to their old address. The intermediate appellate court held that the notice was defective; it was not reasonably calculated to apprise the owners of the sale because the tax collector knew or should have known that the address listed on the tax assessment roll was incorrect. The high court agreed. As the owners sent change of address notices, the return receipt for the statutory notice the clerk mailed was signed by someone other than the owners, and the sheriff provided written notice to the clerk that the owners no longer resided at the old address, the clerk received unique information about the intended recipients that warranted some additional action. Therefore, due process under the Fourteenth Amendment required the clerk to take additional reasonable steps to notify the owners of the tax deed sale. The high court rejected the contrary reasoning of Alwani v. Slocum, 540 So. 2d 908 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1989).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

Garcia v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


949 So. 2d 980; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2614; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 769

Writ of habeas corpus denied Garcia v. McDonough, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 31429 (S.D. Fla., Apr. 4, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Garcia v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 912 (Fla., May 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Diane Ward, Judge - Case No. 85-23640B And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Garcia v. Florida, 515 U.S. 1137, 115 S. Ct. 2570, 132 L. Ed. 2d 822, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 3927 (1995)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) of murdering two women. The trial court imposed two death sentences. After defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal, defendant then filed a motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion. He also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous errors regarding his trial and appellate proceedings. On the appeal of the postconviction motion, the court found that (1) the trial court did not err by accepting defendant's waiver of his penalty phase claims as defendant waived his penalty phase claims knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily; (2) no conflict of interest existed regarding defense counsel at trial in light of defendant's informed consent; (3) defendant was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing regarding public records of witness interviews because a law enforcement agency expressly denied that the records existed; and (4) defendant failed to show ineffective assistance of trial counsel as to the presentment of the familial relationship between three witnesses, the impeachment of witnesses, the existence of other suspects, defendant's intoxication defense, and the cross-examination of a witness. In the review of the habeas petition, the court found that defendant failed to show ineffective assistance of appellate counsel as to ensuring the complete record on appeal, challenging victim impact testimony, challenging evidentiary rulings, and challenging the limitation of cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's postconviction motion was affirmed. Defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

441 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Hosty


No. SC03-511, No. SC03-512


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


944 So. 2d 255; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2615; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 783



November 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 9, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity And an Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-3457 (Broward County).
State v. Hosty, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1026 (Fla., June 8, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) declared § 90.803(24), Fla. Stat. (2001) invalid and certified the following question for review: As it applied to a disabled adult, was § 90-803(24) violative of a criminal defendant's right to confront witnesses under the Florida and U.S. Constitutions? The instant matter followed.


OVERVIEW: After restating the question to read whether § 90.803(24), Fla. Stat. (2001), as it applied to a mentally disabled adult who non-testimonial hearsay statement met certain qualifications of reliability, violated a criminal defendant's right to confrontation under both the Florida and U.S. Constitutions, the court upheld the statute as constitutional as applied to the non-testimonial hearsay statements. Those statements were admissible provided that in accordance with the statute. But, as to the testimonial statements made to law enforcement officers, the statute did violate the Confrontation Clause, and therefore the statute was unconstitutional as applied to those statements. Thus, the matter was remanded for the trial court to place on the record specific findings indicating the basis for determining the reliability of the declarant's statements introduced as hearsay under § 90.803(24). Further, the court did not reach the issue of whether the statute was constitutional as applied to physically disabled adults who have no mental impairment.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal was reversed, as that decision related to a mentally disabled adult with respect to the non-testimonial statements made to the victim's teacher. However, the statute was unconstitutional as it related to testimonial statements made to law enforcement.


 

442 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Burns v. State


No. SC01-166


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


944 So. 2d 234; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2593; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 752



November 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at Burns v. State, 3 So. 3d 316, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 199 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Manatee County, William Clayton Johnson, Judge - Case No. 87-2014F.
Burns v. State, 699 So. 2d 646, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1014 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following convictions for first-degree murder and cocaine trafficking for which a death sentence was imposed, appellant inmate filed a motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate appealed orders of the Circuit Court in and for Manatee County (Florida), denying that motion and finding that the inmate did not meet the statutory definition of mental retardation.


OVERVIEW: The inmate asserted, inter alia, that the postconviction court erred in denying his claim that resentencing counsel were ineffective for failing to present available mental mitigation evidence. The supreme court disagreed, noting that there was competent, substantial evidence to support the postconviction court's finding that resentencing counsel made a strategic decision not to present mental mitigation evidence. The transcript of the postconviction proceeding indicated that counsel considered but eventually rejected the idea of calling the forensic psychologist. The record demonstrated that the defense strategy was to show that the inmate had been a productive member of society who supported and led his family. The inmate also challenged the circuit court's determination that he was not mentally retarded in accordance with Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203(b). The supreme court agreed with the circuit court, noting that although the inmate's IQ scores indicated mild mental retardation, the inmate communicated well, was able to work, and was able to care for himself. In addition, there was no evidence that the inmate met the statutory criteria of mental retardation before the age of 18.


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's postconviction motion and determination that the inmate was not mentally retarded were affirmed.


 

443 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Coday v. State


No. SC02-1920


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


946 So. 2d 988; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2533; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 714



October 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 8, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Alfred J. Horowitz, Judge - Case No. 97-021145-CF10A.
Coday v. State, 823 So. 2d 122, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1620 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder and a sentence of death imposed in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit in and for Broward County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from the brutal beating and stabbing death of his former girlfriend. Defendant asserted on appeal that the trial court abused its discretion by denying his proffered jury instruction on heat of passion. The court found no error, concluding that case law precedent had already established that the standard jury instruction on excusable homicide was sufficient to explain heat of passion in the context of premeditation. The court further found no error with regard to the denial of defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal/sufficiency of the evidence since there was an abundance of evidence establishing that the murder was premeditated by defendant in that he called the victim and planned a meeting under the ruse that he was dying of cancer. The 144 stab wounds and hammer blows inflicted by defendant also supported his conviction. The court did find error with the trial court finding that the mitigator of being unable to conform his conduct to the requirements of the law had not been established since six mental health experts testified that defendant was not able to conform his conduct to the requirements of the law at the time of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction but vacated the sentenced because the trial court erred in finding that the mitigating circumstance of being unable to conform one's conduct to the requirements of the law had not been established. The court remanded the case to the trial judge for reevaluation of the mitigation and the sentence.

Rodgers v. State


No. SC04-1425


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


948 So. 2d 655; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2542; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 705



October 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Rodgers v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 124 (Fla., Jan. 24, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rodgers v. Florida, 552 U.S. 833, 128 S. Ct. 59, 169 L. Ed. 2d 50, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9187 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Rodgers v. State, 113 So. 3d 761, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 952 (Fla., 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at Rodgers v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 312 (Fla., Feb. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Belvin Perry, Jr., Chief Judge, Judge - Case No. 01CF-2386.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death, entered by the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Belvin, Florida.


OVERVIEW: After discovering his wife's infidelity in the morning, defendant went to work, told a friend he was going to murder his wife, drove to the day care where she worked, confronted her, hit and kicked her, left the room and returned with a gun, and then shot at her several times while she tried to escape. He then drove to a pool hall and told two friends what he had done. Under these circumstances, sufficient evidence supported defendant's murder conviction. With respect to sentencing, while defendant was mildly retarded, three experts testified that he was not mentally retarded within the definition set forth in Fla. Stat. § 921.137(1), and there was no evidence of onset before age 18. Therefore, he was eligible for the death penalty. He was able to appreciate the criminality of his conduct, and there was no link between his age and the crime, such as immaturity. Defendant did not show that the trial court abused its discretion in the weight it afforded to the mitigation found. His death sentence was proportional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were upheld.

Troy v. State


No. SC04-332


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


948 So. 2d 635; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2419; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 677



October 19, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Troy v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 122 (Fla., Jan. 24, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Troy v. Florida, 551 U.S. 1135, 127 S. Ct. 2981, 168 L. Ed. 2d 711, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 7802 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Troy v. State, 57 So. 3d 828, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2 (Fla., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Troy v. Sec'y of Dep't of Corr., 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 271 (M.D. Fla., Jan. 2, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Sarasota County (Florida) that convicted him upon a jury verdict of armed burglary, armed robbery, attempted sexual battery with a weapon, and first-degree murder, and sentenced him to death for the murder conviction under § 921.141, Fla. Stat. (1983). He was also convicted of the related burglary, battery, kidnapping, and robbery of another victim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed. Section 775.051, Fla. Stat. (2001), did not violate due process or equal protection because there was no fundamental right to use a voluntary intoxication defense and a rational basis existed for permitting prescription drug users to assert it. The death sentence was properly based on the totality of the circumstances. Section 921.141, Fla. Stat. (1983) was not unconstitutional because the aggravator for murders committed during felonies depended on facts found by juries. The murder conviction was sustained by sufficient evidence, and the death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the convictions and sentence.

Rolling v. State


No. SC06-1966


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


944 So. 2d 176; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2376; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 667



October 18, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by Rolling v. Florida, 127 S. Ct. 466, 166 L. Ed. 2d 332, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8002 (U.S., Oct. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County, Stan R. Morris, Judge - Case No. 91-3832-CFA.
Rolling v. State, 825 So. 2d 293, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1397 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Alachua County (Florida) summarily denied appellant inmate's successive motion for postconviction relief, filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate first argued that the trial court erred in denying his claim that death by lethal injection violated his right to be free of cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution, and his First Amendment right to free speech. But, summary denial of this claim was upheld, as the instant court had previously decided that lethal injection did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. Finally, the ABA Report cited was not newly discovered evidence. Further, nothing in the report would cause the instant court to recede from its past decisions upholding the facial constitutionality of the death penalty, and the inmate did not allege how any of the conclusions in the report rendered his death sentence unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Evans v. State


No. SC05-632, No. SC05-1974


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


946 So. 2d 1; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2277; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 628

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Evans v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 3043 (Fla., Dec. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, W. David Dugan, Judge - Case No. 1998-CF-025245-AXXX.
Evans v. State, 838 So. 2d 1090, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2406 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner, who was convicted of kidnapping, aggravated assault, and first-degree murder and subsequently sentenced to death, sought review of the denial by the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida) of his motion for postconviction relief. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner shot and killed his brother's 17-year-old girlfriend during an argument over her alleged unfaithfulness to his brother. During the guilt phase, the defense's theory was that he accidentally shot her while trying to hand a gun to her. The prisoner claimed his defense counsel was ineffective for, among other things, failing to discover that the prisoner suffered a closed head injury at age three. The appellate court held the trial court correctly held that defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to present the defense of diminished capacity because diminished capacity was not a viable defense in Florida. Moreover, it would have been inconsistent with the prisoner's theory that the shooting was an accident. The mere fact that the prisoner was represented by one attorney alone was insufficient to establish a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel for failing to request a second attorney. § 921.141, Fla. Stat. had already been held to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Ponticelli v. State


No. SC03-17, No. SC03-1858


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


941 So. 2d 1073; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1855; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 561



August 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Ponticelli v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2602 (Fla., Oct. 23, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ponticelli v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1966 (Fla., Nov. 10, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Victor J. Musleh, Chief Judge - Case No. 87-2719-CF-A-W And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Ponticelli v. State, 593 So. 2d 483, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1742 (Fla., 1991)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Marion County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that given the significant amount of evidence impeaching a cellmate's credibility, as well as the State's credibility in calling him to testify, the inmate had not established that the State's failure to disclose before trial a prosecutor's note following a telephone conversation with the cellmate's defense counsel constituted prejudice under Brady. Under Giglio, informing the jury that the cellmate might be testifying falsely because of his hope for an unguaranteed, unspecified award would not have rendered him sufficiently less credible in the jury's eyes to establish a reasonable possibility that this contributed to the verdict. Counsel was not ineffective for allowing a state investigator to be excluded from the rule of witness sequestration, as even if counsel should have objected, the inmate had not established that the state investigator's presence prejudiced him. The inmate's claim in his habeas petition that Florida's capital sentencing procedure was unconstitutional in light of Ring was without merit, as his convictions and sentences became final in 1993, nearly nine years before Ring was decided, and the decision did not apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying the inmate's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed and his petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Branch v. State


No. SC05-433, No. SC05-1558


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


952 So. 2d 470; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1825; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 573



August 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 12, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Branch v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 489 (Fla., Mar. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Edward Phillips Nickinson, III, Judge - Case No. 93-879 CFA. And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Branch v. State, 685 So. 2d 1250, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2076 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner, who was convicted by a jury of first-degree murder, sexual battery, and grand theft, appealed the denial of his motion for postconviction relief by the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida) and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant's conviction and sentence had been affirmed on appeal. He alleged, inter alia, that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to file a motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of accosting the victim, stealing her car, sexually assaulting her, and killing her. The appellate court concluded that the prisoner had not demonstrated that the trial court erred in concluding that trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to file a motion to suppress. It also found no error in the trial court's analysis regarding sentencing, which relied in large part on the failure of the prisoner to demonstrate that substantial mitigation evidence existed that counsel failed to discover. Most of the evidence put forth at the postconviction hearing was cumulative to evidence that was presented earlier and considered as mitigation, was not credible, or would actually have been harmful to the prisoner's case. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a claim on direct appeal as it was not preserved for appellate review. An expert had an adequate basis on which to render an opinion on the DNA statistics evidence. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the prisoner's attempt to confer with counsel in the middle of his testimony. Appellate counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise an issue that was without merit.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

451 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Hannon v. State


No. SC03-893, No. SC04-1662


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


941 So. 2d 1109; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1826; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 539



August 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 27, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Hannon v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2627 (Fla., Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, J. Rogers Padgett, Judge - Case No. 91-1927. And an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Hannon v. State, 638 So. 2d 39, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 834 (Fla., June 2, 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. Appellant was convicted on two counts of first-degree murder, with the jury unanimously recommending the death penalty. The trial imposed separate death sentences.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's convictions and sentences were upheld on direct appeal. On appeal, defendant contended that his trial counsel was ineffective for numerous reasons, including for failing to depose a witness or to challenge the credentials and testimony of the State's blood spatter expert. As to the failure to depose the witness, the court found that the record supported a carefully considered and planned defense strategy on behalf of appellant to continue to rely on an alibi defense of which the witness was not a part of. Trial counsel's decision not to request a continuance to depose the witness was also strategic in that defense counsel did not want to give the State any additional time to prepare the witness for trial. The failure to challenge the testimony or credentials of the blood spatter expert was also strategic in that the credentials of the expert were not relevant and the expert's testimony did not implicate appellant in the murders, nor was it even an element in the State's case against appellant. The court found no merit to any of appellant's ineffective assistance claims and that appellant's other claims were procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's post-conviction motion and denied appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus.

Klein v. Robbins

453 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Engle v. Liggett Group, Inc.


No. SC03-1856


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2006 Fla. LEXIS 1480; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 464



July 6, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Rehearing granted by, in part, Rehearing denied by, in part, Opinion withdrawn by Engle v. Liggett Group, Inc., 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2949 (Fla., Dec. 21, 2006)
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Engle v. Liggett Group, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2952 (Fla., Dec. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case Nos. 3D00-3206, 3D00-3207, 3D00-3208, 3D00-3210, 3D00-3212, 3D00-3215, and 3D00-3400 (Dade County).
Liggett Group Inc. v. Engle, 853 So. 2d 434, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7500 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: The court approved a reversal of the punitive damages award but quashed the rest of the Third District's decision. Compensatory awards to two smokers were reinstated, an award to a third smoker was vacated, and the case was remanded with directions to decertify the class without prejudice to the right of the members to bring individual claims. Judgments against two defendants were reversed, but certain findings were approved.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action that plaintiff smokers brought against defendant tobacco companies (Tobacco), the District Court of Appeal, Direct Conflict of Decisions, Third District, Florida (Third District), reversed a judgment for the smokers after a trial court had awarded $12.7 million to the three named class members and $145 billion in punitive damages. The smokers appealed, in part challenging the decertification of the class and other rulings.


OVERVIEW: The Third District ruled that a settlement in the State's prior case against Tobacco was res judicata, barring the punitive damages. The supreme court ruled that res judicata did not bar the punitive damages as the State sued on behalf of public issues of common concern, but the smokers claimed personal injuries from their smoking. The punitive damages, however, were excessive; they were set before any compensatory damages were decided on, which was a due process violation. The amount also would have bankrupted some defendants. The court held that there had to be a reasonable relationship between any punitive and compensatory damages. The Third District erred under the law of the case doctrine by decertifying the class; Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(d)(1) did not allow decertification after notice to thousands of citizens, a long trial, and entry of final judgment. Under Fla. Const. art. I, § 22, the date of class certification closed the class, so as not to affect the right to opt out under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(d)(2) or affect the right of access to the courts under Fla. Const. art. I, § 21. Defense counsel's racial pandering did not require reversal as the remarks were spread out.


OUTCOME: The court approved a reversal of the punitive damages award but quashed the rest of the Third District's decision. Compensatory awards to two smokers were reinstated, an award to a third smoker was vacated, and the case was remanded with directions to decertify the class without prejudice to the right of the members to bring individual claims. Judgments against two defendants were reversed, but certain findings were approved.

Farina v. State


No. SC04-1610, No. SC05-935


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


937 So. 2d 612; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1482; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 517



July 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 30, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Farina v. Florida, 127 S. Ct. 1153, 166 L. Ed. 2d 999, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1224 (U.S., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Farina v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1152 (Fla., June 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, C. McFerrin Smith, III, Judge - Case No. 92-32105-CFAES. And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Farina v. State, 801 So. 2d 44, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1579 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. Defendant also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from the robbery of a fast food restaurant. Defendant and co-defendant shot or stabbed four people, with one victim dying. Of defendant's various claims, the court only addressed a few because many of the claims were procedurally barred or legally insufficient. Defendant asserted that co-defendant's receipt of a reduction in sentence to a life sentence was newly discovered evidence that warranted granting defendant a new sentencing phase. The court agreed that the reduced sentence was newly discovered evidence but that co-defendant was not legally eligible for the death sentence. Although co-defendant was the triggerman, the basis for co-defendant's reduction in sentence hindered defendant's ability to satisfy the second prong of the newly discovered evidence test since the evidence of the murder was not so strong that it would probably result in a life sentence for defendant. The court further found no ineffective assistance of counsel since the errors raised by defendant were not preserved for appeal and did not qualify for the fundamental error exception. The prosecutor's questions regarding the Bible were not objected to at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief. The court denied defendant's petition for habeas corpus.

Archer v. State


No. SC04-451, No. SC05-696


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


934 So. 2d 1187; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1403; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 443



June 29, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, T. Michael Jones, Judge - Case No. 91-606-CFA And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Archer v. State, 673 So. 2d 17, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 436 (Fla., Mar. 14, 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), which denied the inmate's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Additionally, the inmate petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate had been convicted of armed robbery, grand theft, and first-degree murder and had received a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of first-degree murder, based in part on testimony from the inmate's cousin. The cousin testified that the inmate recruited the cousin to rob the store where the inmate used to work and to kill a clerk. The cousin and a friend went to the store, got the cash boxes, and killed the clerk on duty. The inmate claimed that the cousin's subsequent recantation established the inmate's innocence. The court held that it was error for the postconviction court not to characterize the recantation testimony as newly discovered evidence. However, the recantation testimony was not credible, and there was competent, substantial evidence to support rejection of the recanted testimony. The skepticism expressed by a prosecutor concerning certain aspects of the cousin's testimony did not provide sufficient grounds for a Giglio violation. The inmate had not established a Brady claim because there was no evidence that the State had more information about the cousin's prior crimes than the inmate had. The inmate's habeas corpus claims for ineffective assistance of appellate counsel were without merit because the arguments did not impact the verdict reached.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the postconviction court's denial of the inmate's motion for postconviction relief. The court denied the inmate's habeas corpus claims.

Looney v. State


No. SC05-159


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


941 So. 2d 1017; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1339; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 413



June 22, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 27, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Looney v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2625 (Fla., Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County, N. Sanders Sauls, Judge - Case No. 97-215-CF.
Looney v. State, 803 So. 2d 656, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2210 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murders and other crimes and was sentenced to death. After his direct appeals failed, he filed a motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel. After conducting a Huff hearing, the Wakulla County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the inmate's motion; he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and two accomplices robbed two persons, killed them, and set their house on fire. At the Huff hearing, a forensic psychologist testified that defense counsel, who did not use a mental health expert during the penalty phase, failed to present statutory and nonstatutory mental health mitigation evidence or presented it in an ineffective manner. The high court held that counsel's decision not to call a mental health expert was valid strategy, since this could have opened the door to the admission of the opinion of a defense expert, who did not testify, that the inmate was a psychopath. The additional mitigators that the inmate asserted were not presented during the penalty phase were either presented or were not presented because defense counsel had no indication that they might apply. Additionally, even if the mitigation evidence had been presented in the manner proposed by the expert during his testimony at the evidentiary hearing, the trial court found him to be an unconvincing witness. None of the testimony presented by the inmate at the postconviction evidentiary hearing undermined the high court's confidence in the proceedings below.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hertz v. State


No. SC05-59


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


941 So. 2d 1031; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1342; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 408



June 22, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 27, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Hertz v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2677 (Fla., Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County, N. Sanders Sauls, Judge - Case No. 97-214-CF.
Hertz v. State, 803 So. 2d 629, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2209 (Fla., Nov. 1, 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of two first-degree murders and was sentenced to death. He sought postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 on grounds of ineffective assistance of counsel. After holding an evidentiary hearing, the Wakulla County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the inmate's petition. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and two accomplices robbed and killed two persons and set their house on fire. The inmate alleged his trial counsel was ineffective at the penalty phase for failing to present all available mental health mitigation. A neuropsychologist who testified for the defense at the competency hearing found no indication of retardation, borderline intellectual functioning, or major mental illness. The high court held that trial counsel's failure to call that expert at the penalty phase was valid strategy, as counsel found that his testimony during cross examination at the competency hearing was not helpful to the inmate. A forensic psychologist testified at the evidentiary hearing that the inmate had organic brain damage and functioned at the mental age of 14. However, counsel was unaware of any theory that the inmate's possible mental age was 14, and the trial court did not find the psychologist's testimony credible. All of the additional mitigators that the inmate asserted were not presented during the penalty phase were either presented or not supported by the record. Counsel's manner of presenting evidence that detailed the inmate's background was a reasonable trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

P. 3.851. The inmate further sought a writ of habeas corpus pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, §§ 3(b)(1), (9). The inmate had been convicted by the trial court and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, the inmate was convicted of first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit robbery with a deadly weapon, carjacking with a deadly weapon, kidnapping, robbery with a deadly weapon, and third-degree grand theft, and the death sentence was imposed. State v. Hosty


No. SC03-511, No. SC03-512


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2006 Fla. LEXIS 1026; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 369



June 8, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION, AND IF FILED, DETERMINED.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by, Remanded by State v. Hosty, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2615 (Fla., Nov. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity And an Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-3457 (Broward County).
State v. Hosty, 835 So. 2d 1202, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two cases consolidated for appeal, Appellant State sought review of two decisions of the Florida District Court of Appeal, which declared invalid Fla. Stat. § 90.803(24) as applied to nontestimonial hearsay statements made by a mentally disabled adult. A question was certified for the court to review and answer.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed to address a certified question relating to the admission of a nontestimonial hearsay statements from a mentally disabled victim pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 90.803(24)(2001). The issue arose after defendant was charged with a sexual battery on a mentally disabled victim. The State sought to introduce into evidence the victim's hearsay statements that were made to the victim's teacher and the statements that were later made to a law enforcement officer under the disabled adult hearsay exception set forth in Fla. Stat. § 90.803(24)(2001). The trial court granted defendant's motion to strike. The intermediate appellate court agreed with the trial court that the statute was unconstitutional under the Confrontation Clauses in U.S. Const. amend. 6 and Fla. Const. art. I, § 16. The court distinguished between the testimony given to the police officer and to the teacher, finding that the testimony to the officer was not admissible after Crawford unless defendant had been given an opportunity to cross examine. The court found that the statements to the teacher were admissible under Fla. Stat. § 90.803(24), if there was a sufficient factual predicate established by the State.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court and remanded the matter to the trial court for consideration in light of the court's opinion.


 

460 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Nichols


No. SC03-1483, No. SC03-1653


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


932 So. 2d 1067; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 982; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 358



June 1, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases Consolidated: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance.

Fifth District - Case No. 5D01-3851. (Orange County).
Nichols v. State Farm Mut., 851 So. 2d 742, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8794 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insured brought suit in a trial court against respondent insurer. A jury found for the insurer, which received attorney's fees under the offer of judgment statute, Fla. Stat. § 768.79 (1999). A question was certified as to whether § 768.79 applied to PIP suits. The Fifth District Court of Appeal, Florida, ruled yes but reversed, as the settlement offer was ambiguous and did not satisfy Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442. The parties sought review.


OVERVIEW: The insurer sought attorney's fees, as the insured rejected a PIP settlement offer. The release was general, and the insured, who also had a claim for uninsured motorist (UM) benefits, refused to sign the release for fear of also releasing her higher UM claim. On review, the court ruled that the offer of judgment statute applied to suits under the PIP statute, Fla. Stat. § 627.736(7)(b) (1999), as they were suits for damages. Further, the attorney's fees provision in the PIP statute did not exclude other such provisions, including the one in the offer of judgment statute. Applying the offer of judgment statute to PIP suits also did not make the PIP system unconstitutional. Until an insurer offered to pay an insured's damages, attorney's fees, and related sums, the "one-way street" under Fla. Stat. § 627.428 (1999) entitled an insured to attorney's fees. But once an offer was made and rejected, the insured who turned down the full sum owed had no right to protection under § 627.428, and the insurer could then seek attorney's fees under the offer of judgment statute. Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442 precluded attorney's fees for the insurer as its release had not been limited to the PIP claim.


OUTCOME: The court approved in full the district court's decision reversing the award of attorney's fees to the insurer.

Raleigh v. State


No. SC03-710, No. SC03-2282


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


932 So. 2d 1054; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 983; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 365



June 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Raleigh v. Florida, 549 U.S. 874, 127 S. Ct. 183, 166 L. Ed. 2d 128, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 7040 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, S. James Foxman, Judge - Case No. 94-00723.

And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Raleigh v. State, 705 So. 2d 1324, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1859 (Fla., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate, who was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Florida, which denied his motion for postconviction relief, filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The inmate also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. He challenged the expert mental health assistance he received and the effectiveness of his trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that he did not receive adequate mental health assistance, as required. He also claimed that his trial counsel was ineffective with regard to how he handled the expert witnesses. On review, the court saw no error, ruling that substantial, competent evidence supported the trial court's ruling that he received a professional, competent, and appropriate mental health evaluation for use in aid of his defense. One expert did not miss signs of mental retardation or organic brain damage, and two experts concluded that there was no such damage. One doctor also helped establish nonstatutory mitigating sentencing factors. The court also saw no ineffectiveness of counsel, ruling that the inmate failed to prove prejudice, even if error occurred. He did not show that if his counsel had prepared one doctor better about the facts of the case that the outcome would have been different; there was no proof that the doctor's testimony would have been more favorable or materially more credible. Admitting part of fellow defendant's statement that was in the form of a recording was competent trial strategy even though the State was allowed to introduce the rest of his statement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the motion for postconviction relief and denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Trotter v. State


No. SC03-735, No. SC03-1967


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


932 So. 2d 1045; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 940; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 332



May 25, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Trotter v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 724 (Fla., Apr. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases Consolidated: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Manatee County, Andrew D. Owens, Jr., Judge. Case No. 86-1225-F.
Trotter v. State, 690 So. 2d 1234, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2143 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Manatee County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and concluded he was not mentally retarded. The inmate also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. Both actions were consolidated, and this matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate challenged the orders entered against him, first arguing that (1) the circuit court erred in determining he was not mentally retarded and (2) his death sentence was not proportional. The appeals court disagreed, as he failed to meet any of the three prongs for determining mental retardation. No expert who tested the inmate as an adult, including those who also examined his adaptive skills, found that he met the definition for mental retardation. Further, the one doctor that tested the inmate when he was 15 concluded he was not mentally retarded. Second, the inmate's allegations that a 1993 resentencing order was deficient and that his death sentence was not proportional were not preserved and were procedurally barred, as they were considered on direct appeal from the inmate's resentencing. Third, the inmate failed to establish that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel to support his motion for post-conviction relief. Finally, with regards to his habeas petition, an Apprendi claim was not cognizable, and a claim that he might be incompetent at the time of execution was not ripe for review. Thus, the petition was denied.


OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate's postconviction motion and finding that he was not mentally retarded was affirmed, while his habeas petition was denied.

Henry v. State


Nos. SC03-1312 & SC04-1285


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


937 So. 2d 563; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 943; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 342



May 25, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 29, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Henry v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1857 (Fla., Aug. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Richard D. Eade, Judge. Case No. 87-18628 CF 10.
Henry v. State, 613 So. 2d 429, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2150 (Fla., 1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Broward County of two counts of first-degree murder, armed robbery, and arson. Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed on appeal. The circuit court then denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant appealed the decision and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his Sixth Amendment rights were violated as trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance during the penalty phase of trial as to the presentation of mental health mitigation, under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.216, and that this claimed ineffectiveness affected the validity of defendant's decision to waive his right to present mitigation. The state supreme court found that (1) the trial court did not err in finding that trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to pursue and present evidence of defendant's drug addiction as defendant was adamant that trial counsel not rely on any evidence of intoxication or addiction in defendant's defense; (2) trial counsel was not ineffective in the manner and degree to which he investigated the mental health issues and counsel was not ineffective for not retaining additional mental health experts; and (3) given defendant's adamant, informed refusal to participate in the investigation and preparation of any type of mitigation, counsel's preparation and defendant's decision to waive his rights did not deny defendant of a reliable penalty phase proceeding. Additionally, the writ of habeas corpus claims were insufficiently pleaded.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed. Defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

464 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



England v. State


No. SC04-1521


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


940 So. 2d 389; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 942; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 620



May 25, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 28, 2006.
Rehearing denied by England v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2256 (Fla., Sept. 28, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by England v. Florida, 549 U.S. 1325, 127 S. Ct. 1916, 167 L. Ed. 2d 571, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3852 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied England v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 2120 (Fla., July 3, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, S. James Foxman, Judge. Case No. 2003-35769 CFAES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Florida, entered a judgment convicting appellant of first-degree murder and sentencing him to death. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Although appellant raised 14 issues on appeal, none had merit. For example, testimony by a witness linking appellant to a prior murder, which the trial judge had excluded, did not constitute fundamental error under Fla. Stat. § 924.051, given appellant's admissions tying him to the commission of the murder in the instant case. Crime scene and autopsy photographs admitted into evidence were relevant to both the guilt and penalty phases of appellant's trial. The trial judge applied the correct rule of law, and substantial evidence supported the finding of the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator because the victim was conscious and aware of the beating, which was particularly brutal. He begged for his life but was told to shut up. He moved around the bedroom while fending off blows, experienced significant pain before losing consciousness, and eventually died by a blow to the head that was so severe that it fractured his spine. Finally, in conducting a proportionality review of defendant's sentence, the supreme court, after looking at the totality of the circumstances in comparison to other cases where the sentence of death had been upheld, found death a proportionate sentence.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence of death.


 

465 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Harden


No. SC04-613


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


938 So. 2d 480; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 889; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 350



May 18, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 25, 2006. Released for Publication September 6, 2006.
Rehearing denied by State v. Harden, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1950 (Fla., Sept. 6, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Florida v. Harden, 127 S. Ct. 2097, 167 L. Ed. 2d 812, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 4351 (U.S., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Third District. Case No. 3D03-521 (Dade County).
State v. Harden, 873 So. 2d 352, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 623 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were indicted for violating Fla. Stat. § 409.920(2)(e) (2000), the "anti-kickback" provision of the Florida Medicaid fraud statute. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss on grounds that § 409.920(2)(e) was unconstitutional. The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed, finding that § 409.920(2)(e) was preempted by federal legislation. The State sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that defendants engaged in a "pay for patients" scheme in which individuals received "per head" payments in exchange for soliciting and driving Medicaid-eligible children for dental treatment. The intermediate appellate court concluded that § 409.920(2)(e) criminalized activity that was protected under the federal statute, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1320a-7b, and stood as an obstacle to the accomplishment and execution of the full purposes and objectives of Congress, thereby resulting in implied conflict preemption under the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, cl. 2. The high court agreed. The particular pay arrangement at issue involved protected employer-employee payments for the provision of covered items or services, which were protected from criminal prosecution under the federal statute. Fla. Stat. § 409.920(2)(e) was preempted, and hence unconstitutional, because (1) it criminalized conduct that federal law specifically intended to be lawful and shielded from prosecution; and (2) unlike 42 U.S.C.S. § 1320a-7b, it allowed prosecution of negligent or inadvertent behavior.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

466 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Consalvo v. State


No. SC04-520


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


937 So. 2d 555; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 890; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 313



May 18, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 30, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Consalvo v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1856 (Fla., Aug. 30, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Consalvo v. Florida, 127 S. Ct. 1821, 167 L. Ed. 2d 330, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3125 (U.S., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Howard M. Zeidwig, Judge. Case No. 91-19140-CF10A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, who was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death, filed a motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. After summarily rejecting most of the inmate's claims, and conducting a Huff hearing on the rest, the Broward County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the Huff hearing, a former state witness testified he had lied to the grand jury about the inmate's confession; a second witness testified he gave similar false testimony to the trial jury. The inmate also alleged that the State failed to disclose exculpatory evidence that an assistant state attorney (ASA) had improperly briefed the first witness on the inmate's case, and that the first witness had passed this information on to the second. The trial court found that the recantations were not credible and denied those claims that were based on the truth of the recantations. The high court held that this credibility finding was supported by the witnesses' history of lying, their psychiatric deficiencies, their inconsistencies and lack of memory when testifying at the Huff hearing, and the contrary testimony of the ASA. Therefore, the second witness's recanted testimony was not newly discovered evidence with regards to the "avoid arrest" aggravator sufficient to merit a new penalty phase proceeding. As there was no exculpatory evidence to turn over, the inmate's Brady claim failed. Finally, since there was no misleading testimony, there was no Giglio violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

467 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Reynolds v. State


No. SC03-1919


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


934 So. 2d 1128; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 888; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 318



May 18, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 11, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Reynolds v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1550 (Fla., July 11, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Reynolds v. Florida, 549 U.S. 1122, 127 S. Ct. 943, 166 L. Ed. 2d 721, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 199 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Reynolds v. State, 99 So. 3d 459, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 1860 (Fla., 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at Reynolds v. State, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 2140 (Fla., Oct. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, Kenneth R. Lester, Jr., Judge - Case No. 98-3341-CFA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (Florida), which convicted him of two counts of first-degree murder and imposed corresponding sentences of death. He was also convicted of a lesser-included offense of second-degree murder and burglary of a dwelling during which a battery was committed while defendant was armed with a weapon, and he received varying sentences of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The three victims were found murdered in and near their trailer. Evidence that defendant was involved in a dispute with one victim, injuries that he sustained, and blood, fingerprint, and DNA evidence supported the jury's convictions. The sentences were imposed and on appeal, the court found that exclusion of certain statements by a witness whom defendant alleged had committed the crimes was proper as they were inadmissible hearsay under Fla. Stat. § 90.801(1)(c) (2003) because they were to be offered to prove the truth of the matter asserted. Other statements by the witness were improperly excluded, but the error was harmless. The evidence was more than just circumstantial and supported the convictions. Accordingly, denial of acquittal was proper. Use of an advisory jury for a penalty recommendation was proper, and there was no error in the penalty phase instructions. The aggravating circumstances under Fla. Stat. § 921.141(5) of avoiding arrest, prior violent convictions, heinous, atrocious, and cruel conduct, and during commission of a burglary were supported by the evidence and outweighed any mitigation. The death sentences were not unconstitutional and they were proportional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
