Simmons v. State


No. SC04-19


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


934 So. 2d 1100; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 813; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 285



May 11, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 11, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Simmons v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1548 (Fla., July 11, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Simmons v. Florida, 549 U.S. 1209, 127 S. Ct. 1334, 167 L. Ed. 2d 80, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2125 (2007)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, Remanded by Simmons v. State, 105 So. 3d 475, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 2062 (Fla., 2012)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by Simmons v. State, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 2719 (Fla., Dec. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, T. Michael Johnson, Judge - Case No. 01-CF-2577-01.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence by the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida), for kidnapping, sexual battery using force likely to cause serious injury, and first-degree murder, for which he received a sentence of death. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the guilty verdicts on the charges of kidnapping, sexual battery, and murder were not supported by the evidence and that the trial court did not have jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: There was physical evidence and eyewitness testimony, as well as defendant's statements, which linked defendant to the victim at the time of the murder. The jury was entitled to draw an inference that defendant acknowledged his guilt from his statement that he "must have did it." Thus, the case was not entirely circumstantial. As a circuit court had original jurisdiction over a murder, the trial court properly denied the motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. Although defendant was handcuffed and transported in the back of a police cruiser, those measures were taken for the safety of the police officers involved and the police removed the handcuffs as soon as defendant reached the sheriff's office. Nothing in the record indicated that defendant objected to being handcuffed or at any time expressed a desire to terminate the encounter. Thus, a reasonable person in defendant's position would have felt free to terminate the encounter with police. While the methods employed as to the identification were highly suggestive, the procedures did not give rise to a substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification. Defendant's death penalty was proportionate.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences, including the death sentence, were affirmed.

Schoenwetter v. State


No. SC04-53


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


931 So. 2d 857; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 668; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 261



April 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication June 8, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Schoenwetter v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1328 (Fla., June 8, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Schoenwetter v. Florida, 549 U.S. 1035, 127 S. Ct. 587, 166 L. Ed. 2d 437, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8685 (2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Schoenwetter v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1051 (Fla., July 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, John M. Griesbaum, Judge - Case No. 05-2000-CF-041829-AX.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida) convicted defendant of two counts of first-degree murder and imposed two death sentences against him. Defendant appealed, raising numerous claims of error.


OVERVIEW: After reviewing defendant's many challenges, the instant court found no error. First, his voluntary confession provided a basis to seize the physical evidence. Thus, suppression was unwarranted. Second, the evidence did not support the withdrawal of counsel. Third, the victim impact evidence was admissible as limited by Fla. Stat. § 921.141(7). Fourth, a medical examiner properly testified in place of an unavailable colleague, after he reviewed the autopsy reports, photos, and notes and had spoken with said colleague. Fifth, a mistrial was properly denied, as a curative instruction cured any error. Sixth, defendant's motion to disqualify the trial judge was legally insufficient. Next, photos of the wounds inflicted were relevant to show their extent, depicted the medical intervention necessary to save the victim's life, and also helped to put defendant's actions in context. Further, the evidence surrounding both deaths supported the witness elimination and avoid arrest aggravators, and the trial court gave proper weight to the evidence in mitigation. Finally, the death sentences were proportional and Fla. Stat. § 921.141 conformed with the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgments and sentences, including the two sentences of death, were all affirmed.

Morris v. State


No. SC04-1594, No. SC05-227


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


931 So. 2d 821; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 652; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 250



April 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 2006.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Morris v. Sec'y, Dep't of Corr., 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 95335 (M.D. Fla., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, J. Michael McCarthy, Judge - Case No. CF94-3961A1-XX And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Morris v. State, 811 So. 2d 661, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 325 (Fla., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. The Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) denied his motion for postconviction relief. He appealed and also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus against respondents, an individual and others.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that trial counsel had been ineffective by failing to object to the trial court's decision to permit jurors to ask questions during trial. The court stated that it had approved a procedure nearly identical to the one here. As the trial court had not erred, counsel was not deficient. Next, any failure of counsel to advise petitioner that he had the right to testify during the penalty phase of his trial was not prejudicial because of petitioner's diminished credibility with the jury and the fact that his testimony would have been cumulative to the extensive mitigation evidence. The court next held that because there was no testimony as to mitigating factors under Fla. Stat. § 921.141(6)(b) and (e), trial counsel was not deficient in failing to request jury instructions on statutory mitigation. Finally, had appellate counsel raised the issue of the constitutionality of Florida's capital sentencing scheme, it likely would have been denied because of the nonretroactivity of a United States Supreme Court decision and because of the presence of a prior violent felony aggravating circumstance. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a meritless issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the motion for postconviction relief. It also denied the habeas petition.

Lamarca v. State


No. SC03-1815, No. SC04-847


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


931 So. 2d 838; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 653; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 239



April 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 4, 2006. Released for Publication June 7, 2006.
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Lamarca v. Sec'y, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 66856 (M.D. Fla., Aug. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Brandt C. Downey, III, Judge - Case No. 95-20270 CFANO-I And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Lamarca v. State, 785 So. 2d 1209, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 447 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. The Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) denied his motion for postconviction relief. Petitioner appealed and also sought a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defense counsel was not deficient to failing to order an additional psychological evaluation when petitioner stated that he planned to represent himself during the penalty phase. Nothing suggested that petitioner lacked the ability to consult with his attorney or a factual understanding of the proceeding against him. Next, counsel was not deficient for refusing to file a motion to suppress that would have been frivolous. Counsel also was not ineffective for refusing to call certain witnesses and for limiting cross-examination of others for strategic reasons. Next, as petitioner represented himself during the penalty phase, he could not hold counsel deficient for not presenting mitigating evidence. The trial court had followed the procedures required to ensure that he had knowingly waived his right to present mitigation. Finally, because jury selection occurred after Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.180(a)(4) was amended, petitioner's right to participate in a sidebar conference was satisfied because he was present in the courtroom while his counsel participated in the conference. Thus, counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise this issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying petitioner's motion for postconviction relief. It denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Jones v. State


No. SC04-282


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


928 So. 2d 1178; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 561; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 229



April 13, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Waddell A. Wallace, Judge - Case No. 16-1993-CF-2757-AXXX.
Jones v. State, 690 So. 2d 568, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2207 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) convicted defendant of first-degree murder and attempted first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Thereafter, the court denied his motion for postconviction relief, filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Of defendant's claims discussed on appeal, none warranted relief. First, counsel was not ineffective in failing to investigate and present mental health testimony, as: (1) this testimony would have been inconsistent with other evidence presented; (2) counsel did not want to open the door to damaging cross-examination and rebuttal evidence; and (3) trial counsel decided to focus on the humanization of defendant through lay testimony. Second, defendant's claim that trial counsel was ineffective by failing to present mitigating evidence of his positive and cooperative behavior throughout the proceedings and while in jail was legally insufficient. Third, counsel was not ineffective by failing to adequately contest the trial court's application of the pecuniary gain aggravating circumstance. Fourth, defendant failed to allege any overt act or error that might have prejudiced the jury and supported an inquiry into the validity into their verdict. Fifth, defendant failed to demonstrate that the absence of trial counsel's files hindered collateral counsel's investigation. Finally, defendant's Ring claim was denied, as Ring was not retroactive.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant any postconviction relief was affirmed.

Mungin v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


932 So. 2d 986; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 553; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 215



April 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 13, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Mungin v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1330 (Fla., June 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County. John Southwood, Judge. Case No. 92-3178-CF. And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Mungin v. State, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 172 (Fla., Mar. 6, 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's motion for postconviction relief, which he filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate appealed from that order, and also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing the postconviction relief motion, the instant court first held that no per se disqualification rule required circuit-wide disqualification necessary to preserve judicial impartiality. Second, the inmate waived or abandoned a claim that the trial court failed to conduct an in-camera review of certain public records from both the county sheriff's and State attorney's office. Arizona claim lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the inmate's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed, and his petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

474 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Presidential Women's Ctr.


No. SC04-2186


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


937 So. 2d 114; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 555; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 210



April 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 10, 2006.
Rehearing denied by State v. Presidential Women's Ctr., 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1788 (Fla., Aug. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-4485. (Palm Beach County).
Crist v. Presidential Women's Ctr., 884 So. 2d 526, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15011 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) declared Fla. Stat. § 390.0111 invalid, upholding the imposition of a temporary injunction by the Palm Beach County Circuit Court enjoining enforcement of the Woman's Right to Know Act, Fla. Stat. § 390.0111 (2005) and its entry of summary judgment in favor of respondent clinic. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Upon the State's appeal, the clinic posed two vagueness challenges to the statute. The instant court rejected them both, reasoning that Fla. Stat. § 390.0111(3)(a)(1)(a) required doctors to inform patients as to what a generalized, nondescript, abstract, and hypothetical reasonable patient would consider material when providing the informed consent information. Second, the court adopted the State's interpretation of the "reasonable patient" language as involving the patient who was presenting herself for the procedure. Thus, the doctor need only consider, address, and inform based on that patient's individualized circumstances in determining what information was material. Further, it would be illogical to require physicians who perform this treatment to provide the identical standardized information to every patient, even when that information would be completely irrelevant to the patient's individual circumstances. Second, § 390.0111(3)(a)(1)(a) did not encompass non-medical risks, but was a neutral informed consent statute, comparable to the common law and informed consent statutes implementing the common law that existed for other types of medical procedures.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Fourth District was reversed, and the case was remanded. As a result, the award of attorney's fees to the clinic was vacated.

Miller v. State


Nos. SC04-892 & SC05-472


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


926 So. 2d 1243; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 486; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 188



March 23, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 26, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, L. Haldane Taylor, Judge - Case No. 97-6680CFA And an Original Proceeding.
Miller v. State, 770 So. 2d 1144, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1743 (Fla., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's motion for postconviction relief, filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The inmate appealed. However, in a second action, the inmate also petitioned the Court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged on appeal that his trial counsel was ineffective, that the death penalty statute was unconstitutional and inappropriate in his case, and that the sentencing statute amounted to cruel and unusual punishment. The instant court disagreed, finding that trial counsel performed a proper and thorough investigation of mitigating evidence and made tactical decisions on what evidence and witnesses to present, as well as what objections to forego. Further, while the prosecutor came dangerously close to using victim impact evidence as a nonstatutory aggravator, his statements in closing argument were not improper. Second, claims that Florida's capital sentencing procedures were unconstitutional were procedurally barred, and his "innocent of the death penalty claims" lacked merit because he did not demonstrate that each aggravating circumstance supporting his death sentence was invalid. Third, because Ring was decided after defendant's convictions became final, it was inapplicable. Finally, habeas relief was denied, as no objections were made at trial to the prosecutor's closing arguments, and said comments did not rise to the level of fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The denial of relief was affirmed, and the petition for habeas corpus was denied.

Foster v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Osceola County (Florida) denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief, which he filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered, first contending that his counsel was ineffective in failing to present a voluntary intoxication and mental disability defense. Finally, competent, substantial evidence existed to support the postconviction court's factual findings, including the findings relating to the witnesses' credibility.

Ibar v. State


No. SC00-2043


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


938 So. 2d 451; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 383; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 149



March 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 7, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Ibar v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2223 (Fla., Sept. 7, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ibar v. Florida, 549 U.S. 1208, 127 S. Ct. 1326, 167 L. Ed. 2d 79, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2117 (2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at Ibar v. State, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 236 (Fla., Feb. 4, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Dale Ross, Chief Judge - Case No. 94-13062 CF10B.
Penalver v. State, 926 So. 2d 1118, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 141 (Fla., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Broward County Circuit Court (Florida) of three counts of first-degree murder and received three consecutive sentences of death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two men murdered three victims; the crime was videotaped by a security camera. The high court held that an officer's testimony about witnesses' prior identifications of defendant as one of the men in the video should not have been admitted as substantive evidence under Fla. Stat. § 90.801(2)(c), as the witnesses were not victims of or witnesses to the crimes. But the error was harmless in view of the other identification evidence. Expert testimony about footprint evidence was not based on novel science and thus was not subject to Frye analysis. A taped conversation was properly excluded under Fla. Stat. § 934.06 (1999), as there was no evidence that one of the parties to the conversation consented to its being recorded, as required by Fla. Stat. § 934.03(2)(d) (1999). An officer who testified about defendant's reluctance to talk had not commented on his invocation of the right to remain silent. As a pre-arrest investigatory lineup was not a critical stage of the proceedings, he had not been entitled to counsel. The evidence established the "cold, calculated, and premeditated," "heinous, atrocious, or cruel," and "avoid arrest" aggravators. The death sentences were proportional.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the convictions and the sentences.

 

478 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. State


Nos. SC03-454 & SC05-100


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


931 So. 2d 790; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 388; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 159



March 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 8, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Smith v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1329 (Fla., June 8, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Florida, 549 U.S. 1035, 127 S. Ct. 587, 166 L. Ed. 2d 436, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8683 (Nov. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Mark I. Shames, Judge - Case No. CRC 83-02653 CFANO, And an Original Proceeding.
Smith v. State, 641 So. 2d 1319, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 901 (Fla., June 9, 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's motion for postconviction relief, which he filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate appealed said denial and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Upon reviewing the evidence in the record, the instant court found that no error existed in denying the inmate's petition for postconviction relief. First, any failure to disclose the evidence sought would not have changed the outcome of the trial. Second, the inmate failed to establish the elements of a Giglio claim. Third, testimony which consisted of newly discovered evidence was insufficient to produce an acquittal. Finally, the inmate failed to establish either Strickland prong to support his ineffective assistance of counsel claims. As to the habeas petition, the court found that: (1) the trial court did not violate the inmate's right to the effective assistance of counsel; (2) claims that the inmate's due process rights in his direct appeal were violated because of State's failure to disclose facts pertinent to his direct appeal were procedurally barred because they were or should have been litigated on direct appeal or were or should have been brought in his postconviction relief motion; (3) prior convictions of one of the inmate's own witness's were a matter of public record, and not concealed by the State; and (4) Ring did not apply retroactively against the inmate.


OUTCOME: The order denying relief was affirmed, and the petition for habeas relief was denied.


 

479 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Ballard v. State


No. SC03-1012


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


923 So. 2d 475; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 273; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 139



February 23, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Collier County, Lauren Levy Brodie, Judge - Case No. 01-001353CR LLM.



DISPOSITION: We reverse. Judgment of acquittal is entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for a judgment of acquittal after the State's case-in-chief, and renewed the motion at the close of all the evidence. The Collier County Circuit Court (Florida) denied the motions. He was convicted of robbery and two counts of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's neighbors were beaten to death; their bodies were found in their apartment. He was a frequent visitor to their apartment. There was no direct evidence of his guilt. The entire circumstantial case presented against him consisted of (1) his fingerprint located on a waterbed frame near one victim's body, with no evidence presented as to when or how the fingerprint was left; and (2) one hair found on that victim's hand consistent with defendant's arm hair, with no evidence to ascertain if the hair was pulled out prematurely or naturally shed, and with that hair being only one out of six total arm hairs found in the victim's hand and among hundreds of hairs found at the crime scene. The high court held that the evidence was insufficient to prove that he robbed and killed the victims. The evidence was not inconsistent with his hypothesis of innocence -- that he was not guilty, and that someone else, perhaps a member of a gang that had shot into the victims' apartment a week before the murders, was guilty. The hair and fingerprint could just as well have been left at the apartment during one of defendant's numerous innocent visits to the premises as during the murders.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to enter a judgment of acquittal.


 

480 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Seibert v. State


No. SC03-800


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


923 So. 2d 460; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 260; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 125



February 16, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 4, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Seibert v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 793 (Fla., May 4, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Seibert v. Florida, 549 U.S. 893, 127 S. Ct. 198, 166 L. Ed. 2d 162, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5446 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Post-conviction relief denied at Seibert v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1113 (Fla., July 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Stanford Blake, Judge - Case No. F98008943.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Florida, denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and statements, he was convicted of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's roommate left him alone in his apartment with the victim. Later, defendant would not let him in and said he was going to kill himself. The roommate called 911. When police responded, defendant opened the door slightly, told them he was "okay," and shut the door. When he finally opened the door again, police forced their way in. Through an opened bathroom door, an officer saw a severed foot. The victim's body was dismembered; DNA in semen found in her vagina was consistent with defendant's. The high court held that the warrantless entry was justified by exigent circumstances, as police were not investigating a crime but were attempting to ensure that defendant would not kill himself. The State's asking experts if intercourse occurred after death did not require a mistrial. The prosecution did not bolster a witness's alibi. As the trial court sustained the objection to a question as to whether defendant hustled money from "gay guys," and gave a curative instruction, a mistrial was not required. Substantial evidence supported the conviction. The death sentence was proportionate. Defendant's prior violent felonies, an aggravating factor, fulfilled Ring v. Arizona's mandate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

481 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Frierson


No. SC03-1528


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


926 So. 2d 1139; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 147; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 81



February 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 12, 2006.
Rehearing denied by State v. Frierson, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 734 (Fla., Mar. 31, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Frierson v. Florida, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 9323 (U.S., Dec. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-1875. (Palm Beach County).
Frierson v. State, 851 So. 2d 293, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11774 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Up for review was a decision rendered by the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), specifically involving defendant, which was certified as directly in conflict with a separate decision in the Third District that didn't involve defendant, which held that the reasonableness of a search after arrest was not affected by the fact that the original stop made might have been without probable cause.


OVERVIEW: The conflict issue presented was: where there was no reasonable cause to justify a traffic stop, could an outstanding arrest warrant constitute an intervening circumstance that dissipated the taint of the illegal action, so that evidence uncovered during a search incident to arrest was admissible in evidence? The instant court first agreed with defendant that a stop for a violation of motor vehicle laws was similar to a Terry investigative detention and could be made when there was founded suspicion. But, a search incident to an outstanding warrant was sufficiently attenuated from the illegality of the original stop so as not to be sufficiently tainted by it to be the fruit of the poisonous tree, regardless of whether the standard for the original stop was probable cause or founded suspicion. Here, the brief amount of time that elapsed between the illegal stop and defendant's arrest weighed against finding the search attenuated. But, the outstanding arrest warrant was an intervening circumstance that weighed in favor of the firearm found in a search incident to the arrest being sufficiently distinguishable from the illegal stop so as to be purged of the stop's primary taint.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Fourth District was quashed, and the conviction and sentence imposed against defendant were ordered reinstated.

Walls v. State


No. SC03-633, No. SC03-1955


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


926 So. 2d 1156; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 150; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 101



February 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 7, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Walls v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 740 (Fla., Apr. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Okaloosa County, G. Robert Barron, Judge - Case No. 87-856CFA.
Walls v. State, 641 So. 2d 381, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1014 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Okaloosa County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in denying various ineffective assistance of counsel claims following an evidentiary hearing on the claims, and that the court erred in denying him a hearing on other ineffective assistance of counsel claims and a claim that his death sentence was improper because he was mentally retarded. The supreme court found that because the trial court did not have the benefit of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.203 when it denied a hearing on mental retardation, the court did not err in denying him post-conviction relief, but he could still file a Rule 3.203 motion for a determination of mental retardation as a bar to execution in the trial court and was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on that motion. His claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were denied. As to his habeas corpus petition, the trial court found the aggravating circumstances of a prior violent felony conviction, based on the contemporaneous murder of the victim, and that the murder was committed during the course of a burglary and a kidnapping. A unanimous jury found him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of these offenses. He was not entitled to postconviction relief on his Ring claims.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed, but appellant was entitled to file a motion for determination of mental retardation as a bar to execution in the circuit court. Habeas relief was denied.

Rutherford v. State


No. SC06-18


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


926 So. 2d 1100; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 101; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 59



January 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by Rutherford v. Florida, 126 S. Ct. 1191, 163 L. Ed. 2d 1145, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1081 (U.S., 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Post-conviction relief denied at Rutherford v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2370 (Fla., Oct. 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Paul Rasmussen, Judge - Case No. 85-I-476.
Rutherford v. State, 727 So. 2d 216, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2423 (Fla., 1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an inmate, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida), which denied his successive postconviction motion for relief (PCR) pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 with respect to a request to vacate his conviction and sentences. The inmate also sought a new trial. He had been convicted of first-degree murder and armed robbery, and he was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was found guilty in his initial trial, but a mistrial was granted. After a retrial, he was again found guilty. The jury recommended death, based on the presence of three aggravating factors. Post-conviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and petitions for writs of habeas corpus were denied. The trial court denied several motions relating to discovery and public records requests, and it denied the inmate's motion to vacate judgments of conviction and sentences pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. There was no merit to the alleged Brady violation, as it was uncertain whether the uncorroborated assertion of the witness was even made. Defendant's claims that a lethal injection violated the First and Eighth Amendments lacked merit, as they were based on the improper administration of sedatives, and there was no evidence of such misconduct. There was no entitlement to the public records requested under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.852(h)(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court and it denied the inmate's request for a new trial.

Fla. Dep't of Fin. Servs. v. Freeman


No. SC04-1492


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


921 So. 2d 598; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 35; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 53



January 26, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Donald R. Moran, Jr., Judge - Case No. 16 1986 CF 11599 A.
Freeman v. State, 858 So. 2d 319, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1175 (Fla., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 27.711 (2005), counsel for appellee death row inmate sought attorney fees from appellant Florida Department of Financial Services for work done on a petition for writ of certiorari filed in the United States Supreme Court. The Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Florida, granted counsel all the fees he requested; the Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court appointed counsel to represent the inmate in his appeal from the trial court's denial of postconviction relief. After the state supreme court denied relief, counsel filed a petition for writ of certiorari in the United States Supreme Court. The Department argued that counsel's fee request was unreasonable and that under § 27.711(4)(g), fees had to be limited to $ 2,500, plus applicable costs. The trial court awarded almost $ 28,000 in fees. The state supreme court held that the record did not adequately establish that unusual or extraordinary circumstances sufficiently existed in order to warrant compensation in excess of the statutory cap. No experts testified on behalf of counsel regarding what would have been a reasonable fee, or whether the case presented an extraordinary or unusual situation requiring fees in excess of the statutory amount. There was thus no competent, substantial evidence to support the trial court's decision. The court rejected counsel's constitutional challenges to § 27.711, as he raised them for the first time on appeal and it had previously ruled that statutory fee caps in death penalty cases were not facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The supreme court vacated the trial court's order and remanded for an evidentiary hearing on the issue of attorney's fees.

Maddox v. State


No. SC03-2110


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


923 So. 2d 442; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 6; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 24



January 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 2, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Maddox v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 407 (Fla., Mar. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. Second District - Case No. 2D02-4143 (Polk County).
Maddox v. State, 862 So. 2d 783, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 17372 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed the circuit court's convictions entered against petitioner of two counts of forgery, two counts of uttering a forged instrument, and one count each of driving with a suspended license and giving false information to a police officer. After a conflict of that decision was certified with a First District decision, the instant matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The Second District addressed petitioner's contention that the forged traffic citations were inadmissible pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 316.650(9) (2001), and that when the deputy issuing the citation learned that petitioner was not the person he said he was, but had signed that person's name, the deputy withdrew the charges and retained the documents as evidence of the forgery. Thus, it determined that the charges were no longer pending and the citations served as documentary evidence of petitioner's criminal conduct. In contrast, the First District's decision stating that the statute was unambiguous and not subject to judicial interpretation missed the mark in holding that citations should not be admissible in any trial under any circumstances. Further, its interpretation of § 316.650(9) essentially eradicated all prosecutions for forgery of a traffic citation, because in order to convict someone of forgery, the State had to specifically prove that the allegedly forged document was in fact a "public document" and was therefore actionable under the statute. Such could never be accomplished if the traffic citation could not be admitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: The First District decision was disapproved, and the judgment of the Second District Court of Appeal was upheld.

 

486 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Bush v. Holmes


No. SC04-2323, No. SC04-2324, No. SC04-2325


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


919 So. 2d 392; 2006 Fla. LEXIS 4; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 1



January 5, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District - Case Nos. 1D02-3160, 1D02-3163 and 1D02-3199 (Leon County).
Bush v. Holmes, 886 So. 2d 340, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17242 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida Appellate Court found that Florida was prohibited by Fla. Const. art. IX, § 1(a) from expending public funds to allow students to obtain a private school education in kindergarten through grade 12 as an alternative to a public school education. In so ruling, it found Fla. Stat. § 1002.38 (2005), authorizing school vouchers to pay for the private education, to be unconstitutional. Appellant governor appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellee concerned citizens filed complaints in the trial court challenging the constitutionality of a program, the Opportunity Scholarship Program (OSP), that permitted Florida to pay a student's tuition at a private school to allow the student to attend that school in a case where the student was attending a public school that was failing to meet certain minimum state standards. The OSP was codified at Fla. Stat. § 1002.38 (2005), and the concerned citizens challenged it on various constitutional grounds, including Fla. Const. art. IX, § 1(a), which governed the provision of public education to students in Florida. The trial court entered final summary judgment in favor of the concerned citizens and declared the OSP to be unconstitutional. On appeal, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment and agreed that the OSP was unconstitutional. On further review, the state supreme court found that Fla. Const. art. IX, § 1(a) mandated the provision of education through a free, uniform public school system and that the OSP's diversion of public money to the private school system that did not have to meet uniform educational standards violated that constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's decision finding that the state statute was unconstitutional and directed that the decision have prospective application to commence at the conclusion of the current school year.

Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. City of Gainesville


No. SC03-2273


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


918 So. 2d 250; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2507; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 829



December 8, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District - Case No. 1D02-1582 (Leon County).
Dep't of Revenue v. City of Gainesville, 859 So. 2d 595, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18074 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Department of Revenue, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which affirmed a trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee city. The city had brought suit seeking a declaration that the portions of Fla. Stat. ch. 97-197, imposing the tax obligation on its telecommunications facilities, were unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. VII, § 3(a).


OVERVIEW: The city became involved in the business of providing telecommunication services. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city and declared §§ 2 and 3 of Fla. Stat. ch. 97 - 197 facially unconstitutional. The lower court affirmed, holding that the property in question was being used by the city for a municipal purpose and that the legislature's attempt to condition the provision of those municipal services on the payment of an amount equal to any ad valorem tax liability was in direct conflict with Fla. Const. art. VII, § 3(a). The court, upon reviewing the applicable statutes and the meaning being various terms such as municipal purpose, held that providing telecommunications services did not, as a matter of law, always serve municipal or public purposes and, therefore, ad valorem taxation of a municipality's telecommunications facilities was not facially unconstitutional. The court agreed that telecommunications services were essential services but that, in providing those services, a municipality did not as a matter of law engage in an activity essential to the welfare of the community.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court that held that the statutory provisions imposing ad valorem taxation on telecommunications facilities were facially unconstitutional.

Fla. Dep't of State v. Martin


No. SC04-2265


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


916 So. 2d 763; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2207; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 780



November 10, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal--Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District--Case No. 1D04-4517 (Leon County).
Dep't of State, Div. of Elections v. Martin, 885 So. 2d 453, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15734 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2004).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Florida Department of State, Division of Elections, sought review of a declaration by the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) that Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253(2) (2004) was unconstitutional. The issue was whether Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253(2), which gave the Department absolute discretion to allow a candidate to withdraw after the 42nd day before an election, violated the separation of powers principle set forth in Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.


OVERVIEW: A candidate qualified with the Department as the Democratic Party candidate for a congressional district in the general election. Forty days before the election, the candidate sought to withdraw. The Department, relying on Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253(2), notified the candidate that his request to withdraw was denied. Thereafter, appellee Democratic Party Executive Committee sought a mandatory injunction requiring the Department to declare that a vacancy had been created by the candidate's withdrawal and to comply with Fla. Stat. ch. 100.111(4)(b) (2004). The trial court concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 100.111(4)(b) controlled the procedure for allowing a candidate's withdrawal and filling a vacancy in nomination and granted injunctive relief. The supreme court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253(2) vested the Department with absolute, unfettered discretion to decide whether to grant or deny a candidate's request to withdraw after the 42nd day before an election. Thus, Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253(2) was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority in violation of the separation of powers set forth in Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower appellate court was affirmed.

Holland v. State


No. SC03-1033, No. SC04-34


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


916 So. 2d 750; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2208; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 792



November 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Holland v. Florida, 547 U.S. 1078, 126 S. Ct. 1790, 164 L. Ed. 2d 531, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3174 (2006)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Holland v. Florida, 539 F.3d 1334, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 17552 (11th Cir. Fla., 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part Holland v. Tucker, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 46834 (S.D. Fla., Mar. 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Charles M. Greene, Judge--Case No. 90-15905 CF 10A. And an Original Proceeding--Habeas Corpus.
Holland v. State, 773 So. 2d 1065, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1979 (Fla., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief, filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851, in which he alleged two claims involving the ineffective assistance of counsel and one claim involving the trial court's summary denial of some of his claims. Defendant appealed said order and, also, petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing defendant's postconviction relief motion, the instant court found that the claims therein lacked merit, as defense counsel did not concede defendant's guilt and defendant failed to establish that any unprecedented mitigation, which would have assisted him at sentencing, actually existed. Second, the trial court made findings in summarily denying the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion, and also adopted and incorporated by reference the State's response to defendant's motion, making for meaningful appellate review. As to the habeas request, internal police records were not admissible; therefore, appellate counsel could not be deemed deficient for failing to raise the issue. Moreover, because defendant was convicted of attempting to commit a forcible felony, he was barred from asserting self-defense. Also, counsel testified to extensive preparation for trial and the potential penalty phase. Finally, appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the trial court's denial of a cause challenge to a juror and for denial of adequate peremptory challenges, as defendant failed to establish that counsel acted deficiently or that such deficiency prejudiced him.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed, and his petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

493 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Knight v. State


No. SC03-631, No. SC04-1366


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


923 So. 2d 387; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2124; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 768



November 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 10, 2005. Released for Publication February 24, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Peter R. Lopez, Judge--Case No. F74-5978. And an Original Proceedings--Habeas Corpus.
Knight v. State, 746 So. 2d 423, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2651 (Fla., 1998).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 from his convictions of two counts of first-degree murder and his death sentence. The inmate also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In 1974, the inmate was convicted of shooting the two victims to death during a robbery and was sentenced to death. On appeal of the trial court's judgment, the inmate contested the summary denial of the majority of his postconviction claims. The court affirmed, holding that there was no error in the trial court's determination that summary denial was appropriate. The court found that the inmate's claims were either procedurally barred, conclusively refuted by the record, facially or legally insufficient as alleged, or without merit as a matter of law. The court further held that the inmate was not entitled to habeas corpus relief on his claim that his counsel was ineffective for failing to raise on appeal the issue of the State's failure to resentence the inmate within a reasonable period of time because it concluded that the inmate was responsible, in part, for the delay in resentencing. The court also denied the inmate relief on his claim that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to ensure that a complete record was compiled on appeal because the record did in fact contain the allegedly omitted portions.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the inmate's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed, and the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

494 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Perez v. State


No. SC03-1651


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


919 So. 2d 347; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2057; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 729



October 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Perez v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 100 (Fla., Jan. 5, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Perez v. Florida, 126 S. Ct. 2359, 165 L. Ed. 2d 285, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 4407 (U.S., 2006)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Perez v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 7974 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., May 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County,

Burton C. Conner, Judge - Case No. 56 2001 CF003058A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County (Florida), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant was found guilty of murder, burglary, and robbery with a deadly weapon. The convictions arose against defendant and another from the stabbing of defendant's wife's aunt, and the removal of property from her residence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's case and his accomplice's case were severed prior to trial pursuant to stipulation. Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress the statements he made to a police detective because the detective implied that defendant was free to leave when he in fact knew that there was an outstanding felony arrest warrant for defendant at the time of the interview. The court found no error and held that, in the totality of the circumstances surrounding the interrogation, defendant's statement was made voluntarily in that defendant was given breaks, food, and was allowed to sleep, which contradicted any contention that his waiver was not voluntary. The court did find error, however, with regard to the application of the heinous, atrocious, or cruel fashion (HAC) factor to defendant because there was no eyewitness testimony that defendant struck the victim. Given there was no evidence establishing that defendant directed or otherwise knew that the victim would be killed or the manner of death, the trial court erred in applying the HAC aggravator to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated the death sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for a new penalty phase proceeding.

Logan v. State


No. SC03-1155


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


921 So. 2d 556; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2049; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 89



October 20, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 9, 2006.
Motion denied by Logan v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 149 (Fla., Feb. 9, 2006)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Logan v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 13820 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Sept. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions

Second District - Case No. 2D01-3151.

(Hendry County).
Logan v. State, 846 So. 2d 657, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7974 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) held that defendant's election in 2001 to be sentenced under Fla. Stat. ch. 921.001(4)(b)(1) (2001), also known as the 1983 guidelines, or Fla. Stat. ch. 921.002 (2001), also known as the Criminal Punishment Code (CPC), was an election to be resentenced according to the CPC. This decision conflicted with one from the instant court in 1989. Thus, this matter followed to address the conflict.


OVERVIEW: The question before the instant court was which sentencing provision applied to defendant's election: Fla. Stat. ch. 921.001(4)(b)(1) (2001) or Fla. Stat. ch. 921.002 (2001). Defendant argued that, like the appellant in Smith, his election was to be sentenced according to the 1983 guidelines. The instant court held that he was correct. The Second District's reliance upon Smith to reach its conclusion that defendant's election to be sentenced under the 1983 guidelines was an election to be sentenced under the CPC was erroneous, as a defendant who elected to be sentenced under the guidelines elected to be sentenced under the guidelines in effect at the time of the election. Under the facts herein, defendant's crime were committed prior to July 1, 1984, the effective date of the 1983 guidelines. Finally, the Second District also erred in concluding that the CPC applied to defendant, as defendant's offenses were not committed on or after October 1, 1998. The pertinent date was the date the offenses were committed, not the date of sentencing.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Second District was quashed, and the matter was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

Davis v. State

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 7, 2006.

Writ of habeas corpus denied Davis v. McDonough, 933 So. 2d 1153, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1371 (Fla., 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Davis v. Florida, 549 U.S. 895, 127 S. Ct. 206, 166 L. Ed. 2d 166, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5486 (2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Davis v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1867 (Fla., Nov. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County,

Thomas Penick, Jr., Judge - Case No. 85-8933 CFANO

And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Davis v. State, 915 So. 2d 95, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2052 (Fla., 2005)
Davis v. State, 620 So. 2d 152, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 597 (Fla., 1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida), which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant was convicted of robbery, grand theft, and first-degree murder. On direct appeal, defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and the death sentence imposed against him was affirmed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from the murder of a man who was moving into an apartment complex that defendant allegedly assisted. The jury recommended the death penalty, and the trial judge sentenced defendant to life in prison on the robbery conviction, five years on the grand theft conviction, and death for the murder conviction. Defendant asserted that his counsel was ineffective at the penalty phase of his trial by spending only 11 hours preparing, by failing to conduct a thorough investigation, and by not providing any mitigating circumstances. The court disagreed and held that defendant's trial counsel had the full benefit of information obtained by the public defender's office, which included matters pertaining to defendant's background and upbringing. Since that information contained in the public defender's file was reviewed and considered by defendant's trial counsel, the investigation was not inadequate nor unreasonable. The court also noted that defendant's asserted mitigating evidence was cumulative. Other arguments asserted by defendant were found meritless or procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's postconviction relief motion and the denial of his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


 

497 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



State v. Steele


No. SC04-802


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


921 So. 2d 538; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2043; 31 Fla. L. Weekly S 74



October 12, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 2, 2006. As Corrected February 2, 2006. As Corrected October 20, 2005.
Rehearing denied by State v. Steele, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 140 (Fla., Feb. 2, 2006)
Related proceeding at, Petition denied by Steele v. State, 11 So. 3d 953, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 9883 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2009)
Related proceeding at, Petition dismissed by Steele v. State, 109 So. 3d 213, 2013 Fla. App. LEXIS 4271 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Writ denied by, Certificate of appealability denied Steele v. Sec'y, Dep't of Corr., 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 87356 (M.D. Fla., July 6, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions.

Second District - Case No. 2D04-1049.

(Pasco County).
State v. Steele, 872 So. 2d 364, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5581 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After making a decision on a petition for writ of certiorari, the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), certified two questions on whether a trial court departed from applicable law by: (1) requiring the State to provide pre-guilt or pre-penalty phase notice of aggravating factors to be used for capital punishment; and (2) requiring the jury to use a special verdict form detailing the jurors' determination concerning aggravating factors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for capital murder. He challenged the constitutionality of the death penalty. That challenge was denied, but the trial court imposed requirements that included the State providing advanced notice of the aggravators it intended to rely on and a special verdict form requiring jurors to detail their voting on the aggravators. The State sought certiorari review and the lower appellate court held that the first requirement was improper, but the second was proper. Considering the potential that each decision had to depart from established law, the court certified the two questions for review. The court held that the provision of notice by the State was not a substantial departure from its existing disclosure obligation and was not an undue burden on the State. Moreover, there was no requirement that the State provide such notice, but a trial court could, in its discretion, require it. However, the special jury verdict form imposed an additional statutory factor on Fla. Stat. § 921.141 of a majority on a specific aggravator when only a majority of the jury finding any aggravating factor was required. Therefore, the special verdict form was improper.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision and remanded to deny certiorari on that portion of the order requiring the State to provide notice of aggravators, but to grant certiorari and quash the order requiring a special verdict form to the jury. The court answered the first question "no" and the second question "yes."

Floyd v. State

913 So. 2d 564; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2042



October 12, 2005, Decided

Floyd v. State, 829 So. 2d 212, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 16505 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pinellas County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder. After the jury recommended a death sentence, the trial court sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a fugitive, was living under an alias with his daughter and her son. He believed that the victim had succeeded in causing the loss of the daughter's Medicaid coverage for his sick grandson. He told another co-worker of his daughter that he would "get" the victim. Thereafter, the victim disappeared. Six years later, she was found dead. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death. On appeal, the state supreme court found the evidence supported the conviction, the expert testimony was properly admitted, the evidence of kidnapping should not have been admitted but the error was harmless, and defendant was properly sentenced to death.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder and his sentence of death.

 

499 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Chandler v. Crosby


No. SC04-518


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


916 So. 2d 728; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1988; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 661



October 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 9, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Chandler v. McDonough, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 7564 (U.S., Oct. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Chandler v. State, 873 So. 2d 1222, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 222 (Fla., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought an original habeas corpus proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder, and the trial court sentenced him to death. The inmate's habeas petition claimed that a United States Supreme Court decision compelled reversal. That decision held that a testimonial hearsay statement was inadmissible at trial unless the declarant was shown to be unavailable and the party against whom the statement was admitted had an opportunity for cross-examination. However, the court in the habeas proceeding found that the United States Supreme Court decision did not apply retroactively. The new procedural rule could have only applied retroactively if retroactive application was deemed necessary. The rule's purpose was not to improve the accuracy of trials or even to improve the reliability of evidence. The old rule was relied on for over 20 years, and much testimonial hearsay was admitted under the old rule. The administration of justice would have been greatly affected by retroactive application which would have destroyed the stability of the law, rendered punishments uncertain and therefore ineffectual, and burdened the judicial machinery, fiscally and intellectually, beyond any tolerable limit.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

Duckett v. State


No. SC01-2149, No. SC02-1300


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


918 So. 2d 224; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1986; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 667



October 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 22, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Duckett v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2701 (Fla., Dec. 22, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Duckett v. Florida, 549 U.S. 846, 127 S. Ct. 103, 166 L. Ed. 2d 78, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6586 (Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County,

Jerry T. Lockett, Judge - Case No. 87-1347CF

and a Habeas Corpus - Original Proceeding.
Duckett v. State, 568 So. 2d 891, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 1117 (Fla., Sept. 6, 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida) that denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief; defendant claimed, inter alia, that certain exculpatory evidence was not presented and that his counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a former police officer, took an 11-year old girl to a lake, raped her, and killed her. The evidence was circumstantial: tire tracks at the scene matched the ones on defendant's car, defendant's and the victim's fingerprints were commingled on the hood of defendant's patrol car, and defendant's pubic hair was found in the victim's underpants. One of the State's witnesses recanted her testimony, recanted portions of her recantation, and then invoked the privilege against self-incrimination. The state supreme court held, inter alia, that because the witness would not testify, the purported change in her testimony was unlikely to result in a different verdict. Although the case against defendant was circumstantial, strong evidence besides the witness's testimony linked him to the murder. Trial counsel was not ineffective for stipulating to consolidation of the charges under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.150(a) since the offenses were committed by the same person on a single victim in a single episode. Therefore, the trial court properly denied defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed, and defendant's petition for habeas corpus relief was denied.

Wright v. State


No. SC04-137


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


911 So. 2d 81; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1690; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 611



September 1, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case No. 2D03-3165 (Pinellas County).
Wright v. State, 864 So. 2d 1153, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 19780 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, Second District (Florida), certifed direct conflict with five opinions of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), on the issue of whether the failure of a sentencing court to provide written reasons for retaining jurisdiction, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 947.16(3)(a) (Supp. 1978), constituted an illegal sentence for Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) purposes.


OVERVIEW: The second district had ruled that the failure to provide written reasons for retaining jurisdiction did not constitute an illegal sentence and thus Rule 3.800(a), which allowed for challenge's to illegal sentences at any time, did not apply. The supreme court agreed, noting its approval of the second district's analogy to cases in which a trial court failed to provide written reasons for sentencing departures. Neither failure was of the magnitude necessary to constitute an unlawful sentence. Thus, the court approved the second district's decision and disapproved the decisions in Kirtsey v. State, 855 So. 2d 177 (Fla. 1st Dist. Ct. App. 2003); Hernandez v. State, 825 So. 2d 513 (Fla. 4th Dist. Ct. App. 2002); Bingham v. State, 813 So. 2d 1021 (Fla. 1st Dist. Ct. App. 2002); Thames v. State, 769 So. 2d 448 (Fla. 1st Dist. Ct. App. 2000); Hampton v. State, 764 So. 2d 829 (Fla. 1st Dist. Ct. App. 2000); and Macias v. State, 614 So. 2d 1216 (Fla. 3d Dist. Ct. App. 1993), to the extent they conflicted with the supreme court's ruling.


OUTCOME: The court approved the second district's decision and disapproved each of the first and third district decisions to the extent they conflicted with the supreme court's decision.

Robinson v. State


No. SC03-1229, No. SC04-772


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


913 So. 2d 514; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1452; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 576



July 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 18, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Robinson v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2130 (Fla., Oct. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Dorothy J. Russell, Judge - Case No. CR 94-9210 And an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Robinson v. State, 761 So. 2d 269, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1367 (Fla., 1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) to first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to death. Defendant's sentence of death was affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant's postconviction motion pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 was denied. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion for postconviction relief and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying an evidentiary hearing on claims of ineffective assistance of counsel during the penalty phase and that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate and withdraw defendant's guilty plea. The state supreme court found that (1) trial counsel was not ineffective at the sentencing hearing as counsel secured competent mental health experts who effectively conveyed their findings regarding defendant to the trial court; (2) trial counsel was not ineffective for following the state supreme court's express mandate that defendant's sentencing be conducted before the judge rather than a jury; (3) trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to seek recusal of the sentencing judge because counsel considered the issue, discussed it with defendant, and made a strategic decision not to seek recusal; and (4) trial counsel was not ineffective by failing to support an oral motion to withdraw defendant's guilty plea as the record showed defendant's waiver of a trial was intelligently and voluntarily made; and (5) defendant's habeas claim was procedurally barred because it was also raised in the postconviction proceeding.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's postconviction motion was affirmed, and defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

508 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Global Travel Mktg., Inc. v. Shea


No. SC03-1704


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


908 So. 2d 392; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1454; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 511



July 7, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-910 (Broward County).
Shea v. Global Travel Mktg., Inc., 870 So. 2d 20, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12815 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee father, as personal representative of his minor son's estate, sued appellant travel agency in the trial court on behalf of the estate and for both parents as survivors under Florida's wrongful death statute. The trial court granted the travel agency's motion to stay the proceedings and compel arbitration. The Court of Appeals of Florida for the Fourth District reversed the decision, and certified a question of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: The mother signed a commercial travel contract with the travel agency for an African safari on behalf of herself and her son. The contract contained an arbitration clause. During the safari, the son was killed by one or more hyenas. The father alleged that the mother did not have legal authority to contract away their son's substantive rights through the arbitration clause. The appellate court ruled that the child's estate could not be bound to arbitrate tort claims arising from the safari. The state supreme court found that it was not foreclosed by 9 U.S.C.S. § 2 (2000) of the Federal Arbitration Act from determining the enforceability of the arbitration agreement solely on public policy grounds under Florida law. The court further held that the arbitration provision in the contract was not unconscionable, in violation of any statutory prohibition, or void as against public policy. Because the mother had authority to enter into the contract on behalf of her minor child, pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. 14 and Fla. Stat. art. I, § 23, the arbitration provision was valid and enforceable in the wrongful death action arising from the contract.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court answer the certified question in the affirmative, quashed the decision of the appellate court, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

510 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Ratliff v. State


No. SC02-1239, No. SC03-2059, No. SC03-2304


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


914 So. 2d 938; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1464; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 534



July 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 13, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ratliff v. Florida, 126 S. Ct. 1574, 164 L. Ed. 2d 307, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 2316 (U.S., 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Helm v. Florida, 126 S. Ct. 2300, 164 L. Ed. 2d 823, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 4049 (U.S., May 22, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates filed petitions for writs of habeas corpus. The three cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The inmates argued that their life sentences were unconstitutional pursuant to Fla. Const. art. I, § 17, which prohibited indefinite terms of imprisonment. The court disagreed. Any sentence, no matter how short, may eventually have extended beyond the life of a prisoner. Mortality and life expectancy were irrelevant to limitations on the terms of incarceration set by the legislature for criminal misconduct. It was abundantly clear that the legislature, by prescribing a sentence of life imprisonment, intended that the defendant remain in prison for the rest of his life. The term "life" was sufficiently definite so that it could have been understood and applied. There was nothing indefinite about such a sentence.


OUTCOME: The petitions were denied.

 

511 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sunset Harbour Condo. Ass'n v. Robbins


No. SC03-520


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


914 So. 2d 925; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1459; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 763



July 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Corrected November 3, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Sunset Harbour North Condo. Ass'n v. Robbins, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2125 (Fla., Nov. 3, 2005).


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal--Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Third District--Case No. 3D02-2316 (Dade County).
Sunset Harbour N. Condo. Ass'n v. Robbins, 837 So. 2d 1181, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 2170 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2003).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) found that a statute requiring property appraisers to place no assessed valuation on real property if improvements to it were not substantially completed by January 1st was unconstitutional. Thus, it affirmed the trial court's summary judgment grant to appellee property appraiser, who claimed that the statute violated Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4. Appellant property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's condominium project was in the final stages of construction as of January 1, 1997. The property appraiser determined that it was substantially complete as of that date and assessed the property at a certain valuation. The property owner filed suit and argued that under Fla. Stat. ch. 192.042(1) (1997), the improvements to the property should have been assessed no value because the condominium was not "substantially complete" on January 1, 1997. The property appraiser raised as an affirmative defense that the statute violated Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4, directing the legislature to prescribe regulations securing a just valuation of property and, was, therefore, unconstitutional. The trial court concluded the statute was unconstitutional and granted summary judgment in the property appraiser's favor. The appellate court affirmed. On further review, the property owner raised for the first time the issue of whether the property appraiser had standing to challenge the statute. The state supreme court found that the issue of standing was waived for the property owner's failure to raise it earlier and that the statute did not violate the Florida Constitution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to the appellate court for further proceedings.

Mansfield v. State


No. SC03-1352, No. SC04-331


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


911 So. 2d 1160; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1453; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 598



July 7, 2005, Decided

Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part, Stay granted by Mansfield v. Sec'y, 601 F. Supp. 2d 1267, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15088 (M.D. Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Osceola County, Belvin Perry, Jr., Judge - Case No. CR 95-2078 And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
