CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner death row inmate appealed a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Osceola County (Florida), which denied the inmate's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. The inmate also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted on a charge of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. Both the conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The court affirmed the denial of the postconviction motion, holding that (1) statements made by the trial judge regarding its concern over the timing of a proposed plea agreement did not indicate bias or prejudice against the inmate, and there was no basis for disqualifying the trial judge; (2) none of the inmate's claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel had merit; (3) testimony from a jailhouse informant did not violate Giglio because there was no showing that he gave false testimony about any pending federal charges against him, and thus, the prosecutor could not have been aware of any false testimony, and given other evidence that eroded the informant's credibility, information about other federal charges against him would not have been material; (4) on the habeas petition, counsel on the direct appeal could not be considered ineffective because the claims the inmate argued counsel should have made would have been without merit or procedurally barred; and (5) the inmate's Ring and Caldwell claims were denied.


OUTCOME: The order denying the postconviction motion was affirmed, and the petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.


 

513 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Zack v. State


No. SC03-1374, No. SC04-201


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


911 So. 2d 1190; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1456; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 591



July 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Zack v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1919 (Fla., Sept. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Linda Lee Nobles, Judge - Case No. 96-2517-CFA And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Zack v. State, 753 So. 2d 9, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 8 (Fla., Jan. 6, 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief (PCR) under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 from a jury conviction for first-degree murder, sexual battery, and robbery and from a sentence of death. The prisoner also filed an original petition for a writ of habeas corpus for relief from the same convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was sentenced to death after he was found guilty of murdering a woman he sexually assaulted. the prisoner's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 PCR motion on the grounds of ineffective assistance of trial counsel, failure of the trial court to sua sponte hold a Frye hearing on DNA evidence, and the constitutionality of his death sentence, among other grounds, was denied. On appeal, he also sought habeas corpus relief on multiple grounds of alleged ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The court found that the Rule 3.851 motion was properly denied. Since the prisoner admitted to sexual contact with the victim, DNA evidence did not prove any fact in the case, so any error in not holding a Frye hearing was harmless. The trial court properly found trial counsel's testimony more credible than the prisoner's on whether the prisoner was properly prepared to testify. Whether the prisoner was mentally retarded and thereby not subject to capital punishment was sufficiently explored by the trial court, and the death penalty statute was not unconstitutional. As to habeas corpus relief, appellate counsel was not deficient for failing to raise meritless and unpreserved claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the prisoner's motion for postconviction relief. The court also denied the prisoner relief under the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

516 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. Howard


No. SC03-2270


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


916 So. 2d 640; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1358; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 498



June 30, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District. - Case No. 1D02-3762. (Leon County).
Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. Howard, 859 So. 2d 619, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18069 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Florida Department of Revenue sought review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), which declared that Fla. Stat. ch. 193.016 (2001) violated the mandate of Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court had ruled that Fla. Stat. ch. 193.016 (2001) was unconstitutional because it interfered with a property appraiser's discretion to determine just value, and it favored tangible personal property owners who had received a reduced assessment from an administrative value adjustment board (VAB) in a previous tax year. The supreme court disagreed. Chapter 193.016 required an appraiser to consider the results of an appeal before VAB in the year prior in determining the current just value of tangible personal property. Fla. Stat. ch. 193.011 (2001) set out eight factors that were to be considered in valuing property. Fla. Stat. ch. 193.016 (2001) merely provided a ninth factor for consideration. It did not arbitrarily create a class of property for favored tax treatment. Further, ch. 193.016 did not require an appraiser to follow the VAB's assessment, it only required an appraiser to "consider" it. The statute's second sentence, which required an appraiser to justify his or her reasons for a decision to depart from a VAB assessment, simply regulated the procedural, not substantive, method of assessment where there had been a successful appeal to a VAB.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the appellate court's decision and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the supreme court's decision.

 

517 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Raymond


No. SC03-1263


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


906 So. 2d 1045; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1357; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 500



June 30, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Third District. - Case No. 3D02-1711. (Dade County).
State v. Raymond, 847 So. 2d 565, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8757 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion for nonmonetary pretrial release was denied, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 907.041(4)(b) (2000), a judicial circuit's appellate division reviewed the matter and found that ch. 907.041(b)(4) was unconstitutional as a procedural rule which encroached on the Florida Supreme Court's exclusive rulemaking power. The State of Florida appealed. The Third District Court of Appeal of Florida affirmed the decision. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with misdemeanor battery that involved domestic violence. After defendant was brought before the county court for her first appearance, the county court found that defendant qualified for nonmonetary release to pretrial services because she had no prior offenses. Despite making a finding that defendant qualified, the county court found that it could not grant nonmonetary pretrial release pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 907.041(4)(b). The county court therefore set bond, and scheduled a second hearing. Defendant could not afford to post the bond, and remained in jail until the second scheduled appearance. The state supreme court found that, because ch. 907.041(4)(b) was unconstitutional, and because the Florida Legislature repealed those portions of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.131 and 3.132 that required trial judges to consider nonmonetary pretrial release at the first appearance hearing for defendants charged with dangerous crimes, including domestic violence, a vacuum existed concerning when trial judges could consider these defendants for nonmonetary pretrial release. Therefore, the court temporarily readopted Rules 3.131 and 3.132 in their entirety.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

518 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sult v. State


No. SC03-542


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


906 So. 2d 1013; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1343; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 470



June 23, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 2D01-5013 (Pinellas County).
Sult v. State, 839 So. 2d 798, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 2410 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida District Court of Appeal, Second District, certified the following question as one of great public importance: Is Fla. Stat. ch. 843.085 (2001) unconstitutional as overbroad, vague, or in violation of the right of substantive due process? Petitioner individual had previously been convicted of violating the statute.


OVERVIEW: The individual was arrested for violating ch. 843.085(1) after she was observed wearing an official sheriff's department t-shirt, which she had purchased at a uniform store that was open to the public. The statute made it unlawful for unauthorized individuals to wear such clothing because it could deceive a reasonable person into believing that an individual was authorized by an official agency to display or wear it. Answering the certified question in the affirmative, the supreme court found ch. 843.085(1) to be unconstitutionally overbroad under the First Amendment and Fla. Const. art. I, § 9, and in violation of substantive due process. The statute was overbroad because it did not contain any intent or scienter requirement. It made no distinction between innocent wearing or displaying of law enforcement indicia from that designed to deceive the reasonable public into believing that such display was official. The statute violated substantive due process because the imprecision in its language failed to give fair notice of what conduct it prohibited. Thus, the statute invited arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered in the affirmative, the appellate court's decision was quashed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings in accord with the supreme court's opinion.

Ferrell v. State

Maura T. Smith, Judge - Case No. CR 92-4096 And an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.

Aguilera v. Inservices, Inc.


No. SC03-368


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


905 So. 2d 84; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1298; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 440



June 16, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case No. 3D01-867. (Dade County).
Inservices, Inc. v. Aguilera, 837 So. 2d 464, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 19174 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured employee sought review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Third District (Florida), which reversed the trial court's decision to deny appellee workers' compensation insurance carrier's motion to dismiss based upon immunity under Fla. Stat. ch. 440 (2000).


OVERVIEW: The injured employee was injured at work. He was transported to an emergency room and was found to have blood in his urine. Immediately following the injuries, he received medical care that was supervised and controlled by the carrier. Subsequently, the carrier denied authorization for examination or treatment by a urologist, asserting that the injury was not work-related. The carrier was again notified that emergency urological care was needed because the employee's urine had begun to smell like feces. The carrier intervened and actually blocked the employee's receipt of medication. Testing ultimately revealed that the employee had a hole in his bladder. The employee was forced to be seen by no fewer than six doctors in addition to his initial treating physician. Each of them concluded that his physical injuries were related to the initial accident and that his condition as a result required urgent surgical treatment. The supreme court held that the allegations went far beyond simple claim delay or a simple termination of benefits. The injuries at issue did not occur at the workplace, but the injuries were allegedly inflicted by the carrier during the claims handling process.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower appellate court was quashed. The matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Elledge v. State


No. SC03-1201, SC04-998


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


911 So. 2d 57; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1280; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 429



June 9, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 2, 2005.
Later proceeding at Elledge v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1765 (Fla., Sept. 2, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Elledge v. Florida, 546 U.S. 1157, 126 S. Ct. 1173, 163 L. Ed. 2d 1141, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1054 (U.S., Jan. 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Charles M. Greene, Judge - Case No. 75-87 CF10A.
Elledge v. Florida, 525 U.S. 944, 119 S. Ct. 366, 142 L. Ed. 2d 303, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6435 (1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial by the Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), of his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. The appeal involved allegations of error pertaining to defendant's fourth penalty phase proceeding after which he was sentenced to death for a first-degree murder which occurred 31 years earlier.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to a weekend of crimes, which included the rape and murder of one victim and the murder and robbery of two other victims. Defendant was sentenced to death. The matter was remanded several times. Defendant was again sentenced to death in his fourth penalty phase proceeding. The appellate court held that all of defendant's postconviction issues were meritless. The trial court correctly denied defendant's Brady claim because he could not satisfy any of the elements of the Brady test. Any assertion that an expert could have mined the data underlying an EEG report to discover mitigating evidence pertaining to defendant's mental status was speculative at best and did not support the existence of a Brady violation. Defendant was similarly unable to establish that the State either willfully or inadvertently suppressed the EEG report. Finally, defendant could not satisfy the prejudice prong of the Brady analysis as the results of the EEG were normal. Defense counsel's failure to call the expert could be attributed to no other cause than the expert's clear intent not to testify. Any challenge to the restraint employed during the penalty phase was procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed. The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

523 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Marshall v. Crosby


No. SC02-420


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


911 So. 2d 1129; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1170; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 399



May 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Marshall v. Crosby, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1924 (Fla., Sept. 15, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Marshall v. McDonough, 547 U.S. 1143, 126 S. Ct. 2059, 164 L. Ed. 2d 807, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3706 (May 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Marshall v. State, 604 So. 2d 799, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1274 (Fla., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner under sentence of death, petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. The prisoner argued that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to raise the trial court's denial of a motion for the appointment of an additional mental health expert, that the trial judge's override of the jury's recommendation in favor of life was unconstitutional, and that the standard for jury override cases was arbitrarily applied.


OVERVIEW: The jury found the prisoner guilty of first-degree murder and recommended a sentence of life imprisonment. However, the trial court rejected the jury's recommendation and imposed a sentence of death. The Florida Supreme Court affirmed the jury override on appeal. Defense counsel's request that a specific expert be appointed was granted. Defense counsel's subsequent request that an additional expert be appointed was denied. The supreme court held that appellate counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise that issue. Even if Ring called Florida's jury override procedures into question, the prisoner's nine prior violent felonies were an aggravating circumstance that took his sentence outside the scope of Ring's requirements. The record contained insufficient evidence to reasonably support the jury's recommendation of life. The victim, a fellow prisoner, was bound and died of blows to the back of the head. He received no less than 25 separate wounds. Blood was sprayed about the cell. Nothing in those facts supported self defense or acting in the heat of a fight. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the facts supported the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

524 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Washington v. State


No. SC04-15


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


907 So. 2d 512; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1104; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 345



May 12, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Washington v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1476 (Fla., July 7, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Washington v. Florida, 126 S. Ct. 802, 163 L. Ed. 2d 632, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 9096 (U.S., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Washington v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2488 (Fla., Oct. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Susan F. Schaeffer, Judge - Case No. 90-6491CFANO-M.
Washington v. State, 653 So. 2d 362, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1874 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in overriding the jury's recommendation for a life sentence in imposing a death sentence, primarily relying on the Keen case. The appeals court disagreed. The singular focus was whether there was a reasonable basis to support the jury's recommendation of life, rather than the weighing process which a judge conducted after a death recommendation. The judge here, as in Keen, intermixed the standards for life and death recommendations. However, defendant failed to raise this claim in his present Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion. Thus, he was procedurally barred from raising it under the instant circumstances. Second, the court already addressed the applicability of Keen on collateral review and held that Keen was nothing more than an application of a long-standing analysis. Third, any error in this regard was harmless. Whereas in the Keen case, there was ample mitigating evidence on which the jury reasonably could have based a life recommendation, in defendant's case, there was none. Finally, defendant was not entitled to relief under Ring v. Arizona, as Ring did not apply retroactively in Florida.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant the relief he requested was affirmed.


 

525 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Hughes v. State


No. SC02-2247


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


901 So. 2d 837; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 753; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 285



April 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 27, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 1D02-1258. (Washington County).
Hughes v. State, 826 So. 2d 1070, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 14236 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington County Circuit Court (Florida) convicted petitioner inmate of battery by a jail detainee on a jail detainee, a third-degree felony, and the court sentenced him to a term longer than the statutory maximum. The inmate was also denied relief on his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion. The First District Court of Appeal certified a question for review, and this matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The First District certified as a question of great public importance whether the rule announced in Apprendi applied retroactively. The instant court held that it did not because a retroactive application would require review of the record and sentencing proceedings in many cases simply to identify cases where Apprendi might apply. In every case Apprendi affected, a new jury would have to be empaneled to determine, at least, the issue causing the sentence enhancement. Many, if not all, of the surrounding facts would have to be presented. In others, a jury would have to determine factors unrelated to the case. Finally, the instant court found it unpersuasive that courts unanimously considered Apprendi to be a rule of procedure that simply changed who decided certain sentencing issues. The right to a jury trial itself was not retroactive; thus, the instant court failed to see how a subset of that right, a jury determination of facts relevant to sentencing, could be retroactive.


OUTCOME: The question was answered in the negative, and the decision of the First District was approved.

 

526 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. SC03-1042


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


904 So. 2d 400; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 755; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 297



April 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Johnson v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1345 (Fla., June 10, 2005)
Related proceeding at Johnson v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2884 (Fla., Dec. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, A. Thomas Mihok, Judge - Case No. CR80-101.
Johnson v. State, 442 So. 2d 193, 1983 Fla. LEXIS 2959 (Fla., 1983)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which summarily denied his second successive motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 for postconviction relief (PCR) from murder convictions and a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's first-degree murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Two PCR motions were denied. Defendant filed a third PCR motion, claiming that his due process and equal protection rights were violated when public documents relevant to his case were improperly withheld, that his death sentence was unconstitutional under the Ring rule, and that execution by lethal injection constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The circuit court denied the motion without an evidentiary hearing (EH). Defendant appealed. The court rejected the argument that an EH was required on the document claim since defendant did not explain how the documents would produce an acquittal and the circuit court conducted an appropriate in camera document review before summarily rejecting the claim. The Ring rule's mandate that a jury, not a judge, had to find every fact justifying a death penalty was a new rule. It did not apply retroactively to defendant since his conviction was final when the Ring case was decided. Finally, lethal injection was not cruel and unusual punishment, and the claim was procedurally barred because it was raised and rejected in a prior PCR proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary denial of defendant's PCR motion.

 

527 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Bryant v. State


Nos. SC03-1618 & SC04-83


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


901 So. 2d 810; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 756; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 310



April 28, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Lucy Chernow Brown, Judge - Case No. 92-791CF A02 And an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Bryant v. State, 785 So. 2d 422, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 630 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida), which struck, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion for postconviction relief (PCR) from convictions for murder and armed robbery and from a sentence of death and which, alternatively, denied the motion. Defendant also filed an original proceeding for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's timely PCR motion was struck for failure to satisfy the pleading requirements of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851. A subsequent amended motion was struck as untimely and was summarily denied on the merits. On appeal, the court found that the original motion should have been struck with leave to amend, which would have made the amended motion timely. Regardless, ineffective assistance of trial counsel claims lacked merit. Also, since he waived a jury for his penalty phase, defendant could not challenge the constitutionality of whether a judge, and not a jury, properly determined that sufficient death penalty aggravators existed. The court rejected a separate habeas corpus petition that was premised on ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. A confession was voluntary and was obtained after an arrest properly supported by probable cause, so failure to challenge whether it should have been suppressed was not erroneous. Even though an avoid arrest aggravator under Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(e) (1997) lacked factual support, no prejudice occurred. The properly applied aggravators of a prior violent felony and a crime committed for pecuniary gain were sufficient to impose death.


OUTCOME: The court held that striking defendant's PCR motion on subject matter jurisdiction grounds was improper, but the court affirmed the denial of the motion on the merits. The court also denied defendant's petition for habeas corpus.

Green v. State


No. SC02-2315


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


907 So. 2d 489; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 760; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 318



April 28, 2005, Decided

Rehearing denied by Green v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1469 (Fla., July 7, 2005)

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, William Fuente, Judge - Case No. 86-14233 CFAWS.
Green v. State, 620 So. 2d 188, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 975 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder, appealed his sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) in a new penalty phase trial. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in answering the jury's question with regard to when a life sentence without the possibility of parole would start.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived in a rented duplex apartment with his girlfriend. They rented the apartment from the victims. Defendant paid the victims $ 250 for back rent. After using drugs, defendant went over to retrieve the money to purchase additional drugs. The victims refused. Defendant admitted stabbing both of them to death. The record demonstrated that application of the pecuniary gain aggravator was supported by competent, substantial evidence. Defendant waived any argument in regard to the burglary aggravator. Comparing the circumstances to other cases, the sentence of death was proportionate.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

Dufour v. State


No. SC03-1326, No. SC04-232


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


905 So. 2d 42; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 691; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 247



April 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Dufour v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1347 (Fla., June 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Lawrence Kirkwood, Judge - Case No. 82-8467. And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Dufour v. State, 495 So. 2d 154, 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2617 (Fla., 1986)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of motion affirmed and petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The supreme court found the record demonstrated that trial counsel made an informed and reasoned decision not to pursue a voluntary intoxication defense, which was inconsistent with the underlying defense theory of the case. Moreover, defendant failed to establish that the defense was viable because he could not demonstrate that he was actually intoxicated at the time of the offense. Moreover, the inmate failed to demonstrate that he suffered prejudice as a result of defense counsel's decision not to obtain additional mental health opinions. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the admission of evidence of the inmate's sexuality in order to demonstrate the inmate's motive or state of mind at the time of the murder.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the postconviction relief motion was affirmed, and the petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Patchen v. Fla. Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs.


No. SC02-1291


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


906 So. 2d 1005; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 692; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 241



April 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Patchen v. Fla. Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs., 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1471 (Fla., July 1, 2005)
Petition denied by Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs. v. Patchen, 2010 Fla. App. LEXIS 526 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Jan. 27, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Third District - Case No. 3D01-1440. (Dade County).
Patchen v. State Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs., 817 So. 2d 854, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 2348 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Decision of the district court quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed an order granting summary judgment to respondent, the Florida Department of Agriculture, in petitioner landowners' inverse condemnation action, finding that the landowners had no cause of action because the destruction of citrus trees located within 1900 feet of trees infected with citrus canker had no marketable value. Upon a certified question for review, the instant matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The district court certified the following of great public importance for review by the instant court: Did a Florida Supreme Court decision, which held that the Department of Agriculture's destruction of healthy commercial citrus nursery stock within 125 feet of trees infected with citrus canker did not compel state reimbursement, also apply to the Department's destruction of uninfected, healthy noncommercial, residential citrus trees within 1900 feet of trees infected with citrus canker? The instant court held that both the trial court and the district court decided the case on the basis of the statute and administrative rule in 2000, when the landowners' trees were destroyed. However, the 2002 statute clearly intended that the landowners be included with those affected homeowners covered by Fla. Stat. ch. 581.1845(2) in that their citrus trees were removed as part of a citrus canker eradication program after January 1, 1995. Thus, they were eligible to receive compensation pursuant to that statute, which was remedial in nature.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was quashed, and the case was remanded.

 

532 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. SC02-285


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


899 So. 2d 1090; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 593; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 197



March 31, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fifth District. - Case No. 5D00-3064. (Volusia County).
State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. v. Warren, 805 So. 2d 1074, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 952 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) expressly declared Fla. Stat. ch. 627.736(5)(b) (1999) constitutional after the county court found that said statute unconstitutionally violated petitioner doctor's rights to equal protection, due process, and access to the courts. Petitioner insured and the doctor sought further review of the decision, which favored respondent insurer.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners contended that the 30-day provision within Fla. Stat. ch. 627.736(5)(b) (1999) violated their equal protection and due process rights and the right of access to the courts. The instant court disagreed. The intent of the statute was to impose time limits on the submission of medical bills under the no-fault scheme rather than adhere to the limitations period provided for breach of contract actions. There was a logical explanation for this intent as medical providers frequently provided ongoing medical treatment involving regular office visits. Because the different billing requirements were calculated to reduce unnecessary medical costs, which in turn lowered the costs upon which insurers based personal injury protection (PIP) premiums and ultimately benefitted consumers, ch. 627.736(5)(b) was rationally related to this legitimate purpose. Second, the analysis involved in the due process determination closely resembled that of the equal protection analysis. Thus, the instant court found no due process violation. Finally, the statute imposed a reasonable condition precedent to filing a claim for certain insurance benefits, and compliance preserved access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The holding of the lower court was approved.

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

March 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 26, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Johnson v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1255 (Fla., May 26, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. Florida, 546 U.S. 1064, 126 S. Ct. 802, 163 L. Ed. 2d 632, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 9093 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Johnson v. McDonough, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23048 (S.D. Fla., Mar. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Ronald C. Dresnick, Judge - Case No. F89-12383B and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Johnson v. State, 696 So. 2d 317, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 607 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of two murders, appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) which denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant's convictions and sentences of death had been affirmed on direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted ineffective assistance of counsel claims as well as other claims. The trial court ordered an evidentiary hearing as to whether counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate defendant's mental health. Defendant presented the testimony of a psychologist, his mother, and himself. The State presented the testimony of defendant's trial counsel in both of his murder cases. Thus, his attorney was not ineffective for failing to have defendant evaluated. Nor was his attorney ineffective for failing to discover defendant's sexual orientation as there is no correlation between homosexuality and committing murder. Finally, the attorney presented mitigation evidence. The appellate court held the trial court did not err in its determinations.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying the motion for postconviction relief was affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Later proceeding at Johnson v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 744 (Fla., Apr. 19, 2005)
Rehearing denied by Johnson v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1256 (Fla., May 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Ronald C. Dresnick, Judge - Case No. F89-14998 and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.

The trial court followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The trial court denied defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel, pursuant to the Sixth Amendment, as trial and appellate counsel allegedly committed numerous errors. Parker v. State

Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Parker v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 39 (Fla., Jan. 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Leroy H. Moe, Judge - Case No. 89-8897 CF10A and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) denied a motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 by petitioner, a prisoner. The prisoner appealed the denial and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus challenging his murder conviction and the sentence of death imposed on him.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of murder in relation to a robbery of a restaurant in which a victim was killed. The prisoner argued that the trial court erred in summarily denying his postconviction petition. A defendant was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on any well-pled allegations in a motion for postconviction unless (1) the motion, files, and records in the case conclusively showed that the prisoner was entitled to no relief or (2) the motion or a particular claim was legally insufficient, Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The appellate court held that there was conflicting evidence concerning the bullet issue. There was significant information that was never presented at sentencing which expounded upon both the abuse the prisoner suffered as a child and his mental infirmities. The appellate court held that the prisoner was entitled to an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed solely with respect to the claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel based on counsel's handling of the bullet evidence and counsel's presentation of mitigating evidence at the penalty phase and remanded for an evidentiary hearing on these issues. Otherwise, the order denying postconviction relief was affirmed. Habeas corpus relief was denied.

Amerisure Ins. Co. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. SC04-387


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


897 So. 2d 1287; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 484; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 153



March 17, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. Second District - Case No. 2D02-4757. (Pinellas County). null
Amerisure Ins. Co. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 865 So. 2d 590, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 164 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Approved the lower court decision in Amerisure Insurance Co. v. State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Co., 865 So. 2d 590 (Fla. 2d DCA 2004), the Fifth District Court of Appeal in Dealers Insurance Co. v. Jon Hall Chevrolet Co., 547 So. 2d 325 (Fla. 5th DCA 1989), the First District Court of Appeal in Tucker Transportation Co. v. State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Co., 883 So. 2d 357 (Fla. 1st DCA 2004); and disapproved the Third District Court of Appeal in Florida Farm Bureau Mutual Insurance Co. v. Tropicana Products, Inc., 456 So. 2d 549 (Fla. 3d DCA 1984).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida appellate court found Fla. Stat. ch. 627.7405 (2001) did not violate appellant commercial insurer's federal or state constitution equal protection clause rights where appellee personal injury insurer claimed a right to reimbursement from the commercial insurer after the insured and her children were injured in an accident that was not her fault while she was driving a commercial vehicle. The appellate court then certified a conflict.


OVERVIEW: The insured and her children were injured in an automobile accident while the insured was driving a commercial motor vehicle owned by a construction company and insured by the commercial insurer. The insured was not at fault. Her personal injury insurer paid personal injury protection (PIP) benefits to her. The personal injury insurer then requested reimbursement from the commercial insurer pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 627.7405 (2001), a provision that required insurers of commercial vehicles to reimburse insurers of private vehicles for PIP payments. The commercial insurer refused to pay. The trial court granted summary judgment to the personal injury insurer and found it was entitled to reimbursement under that statute. The appellate court then found that Fla. Stat. ch. 627.7405 (2001) did not violate the commercial insurer's rights under either the federal or state equal protection clauses. A conflict in appellate decisions was certified, and the state supreme court found that the statute did not violate the federal and state equal protection clauses because it was rationally related to the legitimate state objective of regulating insurance rates.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court from which the conflict was certified was approved.

Adaway v. State


No. SC04-239


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


902 So. 2d 746; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 487; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 158



March 17, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Adaway v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1109 (Fla., May 10, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Adaway v. Fla., 126 S. Ct. 436, 163 L. Ed. 2d 331, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7410 (U.S., Oct. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Third District - Case No. 3D02-1907. (Dade County).
Adaway v. State, 864 So. 2d 36, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18113 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence which was affirmed by the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida). The lower appellate court expressly declared valid Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(1) (1999) which mandated life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for persons convicted of capital sexual battery. The sole issue was whether such a sentence for oral union with the vagina of a girl under the age of 12 constituted cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted an 11-year-old girl while she slept in the bedroom she shared with her siblings. Defendant was convicted violating Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(2) (1999), sexual battery on a child under 12, and Fla. Stat. ch. 899.04(5)(b) (1999), lewd or lascivious molestation of a child under 12. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole on the sexual battery charge, which was a mandatory sentence under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(1). Defendant argued the sentence was grossly disproportionate to his crime and therefore violated both U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Fla. Const. art. I, § 17. The supreme court held that for a prison sentence to constitute cruel and unusual punishment solely because of its length, at a minimum the sentence had to be grossly disproportionate to the crime. Defendant failed to demonstrate gross disproportionality. Given the array of potentially lifelong harms associated with sexual abuse of children, the supreme court declined to second-guess the Florida Legislature's judgment that such a crime warranted a lifelong penalty. Thus, defendant's sentence did not violate Fla. Const. art. I, § 17 or U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower appellate court was affirmed.

Orme v. State


Nos. SC02-2625 & SC03-1375


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


896 So. 2d 725; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 360; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 127



February 24, 2005, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Judy Pittman, Judge - Case No. 92-442CF and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Orme v. State, 677 So. 2d 258, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 732 (Fla., May 2, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Writ of habeas corpus denied. Post-conviction proceedings reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida), which denied his motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 for postconviction relief, in which defendant challenged his convictions for premeditated or felony murder, robbery, and sexual battery, and he challenged his sentence of death. Defendant also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was linked to a brutal beating death of a woman. His defense to murder and rape charges was that he was drunk and on drugs when the incident happened, and that he could not form the requisite intent. He was convicted for the crimes and was sentenced to death after a penalty proceeding. After exhausting direct appeals, defendant moved for post-conviction relief on 25 grounds. The motion was denied and he appealed, raising three challenges along with a petition for habeas corpus relief. However, the ineffectiveness did not affect the reliability of the guilt phase proceeding. The court had rejected defendant's constitutional challenge in prior cases and he had no right to be present at the jury qualifications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying postconviction relief on defendant's sentence of death and remanded for a new penalty phase proceeding. The court affirmed all other aspects of the order. The court also denied defendant's petition for habeas corpus relief.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] No. SC03-1321 Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Second District - Case No. 2D02-460. (Pasco County).

No. SC03-2103 An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Third District - Case No. 3D02-1839. (Miami-Dade County).
Milks v. State, 848 So. 2d 1167, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 6220 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)

DISPOSITION: Decision of Second District in Milks approved, decision of Third District in Espindola reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, in appeals of two separate cases, challenged the constitutionality of the Florida Sexual Predators Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (2003). In one case, the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) declared the Act constitutional, rejecting procedural-due-process and separation-of-powers challenges. In the other case, the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) declared the Act unconstitutional on procedural-due-process grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the Florida Sexual Predators Act violated their rights to procedural due process, under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Fla. Const. art. I, § 9. The Supreme Court of Florida found that the Act did not violate procedural due process or separation of powers and, as against the challenges, was constitutional. The court declined to consider the substantive-due-process and equal-protection challenges briefed by the parties but not addressed by the courts below.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Second District was approved, and the judgment of the Third District was reversed.

Fitzpatrick v. State


No. SC01-2759


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


900 So. 2d 495; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 88; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 269



January 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 21, 2005. As Revised April 21, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Fitzpatrick v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 729 (Fla., Apr. 21, 2005)
Post-conviction relief granted at State v. Fitzpatrick, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 1312 (Fla., June 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County,

Maynard F. Swanson, Jr., Judge - Case No. 97-482 CFAES.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sexual battery and which imposed a sentence of death for first-degree murder and 30 years' imprisonment for sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: The victim was found nude and bleeding on the side of the road with stab injuries and later died. Affirming defendant's convictions and death sentence but vacating the sentence for sexual battery, the court held, inter alia, that (1) the State presented substantial evidence to establish identity and to show that the killing occurred during a sexual battery; (2) defendant's statements made to police after he requested assistance of counsel were properly admitted because defendant initiated the discussions; (3) even if defendant's consent to the taking of his blood was involuntary, the police had probable cause to arrest defendant and the blood sample would have been inevitably obtained; (4) the victim's statements made at the hospital were not hearsay because they were inconsistent with statements she made at the crime scene; (5) an officer's testimony that defendant stated that he thought he needed an attorney was isolated and there was no reasonable possibility that the testimony affected the jury verdict; but (6) the record demonstrates that no scoresheet was prepared for the noncapital offense of sexual battery, contrary to the provisions of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.701(d)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death, but it vacated the sentence for the noncapital offense of sexual battery and remanded for resentencing after preparation of a guidelines scoresheet and its consideration by the trial judge.

 

541 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Arbelaez v. State


No. SC02-2284, No. SC03-1718


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


898 So. 2d 25; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 89; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 65



January 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 18, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Arbelaez v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 603 (Fla., Mar. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County,

Leslie Rothenberg, Judge - Case No. 88-5546

And an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Arbelaez v. State, 626 So. 2d 169, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1430 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 after an evidentiary hearing, and denied supplemental claims, a motion to exclude the testimony of a death row mental health counselor, and a motion to disqualify the trial judge who presided over the matter on remand. The inmate appealed and also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged the ineffective assistance of his trial counsel during the penalty phase. The trial court first found that counsel adequately investigated the inmate's history of epilepsy. But, while counsel did not conduct a reasonable investigation of the inmate's mental health status, the inmate failed to show prejudice. Where the strongest evidence of mitigation was that the inmate was of low intelligence, such evidence did not affect the verdict, as the inmate's videotaped confession recounted the facts of the crime in detail, making it clear that the crime was both premeditated and deliberate. Second, counsel was not ineffective for failing to call the inmate's family members, where the inmate did not desire such. Third, the inmate failed to show sufficient evidence to warrant disqualification of the trial judge, or to justify overturning an order denying his motion to exclude an inmate counselor's testimony. Also, his supplemental claims lacked merit. Finally, the inmate was not entitled to habeas relief, as photographs of the victim were admissible, and counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise frivolous claims or for raising issues that were procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the inmate postconviction relief was affirmed, and his petition for habeas corpus was denied.

Kokal v. State


No. SC01-882


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


901 So. 2d 766; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 6; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 21



January 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised April 28, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Kokal v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 757 (Fla., Apr. 28, 2005)
Rehearing denied by Kokal v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1063 (Fla., Apr. 28, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Kokal v. Fla., 126 S. Ct. 560, 163 L. Ed. 2d 471, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7959 (U.S., Oct. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County,

Hugh A. Carithers, Jr., Judge - Case No. 83-8975 CF.
Kokal v. Dugger, 718 So. 2d 138, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1315 (Fla., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which denied his successive motion for postconviction relief from his death penalty judgment under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder of a robbery victim and sentenced to death. The court upheld his conviction and sentence. Defendant filed an unsuccessful post-conviction motion. He later filed a pro se successive postconviction motion claiming actual innocence based upon newly discovered evidence, which consisted of an affidavit from an inmate who claimed that defendant's co-defendant had shared a jail cell with him and admitted that he was the one who had actually shot the victim. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court found that the inmate's testimony would not have been admissible at trial, because it constituted inadmissible hearsay and the alleged confession was not admissible pursuant to the statement against interest exception to the hearsay rule because defendant had failed to demonstrate that the co-defendant was unavailable to testify. Lastly, the court found that the trial court properly determined that acquittal on retrial in light of all the other evidence, was virtually inconceivable, noting that defendant had bloodstains consistent with the victim's blood type on his shoes, and his fingerprints were on the murder weapon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both of the trial court's orders, and held that defendant's due process claim was procedurally barred.

 

543 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Winkles v. State


No. SC03-935


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


894 So. 2d 842; 2005 Fla. LEXIS 8; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 27



January 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Winkles v. Florida, 546 U.S. 829, 126 S. Ct. 46, 163 L. Ed. 2d 78, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6145 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Winkles v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1414 (Fla., Sept. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County,

Richard A. Luce, Judge - Case No. CRC99-5593CFANO-M.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed appellant's convictions and sentences.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of first-degree murder and waived his right to a jury for the penalty phase of the trial. The Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) sentenced defendant to death on both counts. Defendant appealed, challenging the constitutionality of his convictions and death sentences.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that under Apprendi and Ring, a jury had to find the aggravating circumstances required to impose the death penalty. The state supreme court concluded that in cases that included a prior violent felony conviction as an aggravating circumstance, it had repeatedly rejected the argument that Apprendi and Ring required the jury, rather than the judge, to find the remaining aggravators. Defendant also argued that Florida's death penalty statute was unconstitutional because it did not require that aggravating circumstances be charged in the indictment. Again, the state supreme court had regularly rejected such claims where one of the aggravators was a prior violent felony conviction. Because defendant knowingly and voluntarily entered his plea, the trial court properly accepted it. The trial court thoroughly informed defendant about the rights he was waiving and defendant indicated both verbally and in writing that he understood. The trial court explained that defendant was entitled to a jury in both phases of the trial and that if he elected to waive his right to a jury, the judge alone would determine his sentence.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed defendant's convictions of first-degree murder and the sentences of death on both murder charges.

 

544 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Exposito v. State


No. SC03-1248


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


891 So. 2d 525; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2407; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 9



December 23, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict Third District - Case No. 3D02-2467 (Miami-Dade County).
State v. Exposito, 854 So. 2d 674, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9413 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Quashed to extent inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted of trafficking in cannabis, the trial court, pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.620, adjudged him guilty of the lesser-included offense of possession with intent to sell. The State appealed. The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) held that Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07(1) (2004) afforded it the right to hear the State's appeal and reinstated defendant's conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court reduced the charges under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.620 because it found the amendment to the trafficking statute unconstitutional. The court of appeals reversed, finding that the statute was constitutional. It also held that Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07 authorized a State appeal from a posttrial order reducing a charge pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.620 because an order reducing a charge set forth in the information or indictment to some lesser-included charge was, despite its label, an "order dismissing the charge in the information." Thus, it was appealable under Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07(1)(a). The supreme court disagreed. Statutes affording the State the right to appeal in criminal cases had to be construed narrowly. The State's right to appeal a posttrial order reducing the charge had to be the product of express legislative authorization, not judicial extension of provisions authorizing State appeals in other circumstances; ch. 927.01(1) did not expressly authorize a State to appeal an order reducing the charge under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.620.


OUTCOME: The supreme court quashed the court of appeal's decision to the extent it was inconsistent with the supreme court's opinion.

Monlyn v. State


Nos. SC02-1729 & SC03-1757


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


894 So. 2d 832; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2170; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 741



December 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 11, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Monlyn v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 302 (Fla., Feb. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Madison County, E. Vernon Douglas, Judge - Case No. 92-147-CF and an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Monlyn v. State, 705 So. 2d 1, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1520 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Post-conviction relief denied; habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Madison County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, in which defendant challenged his convictions for first-degree murder, armed robbery, and armed kidnapping, and his sentence of death. Defendant also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: After escaping from prison, defendant severely beat a man, took his wallet, and fled in his truck. He was convicted for several crimes, including murder, and he was sentenced to death. He appealed the denial of his motion for postconviction relief, alleging that his counsel was ineffective and that the trial court erred by failing to rule on two of his claims. In a habeas petition, he argued that Florida's death penalty scheme was unconstitutional and that a decision requiring a jury to find the facts leading to death penalty aggravation applied retroactively to his case. The court found that counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the admission of habit testimony since there was no prejudice. Also, defendant did not show that counsel failed to advise him of his right to testify and no prejudice existed since his proposed testimony did not show remorse. The two issues that the trial court did not rule on were procedurally barred. Finally, the court rejected defendant's arguments for habeas relief since it had rejected them in prior decisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief. The court denied defendant's habeas petition.

Dessaure v. State


No. SC02-286


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


891 So. 2d 455; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2171; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 744



December 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Post-conviction relief denied at Dessaure v. State, 55 So. 3d 478, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1638 (Fla., 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Dessaure v. Sec'y of Dep't of Corr., 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 143387 (M.D. Fla., Dec. 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Brandt C. Downey, Judge - Case No. CRC99-15522-CFANO.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of first-degree murder and sentence of death from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the trial court abused its discretion when it denied his motion for mistrial based on the prosecutor's opening statement. The prosecutor remarked that defendant said only two people knew what happened in the victim's apartment, so she had to reconstruct what happened with scientific and other evidence. The supreme court found this statement was a fair characterization of the evidence presented, and the jury was instructed numerous times during voir dire and the trial that the burden of proof rested solely on the State. The trial court also did not abuse its discretion when it barred evidence concerning marijuana cigarettes in the victim's apartment and the victim's boyfriend's marijuana use, as defendant failed to adequately connect either piece of evidence to a material fact in issue. Because defense witnesses had a potential motive to lie at trial, the trial court did not err when it allowed the State to impeach the witnesses with evidence that they were serving mandatory life sentences. Defendant never moved the trial court to withdraw his waiver of a penalty phase jury, so the claim could not be raised on direct appeal. The death sentence was proportionate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first-degree murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed.

Cole v. State


No. SC03-2204


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


895 So. 2d 398; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2117; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 712



November 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 24, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Cole v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 388 (Fla., Feb. 24, 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Cole v. Crosby, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25952 (M.D. Fla., May 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, William T. Swigert, Judge - Case No. 94-498-CF.
Cole v. State, 701 So. 2d 845, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1436 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder, two counts of kidnapping with a weapon, two counts of robbery with a weapon, and two counts of sexual battery; he was sentenced to death. His sentence and convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. He filed a motion for postconviction DNA testing under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.853, which the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Florida, denied. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, aided by an accomplice, kidnapped and physically assaulted a woman and her brother, robbed them, killed the brother by slitting his throat and hitting him in the head, and sexually assaulted the woman. The accomplice pled nolo contendere to murder and other charges and was sentenced to life imprisonment. The woman had testified that only the inmate had raped her. The inmate wanted to test the woman's clothing and evidence in the sexual assault kit, along with his and the accomplice's blood, for DNA. He claimed that if DNA testing showed that the accomplice had also raped the woman, this would call into question the credibility of her testimony linking him to the premeditated murder of her brother. The appellate court noted that Rule 3.853 was not intended to be a fishing expedition. Under Rule 3.853, the inmate had to show a reasonable probability that DNA testing would exonerate him or mitigate his sentence. Under these facts, he failed to meet that burden, and his motion was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's motion was affirmed.

State v. Duncan


Nos. SC02-636 & SC03-145


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


894 So. 2d 817; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2121; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 719



November 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 11, 2005.
Rehearing denied by State v. Duncan, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 307 (Fla., Feb. 11, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Florida v. Duncan, 126 S. Ct. 397, 163 L. Ed. 2d 275, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7184 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and a Cross Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Daniel P. Dawson, Judge - Case No. 90-13778- CR and an Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Duncan v. State, 619 So. 2d 279, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 709 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Court affirmed the trial court's grant of a new penalty phase and denial of the remainder of the claims raised in Duncan's motion for postconviction relief, and further denied Duncan's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Florida appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) granting in part and denying in part petitioner's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Petitioner cross-appealed and petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was found guilty of murder and was sentenced to death. The trial court held petitioner was entitled to a new penalty phase proceeding on petitioner's claim that counsel was ineffective for failing to introduce available mental health mitigation that could have led the jury to recommend a life sentence. In the instant action, the supreme court found the trial court did not improperly shift the burden to the State to prove counsel was effective. A review of the court's order demonstrated that the trial court followed the proper procedure in determining that a new penalty phase was warranted. Petitioner satisfied the requirements of Strickland, and the record was devoid of any justification for counsel's failure to present the available evidence. As to petitioner's habeas claim, it was within the trial court's discretion to allow the use of a dummy as a demonstrative aid during one eyewitness's testimony, and the judge did not abuse his discretion in allowing the use of the demonstrative aid. The death penalty was constitutionally imposed upon petitioner in light of the fact that the trial court properly applied the prior violent felony aggravating factor.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of a new penalty phase and denial of the remainder of the claims raised in petitioner's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed, and his petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

R.J.L. v. State


No. SC02-1493


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


887 So. 2d 1268; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2100; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 673



November 18, 2004, Decided

DISPOSITION: Conflict between districts resolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought an application for review of a decision by the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which affirmed a decision holding that respondent State, though the Florida Department of Law Enforcement (FDLE), properly denied petitioner a certificate of eligibility (COE) for expungement of his criminal history record.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner applied for a COE to have his criminal history record expunged. The FDLE denied his application and petitioner filed a petition in circuit court for expungement of all of his criminal history record information in light of his being pardoned by the governor and for a writ to require the FDLE to issue a COE. The circuit court ruled for the State, determining that the issuance of a pardon did not remove the historical fact that petitioner was convicted of kidnapping without ransom. Therefore, the FDLE properly denied the COE. The lower appellate court affirmed that decision. On review of those decisions, the court found that the lower appellate court correctly held that an individual who received a gubernatorial pardon was not entitled to a COE for records expunction pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0585(2) (2000) because a pardon did not have the effect of eliminating guilt or the fact of conviction. The court approved of the decisions of the lower appellate court in line with that reasoning and disapproved other lower appellate court holdings that conflicted with that reasoning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying petitioner's request for a certificate of eligibility to expunge his criminal record.

State v. J.P.


Nos. SC02-2288 & SC02-2452


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2004 Fla. LEXIS 2101; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 331



November 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Modified by State v. J.P., 907 So. 2d 1101, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2529 (Fla., Nov. 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case Nos. 2D97-1736 and 2D98-3778. (Hillsborough and Pinellas Counties).
State v. T.M., 832 So. 2d 118, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 11700 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2002)
J.P. v. State, 832 So. 2d 110, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 11699 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: First decision approved. Second decision approved in part and disapproved in part. Certified question answered in negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida Second District Court of Appeal determined that two juvenile curfew ordinances enacted by the city councils of Tampa and Pinellas Park were unconstitutional after the matters had been remanded with instructions to apply the strict scrutiny standard. The lower appellate court certified questions of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: The City of Tampa and the City of Pinellas Park enacted similar juvenile curfew ordinances. In reviewing the ordinances, the lower appellate court initially applied intermediate or heightened scrutiny and ruled that both ordinances were constitutional. After remand, the lower appellate court concluded that, while the cities may have had a compelling governmental interest in controlling the whereabouts of juveniles during late night hours, the ordinances were not narrowly tailored to accomplish that goal by the least intrusive means available. The Florida Supreme Court concluded that the ordinances at issue did not implicate the juveniles' rights to free speech and assembly as those activities were specifically exempted from their ambit. It likewise concluded that the findings stated in the ordinances satisfied the compelling interest prong of the strict scrutiny test. It agreed with the lower appellate court that the ordinances were not "narrowly tailored" because the statistical data failed to establish the necessary nexus between the governmental interest and the classification created by the ordinances.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower appellate court were affirmed.

 

553 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. J.P.


Nos. SC02-2288 & SC02-2452


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


907 So. 2d 1101; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2529



November 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Released for Publication May 5, 2005. Rehearing denied by State v. J.P., 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1003 (Fla., May 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case Nos. 2D97-1736 and 2D98-3778 (Hillsborough and Pinellas Counties).
State v. J.P., 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2101 (Fla., Nov. 18, 2004)
State v. T.M., 832 So. 2d 118, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 11700 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2002)
J.P. v. State, 832 So. 2d 110, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 11699 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) applied a strict scrutiny standard and found that juvenile curfew ordinances enacted by the city councils of Tampa and Pinellas Park were unconstitutional. That appellate court then certified questions of great public importance to the state supreme court that asked whether those ordinances, in cases that were consolidated from each of the two cities, were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The cities of Tampa and Pinellas Park enacted similar juvenile curfew ordinances. Respondent first juvenile was cited for violating the Tampa ordinance, while respondent second, third, and fourth juveniles were cited for violating the Pinellas Park ordinance. The State filed petitions for delinquency against the juveniles. The juveniles all moved to dismiss and argued the ordinances were unconstitutional. The respective trial courts came to different conclusions; eventually, the appellate court applied a strict scrutiny standard of review to the juveniles' cases. It then concluded that the juvenile curfew ordinances were unconstitutional. It found that the Tampa ordinance criminalized otherwise innocent conduct by a minor who had parental permission to be at a specified location. It also found the Pinellas Park ordinance was similar but even broader in its application. On further review, the state supreme court found that the ordinances were not "narrowly tailored" because their broad coverage included otherwise innocent and legal conduct by minors, even where they had the permission of their parents, and because the ordinances imposed criminal penalties for curfew violations.


OUTCOME: The certified questions were answered in the negative, and the appellate court's decisions in the two cases were approved to the extent they were consistent with the state supreme court's opinion.

State v. Baez


No. SC02-1173


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


894 So. 2d 115; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1989; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 663



November 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 5, 2005.
Rehearing denied by State v. Baez, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 3 (Fla., Jan. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict. Fourth District - Case No. 4D01-100. (Broward County).
Baez v. State, 814 So. 2d 1149, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 4621 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State applied for review of a decision by the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed defendant's conviction by a jury for possession of cocaine and his sentence of five and a half months in jail.


OVERVIEW: An officer found defendant slumped over the wheel of a van after responding to a call of a vehicle parked at night in a normally abandoned area. After waking defendant, who immediately stepped out of the van, the officer requested identification. Defendant produced a driver's license, which the officer took to perform a warrants check. Defendant was arrested on an outstanding warrant. After defendant was transferred to another police vehicle, cocaine was found in the officer's cruiser at the spot where defendant was seated. Defendant moved to suppress that evidence, arguing the retention of his license after identification constituted an unlawful detention. The motion was denied and defendant was convicted. On appeal, the lower appellate court found that the consensual element of the encounter ended after the officer inspected the license and that the further detention violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights. The State appealed. The supreme court found that, under the totality of the circumstances, the officer had a reasonable basis to investigate defendant. The computer check was justified because the officer had not eliminated all criminal suspicion of defendant's behavior.


OUTCOME: The supreme court quashed the appellate court's decision, held that defendant was not unreasonably detained when an officer ran a warrants check on defendant's driver's license, and remanded for further proceedings.
