Busby v. State


No. SC02-1364


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


894 So. 2d 88; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1925; 30 Fla. L. Weekly S 95



November 4, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 3, 2005. As Corrected February 3, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Busby v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 153 (Fla., Feb. 3, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Florida v. Busby, 125 S. Ct. 2976, 162 L. Ed. 2d 906, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5189 (U.S., June 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Columbia County, E. Vernon Douglas, Judge - Case No. 00-897CF.



DISPOSITION: Busby's conviction reversed, sentence vacated, case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Columbia County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and which sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for murdering a fellow inmate and was sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant raised 13 issues, including reversible error when his challenge for cause was refused for a juror who was a former death row inmate guard. He argued that the juror acknowledged a bias against death row inmates and admitted a willingness to execute accused persons, thus raising a reasonable doubt as to his impartiality and justifying a challenge for cause under Fla. Stat. ch. 913.03(10) (2003). The court agreed, noting that the juror stated that if an accused person was convicted of prior crimes, he might automatically vote for the death penalty. The juror also stated that life imprisonment was not a severe enough punishment for a person convicted of premeditated murder and that since the homicide occurred inside a prison, his ability to serve impartially might be compromised. Defendant showed prejudice, justifying reversal, as he exhausted his peremptory challenges, he would have otherwise removed the objectionable juror with a peremptory challenge, and he was denied additional peremptory challenges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for murder, vacated the sentence of death, and remanded for a new trial.

AFL-CIO v. Hood


No. SC04-1921


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


885 So. 2d 373; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1815; 57 A.L.R.6th 797; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 597



October 18, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certified Judgments of Trial Courts in and for Leon County - L. Ralph Smith, Judge, Case No. 2004-CA-2104 - An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D04-4304.
AFL-CIO v. Hood, 884 So. 2d 21, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1858 (Fla., Oct. 5, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida District Court of Appeal, First District, certified an appeal from trial court judgments which denied declaratory and injunctive relief to plaintiffs, registered voters and labor organizations, in their challenge to the constitutionality of the precinct-specific provision of Fla. Stat. ch. 101.048 (2004).


OVERVIEW: Registered voters and labor organizations filed a petition for a writ of mandamus, alleging that the precinct-specific requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 101.048 (2004) were violative of the Florida Constitution. The matter was transferred and dismissed. Thereafter, the trial court denied relief on an amended complaint which sought declaratory and injunctive relief. On appeal, the matter was certified for review, based on a statement that it involved a matter of great public importance. Plaintiffs claimed that the challenged provision operated as an unnecessary restriction on the right to vote in violation of Fla. Const. art. VI, § 1, and that it imposed an additional qualification on the right of suffrage in violation of Fla. Const. art. VI, § 2. The court noted that the traditional precinct-specific provision that applied to all voters was codified in Fla. Stat. ch. 101.045 (2004). There was no showing how that was distinguishable from the challenged provision, nor that Fla. Stat. ch. 101.048 imposed an unreasonable or unnecessary restraint on the elective process. The court upheld the statute's constitutionality against the challenge by plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling.

Phillips v. State

DISPOSITION: We deny Phillips's petition for habeas corpus and affirm the trial court's summary denial of postconviction relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the order from the Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which denied his amended motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In 1983, defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for the murder of a parole supervisor. The court affirmed the denial of postconviction relief and denied the petition for habeas corpus. P. 3.211(e), to the admissibility of an expert's testimony at defendant's resentencing, because the expert did not state that he had interviewed defendant for a determination of competency, instead, he testified that he examined defendant to evaluate his general intelligence and degree of learning.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's postconviction motion and denied the petition for habeas corpus.

 

559 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Banks v. State


No. SC01-2733


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


887 So. 2d 1191; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1810; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 579



October 14, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D01-3190 (Okaloosa County).
Banks v. State, 801 So. 2d 153, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 16642 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Decision of District Court of Appeal approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Florida District Court of Appeal, First District, which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant sought (1) resentencing to 80.1 months, the low end of the earlier sentencing guidelines; (2) to withdraw his plea in favor of a new plea agreement; or (3) to allow the State to withdraw from the original plea agreement and proceed to trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a negotiated plea of nolo contendere and an agreed sentence based on his belief that the later sentencing guidelines were valid. He claimed that he entered into a plea at the top of the earlier guidelines in order to avoid a sentence under the harsher later guidelines and that he would not have entered into the plea had he known those guidelines were invalid. The trial court summarily denied defendant's motion after it noted that defendant negotiated for a sentence of imprisonment for a term of years and not for a "minimum range" guidelines sentence. The supreme court concluded that defendant's sentence was valid under the earlier sentencing guidelines and approved the lower appellate court's decision to affirm the trial court's order denying postconviction relief. After defendant was sentenced, the later guidelines were invalidated. Thus, they could not have legally superseded the earlier guidelines. Therefore, the earlier guidelines were still in effect and defendant's sentence was legal under those sentencing guidelines, and defendant was not adversely affected by reliance on the later guidelines.


OUTCOME: The lower appellate court's decision was approved.

Franklin v. State


No. SC03-413


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


887 So. 2d 1063; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1700; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 538



September 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 7, 2004. As Corrected November 18, 2004. Released for Publication November 19, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Franklin v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2239 (Fla., Nov. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case No. 3D02-957 (Dade County).
State v. Franklin, 836 So. 2d 1112, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 1463 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Dade County Circuit Court (Florida) convicted defendant of armed robbery and resisting arrest, due to acts that occurred after the effective date of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, and sentenced him as an habitual offender under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 (1999), which was amended by 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, § 3. The Third District Court of Appeal certified a conflict with a case decided while an appeal was pending. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: At issue in the instant action was the constitutionality of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 known as the "Three-Strike Violent Felony Offender Act" (Act). The specific constitutional question presented was whether the provisions of the Act embraced but one subject and matter properly connected therewith as mandated by Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. The instant court first determined that defendant had standing to assert a single-subject challenge, notwithstanding the fact that he was not directly affected by either §§ 11 or 13 of the Act. Second, the court held that there was a natural or logical and thus proper connection between the requirements of § 11 that sentences of non-citizen offenders be provided to the Immigration and Naturalization Service (INS). This conclusion was buttressed by the fact that in requiring the transmission of sentences to the INS, § 11 also promoted the Act's purpose of protecting the public from persons sentenced as serious or repeat violent offenders. Third, § 13 made effective one of the purposes included within the subject--imposing harsher sentences on violent offenders. Thus, the provisions at issue did not violate the single-subject rule.


OUTCOME: The sentence was upheld as non-violative of the single-subject rule.

Bush v. Schiavo


No. SC04-925


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


885 So. 2d 321; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1539; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 515



September 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Released for Publication October 21, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Bush v. Schiavo, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1918 (Fla., Oct. 21, 2004)
Writ denied by, Sub nomine at Schindler v. Schiavo, 916 So. 2d 5, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17889 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Nov. 24, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bush v. Schiavo, 543 U.S. 1121, 160 L. Ed. 2d 1069, 125 S. Ct. 1086, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 810 (U.S., 2005)
Stay denied by, Sub nomine at Schindler v. Schiavo (In re Schiavo), 916 So. 2d 814, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3574 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Mar. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified Judgments of Trial Courts in and for Pinellas County - W. Douglas Baird, Judge, Case No. 03-8212-CI-20 - An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, Second District, Case No. 2D04-2045.
Bush v. Schiavo, 871 So. 2d 1012, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6573 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Pinellas County (Florida) held that 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 418, which prompted appellant governor to issue an executive order, was unconstitutional as a violation of the separation of powers doctrine, a person's right to privacy, and as retroactive legislation. The Second District Court of Appeal certified the case as one of great public importance requiring immediate resolution.


OVERVIEW: The governor's executive order effectively reversed a properly rendered final judgment and amounted to an unconstitutional encroachment on the power reserved for the judiciary. Further, it inappropriately delegated legislative power to the governor. In all, 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 418 contained no guidelines or standards to limit the governor from exercising completely unrestricted discretion in applying the law. Further, the legislature failed to provide any criteria for lifting the stay. This absolute, unfettered discretion to decide whether to issue and then when to lift a stay made the governor's decision virtually unreviewable. Second, the legislation did not provide an additional layer of due process protection to those who were unable to communicate their wishes regarding end-of-life decisions. The law did not even require the governor to consider a patient's wishes, but instead allowed a unilateral decision by the governor to stay the withholding of life-prolonging procedures without any procedural process to the patient. Finally, the legislature's grant of authority to issue the stay under 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 418 was not a valid exercise of the state's parens patriae power.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.


 

564 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Zingale v. Powell


No. SC03-1270


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


885 So. 2d 277; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1518



September 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 21, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Zingale v. Powell, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1920 (Fla., Oct. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction. Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-3754 (Broward County).
Powell v. Markham, 847 So. 2d 1105, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8984 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Quash the decision of the Fourth District and remand for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Executive Director of the Florida Department of Revenue, sought review of an order from the Florida Fourth District Court of Appeal, which held that the homestead exemption cap in Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4(c) applied to the increase in the assessed value of respondent homeowners' house from 2000 to 2001.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners did not apply for a homestead exemption until September 2001, after an appraiser notified them of an increase in their property taxes. In addition to filing for an exemption, they also sought to have the "Save Our Homes" cap in Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4(c) applied to limit the increase in their assessment from 2000 to 2001. Their application was approved for 2001, but the appraiser did not reduce the 2001 assessment. The homeowners filed suit to challenge the county's refusal to apply the cap to the increase in the assessed value of their home from 2000 to 2001. The lower court held that the cap applied to homeowners who qualified for the exemption, not just to those who applied for it. On appeal, the court held that the grant of an exemption was necessary for a homeowner to obtain the baseline assessment for the cap. Hence, the homeowners were precluded from benefitting from the cap for the increase in their property taxes from 2000 to 2001. Their successful application for the exemption in 2001 constituted an establishment of the homestead, which triggered the baseline assessment for the cap. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 193.155 (2001), their baseline year was 2001.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the order of the lower court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

565 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Warner v. City of Boca Raton


No. SC01-2206


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


887 So. 2d 1023; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1449; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 454



September 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Warner v. City of Boca Raton, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2110 (Fla., Nov. 16, 2004)Released for Publication November 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified Question of Law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit - Case No. 99-13730.
Warner v. City of Boca Raton, 267 F.3d 1223, 2001 U.S. App. LEXIS 21253 (11th Cir. Fla., 2001)



DISPOSITION: We answer the first certified question concerning Florida Religious Freedom Restoration Act in the affirmative and the second question, does the City of Boca Raton Ordinance violate the Florida Religious Freedom Restoration Act answer in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following certification of two questions by the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit, the appellate court considered whether restrictions on the manner in which religious decorations could be displayed on grave sites were constitutional or whether the restrictions merely inconvenienced the practices of plaintiffs, the owners and family members of those interred, of marking graves and decorating them with religious symbols.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city maintained a 21.5-acre cemetery for its residents. The city passed a regulation prohibiting vertical grave markers, memorials, monuments, and structures on cemetery plots. The regulation allowed individuals to place stone or bronze markers on plots provided that they were level with the ground surface. The owners argued that the imposition of such restrictions violated their right to free exercise of religion because they could not then place religious symbols on the vertical grave markers. However, the city's regulations did not prohibit the owners from marking graves and decorating them with religious symbols. Rather, the regulations permitted only horizontal grave markers. Those markers could have been engraved with any type of religious symbol. Moreover, out of consideration for mourners, vertical grave decorations were permitted for 60 days after the date of burial and for a few days around certain holidays. Accordingly, the prohibition on vertical grave decorations did not substantially burden the owners' exercise of religion within the meaning of the Florida Religious Freedom Restoration Act (FRFRA), 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 412, §§ 1-6, 3297-98.


OUTCOME: The restrictions did not violate the free exercise of religion.

Writ of habeas corpus denied Pietri v. Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 32270 (S.D. Fla., Apr. 18, 2008)
Decision reached on appeal by Pietri v. State, 94 So. 3d 501, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 813 (Fla., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Marvin U. Mounts, Jr., Judge - Case No. 88-11366CF A02, An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida) that denied his motion for post conviction relief, pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. On appeal, defendant asserted 10 claims of error. Defendant also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in which he raised four issues.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his trial counsel were ineffective for failing to investigate and present a voluntary intoxication defense, and that if they had performed effectively, it could have been demonstrated that due to defendant's intoxication, he lacked the requisite specific intent to commit the murder. Further, as to the claim that counsel was ineffective for not challenging a juror, at the conclusion of additional questioning and upon being provided appropriate criteria, the juror affirmed that he could follow the law and would not automatically vote for death simply upon the existence of a verdict of guilt. Finally, although counsel was admittedly not focused on the penalty phase from the outset or in the months prior to the start of the guilt phase trial, counsel began attempts to secure a mental health expert well before the penalty phase began.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and defendant's petition for habeas corpus was denied.

Dillbeck v. State


Nos. SC02-2044 & SC03-1123


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


882 So. 2d 969; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1366; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 437



August 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Post-conviction relief denied at Dillbeck v. State, 964 So. 2d 95, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 845 (Fla., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County, F.E. Steinmeyer, Judge - Case No. 90-2795-AF, An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Dillbeck v. State, 643 So. 2d 1027, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 569 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, remanded; writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) that denied his motion for post conviction relief, pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant also filed a petition for habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In his amended motion, defendant raised several claims of ineffective assistance of counsel, some falling under the ineffectiveness per se, presumed prejudice standard, and some falling under the traditional, two-pronged standard of Strickland. However, all of the claims defendant raised had to be analyzed under the two-pronged test of Strickland. As to defendant's claim that his counsel was ineffective per se for conceding that he was guilty of first-degree murder without his consent, during voir dire and at trial, counsel repeatedly conceded that defendant was guilty of felony murder. In his opening statement, counsel conceded defendant had killed the victim, and he told the jury that the two issues for them to decide were whether the killing had been premeditated and whether defendant should have been sentenced to life imprisonment or death. However, in defendant's own trial testimony, which mirrored counsel's strategy of conceding guilt to felony murder but contesting a finding of premeditation, defendant himself admitted at trial that he was guilty of felony murder, but he argued that the killing was not done with premeditation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the denial of relief on defendant's claim that his counsel was ineffective per se for conceding his guilt to felony murder. All other claims were remanded for findings of fact and conclusions of law.

569 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Gibson v. Fla. Dep't of Corr.


No. SC02-2362


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2004 Fla. LEXIS 983; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 356



July 8, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing granted by Gibson v. Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1832 (Fla., Oct. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D02-0118. (Leon County).
Gibson v. Fla. Dep't of Corr., 828 So. 2d 422, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 14577 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, certified question answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a writ of mandamus challenging the authority of respondent, the Department of Corrections (DOC), to forfeit gain time from two served sentences and apply it to petitioner's sentences imposed upon revocation of probation for a third sentence. The trial court denied the petition, and the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) agreed with the trial court. The appellate court certified a question of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted in three different cases arising from crimes committed on different dates, and all the offenses were included in a single guidelines scoresheet. Petitioner served two sentences, but after he began serving his sentence for violation of probation of the third sentence, respondent, the Florida Department of Corrections, declared a forfeiture of previously unforfeited gain time from the served sentences and applied them to the sentences imposed upon revocation of probation. The certified question was whether the forfeiture penalty authorized by the court's interpretation of Fla. Stat. ch. 944.28(1) in Eldridge also applied to the type of sentence imposed in Tripp. The court held that because petitioner was eligible to receive Tripp credit from another offense, the statutory forfeiture penalty contained in ch. 944.28(1) likewise authorized the DOC to forfeit gain time from the completed sentences and add that gain time to the revocation of probation sentence. However, in order to comply with the constitutional prohibition against double jeopardy, the penalty from the expired sentence could not exceed the credit for time actually served from that same sentence.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative but with a caveat.

 

570 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Children & Families v. F.L.


No. SC03-1602


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


880 So. 2d 602; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 984; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 351



July 8, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-4396. (Broward County).
F.L. v. Dep't of Children & Families, 849 So. 2d 1114, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10150 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court terminated the parental rights of appellee mother to her seventh child. On appeal, the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed on grounds that Fla. Stat. ch. 39.806(1)(i) (2002), on which the trial court relied in terminating the mother's parental rights, was unconstitutional. Appellants, the Florida Department of Children and Families (DCF) and the child's guardian ad litem, sought review.


OVERVIEW: The mother's parental rights to her first six children had been terminated due to her neglect and substance abuse. Her rights to the seventh child were terminated after the trial court found that the grounds for termination set forth in ch. 39.806(1)(c) and (i) had been met and that the mother showed a continued unwillingness and inability to parent the child. The district court of appeal reversed, holding that ch. 39.806(1)(i) was facially unconstitutional since it impermissibly shifted the burden to the parent to show that her past conduct did not predict that a current child was at risk. The supreme court held that to terminate parental rights under ch. 39.806(1)(i), the DCF had to prove by clear and convincing evidence that the parent's rights to a prior child were terminated involuntarily, that the current child was at substantial risk of significant harm, and that termination was the least restrictive means of protecting the child from harm. Interpreted in this light, ch. 39.806(1)(i) was constitutional. However, the trial court impermissibly placed the burden on the mother to present evidence that her prior conduct was not a predictor of her conduct with the child at issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court of appeal was reversed and the case was remanded for the trial court to apply the constitutional interpretation of the termination statute to the facts.

 

571 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sochor v. State


Nos. SC01-885 & SC02-1797


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


883 So. 2d 766; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 985; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 363



July 8, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 21, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Sochor v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1703 (Fla., Sept. 21, 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Sochor v. McNeil, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 132027 (S.D. Fla., Sept. 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Paul Blackman, Judge - Case No. 86-15270.
Sochor v. State, 619 So. 2d 285, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 747 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate under sentence of death, appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), that denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. He was convicted of kidnapping and first-degree murder. On appeal of the denial of his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion, petitioner raised 10 claims, and five claims in his habeas petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, among other things, that he was deprived of his Sixth Amendment right to effective assistance of counsel because his lawyer failed to investigate, prepare, and present evidence that would have supported the existence of two statutory mitigating circumstances and several nonstatutory mitigating circumstances. The penalty-phase transcript and the evidentiary-hearing testimony revealed that petitioner's counsel put little time or effort into preparing expressly for the penalty phase. The only witnesses counsel presented at the penalty phase were four members of defendant's family. One of these witnesses, a sister, was not even contacted by counsel. However, petitioner failed to show a reasonable probability that absent counsel's errors, he would not have been sentenced to death. Specifically, the trial court's decision to give the State's expert's testimony greater weight than the testimony of defendant's new experts was supported by competent, substantial evidence because she evaluated petitioner much closer to the time of the murder than the new experts did. At the time of her testimony, the expert was also aware of petitioner's history of alcohol and drug abuse.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was affirmed, and the habeas petition was denied.

Hutchinson v. State


No. SC01-500


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


882 So. 2d 943; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 977; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 337



July 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Hutchinson v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1019 (Fla., July 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal and a Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Okaloosa County. G. Robert Barron, Judge - Case No. 98-1382-CF-001.



DISPOSITION: Affirm the convictions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Okaloosa County (Florida) which convicted him of four counts of first-degree murder with a firearm and imposed three sentences of death after the murder of his live-in-girlfriend and her three children. The State cross-appealed and contended that aggravated child abuse should have been considered separately from the under-the-age-of-12 aggravator.


OVERVIEW: The evidence established that defendant and his girlfriend had argued on the night of the murder and that defendant called 911 and stated that he had shot his family. Affirming the convictions and sentences, the court held, inter alia, that (1) although the girlfriend's statement to a friend that she and defendant were fighting that night should not have been admitted under the excited utterance or spontaneous statement exceptions to the hearsay rule, Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(2) and because there was no evidence that the girlfriend did not engage in reflective thought, the error was harmless in light of the other, overwhelming evidence of guilt; (2) the evidence was sufficient to sustain a conviction of premeditated first-degree murder based on defendant's use of a pump-action shotgun and the time that passed between the argument and the murders; (3) the heinous, atrocious, or cruel factor finding with respect to one of the children was supported by substantial evidence that the child witnessed the murder of his family and saw defendant point the gun at him; and (4) defendant's sentence of death was proportional to sentences in other murder cases involving multiple child-victims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences, and it denied the State's cross appeal.

Kimbrough v. State


Nos. SC02-1158 & SC03-228


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


886 So. 2d 965; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 958; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 323



June 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by, in part Kimbrough v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1466 (Fla., Aug. 31, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Dorothy J. Russell, Judge - Case No. CR92-10868 and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Kimbrough v. State, 700 So. 2d 634, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1305 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 that was filed after he was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death and after the court affirmed the conviction and sentence on direct appeal. Defendant also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions related to the murder and sexual assault of a victim. Affirming the denial of defendant's Rule 3.850 motion and denying his petition for habeas relief, the court held that (1) defendant's Ake claim was properly denied because defense counsel weighed the mitigation evidence that the mental health experts could have presented against the potential risks of having them testify and made a strategic decisions to exclude mental mitigation evidence; (2) the summary denial of several challenged claims without an evidentiary hearing was proper because, inter alia, there was no basis in the record for alleging that trial counsel's decision not to voir dire an expert witness for the State constituted deficient performance and it was clear that counsel's failure to rehabilitate an African-American juror during voir dire would have failed; and (3) Florida's death penalty scheme was not unconstitutional under Apprendi or Ring, especially where the trial court found a violent felony aggravator, and defendant's claim that his Eighth Amendment right would be violated as he may be incompetent at the time of execution was not ripe until the Governor issued a death warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's post-conviction relief motion and denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Bunkley v. State


No. SC01-297


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


882 So. 2d 890; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 858; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 251



May 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Bunkley v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1533 (Fla., Sept. 15, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bunkley v. Fla., 2005 U.S. LEXIS 264 (U.S., Jan. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 2D99-4511 (Sarasota County).
Bunkley v. Florida, 538 U.S. 835, 155 L. Ed. 2d 1046, 123 S. Ct. 2020, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 4273 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand with instructions from the U.S. Supreme Court, the court considered whether, in light of recent case law on what constituted a "dangerous weapon," defendant was convicted without proof of one of the elements of the offense of armed burglary under Fla. Stat. ch. 810.02(2)(b) (1985).


OVERVIEW: In 1986, defendant burglarized a closed, unoccupied restaurant. When he was arrested, he had in his pocket a folding knife with a blade shorter than four inches. Defendant was charged with armed burglary, which required the State to prove that he was armed with a "dangerous weapon." The State described the blade as thick and capable of being locked in an open position, unlike a common pocketknife. The jury concluded that defendant's knife was a dangerous weapon, not a common pocketknife, and convicted him of armed burglary. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment. In a 1997 decision, the court held that a defendant's knife with a three and three-quarter inch blade fell within the common pocketknife exception to the Fla. Stat. ch. 790.001(13) definition of a weapon. Defendant unsuccessfully sought retroactive application of the 1997 decision. The U.S. Supreme Court remanded for reconsideration as to whether defendant's due process rights were violated. The court reaffirmed its decision, finding that defendant was properly convicted of armed robbery as the law stood in 1989, because at the time, whether a subject weapon was dangerous was an issue for a jury to determine.


OUTCOME: The court reaffirmed it decision upholding defendant's conviction.

Henyard v. State


No. SC02-1105, No. SC02-2538


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


883 So. 2d 753; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 859; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 271



May 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 22, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Henyard v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1704 (Fla., Sept. 22, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Henyard v. State, 929 So. 2d 1052, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 716 (Fla., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, Mark J. Hill, Judge - Case No. 93-159-CF-A-MH, and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Henyard v. State, 689 So. 2d 239, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 2145 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 based on claims that counsel was ineffective during the death penalty phase of his trial for armed kidnapping, sexual battery with use of a fire arm, and first-degree murder. Defendant also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his counsel was ineffective during the penalty phase for failing to investigate certain mitigating factors. Affirming the denial, the court held, inter alia, that (1) trial counsel's decision not to present evidence that defendant was abused by his stepmother was a tactical decision; (2) because defendant denied on at least two occasions that he had been sexually abused, it was not clear that trial counsel's failure to investigate the conflicting evidence amounted to ineffective assistance of counsel; and (3) because defendant's suicide attempt could have potentially been viewed as manipulative, trial counsel was not deficient in not introducing this evidence. The court also denied defendant's petition for habeas relief and held that appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the trial court's denial of the public defender's motion to withdraw; that Florida's capital sentencing scheme did not violate the United States and Florida Constitutions; and that because no death warrant for defendant had been signed, his Eight Amendment claim that he was incompetent to be executed was not yet ripe for review under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.811(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's postconviction motion and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.

Patton v. State


No. SC02-423, No. SC02-2158


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


878 So. 2d 368; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 676; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 243



May 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 14, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Patton v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1072 (Fla., July 14, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County, Jerald Bagley, Judge - Case No. 81-19702, and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Patton v. State, 784 So. 2d 380, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1895 (Fla., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Court affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief and denied habeas corpus relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County (Florida) of first-degree murder, armed robbery, grand theft, and violation of probation for the offense of auto theft. The trial court sentenced defendant to death. Later, the trial court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant appealed and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: While a police officer was pursuing defendant on foot, after defendant abandoned a stolen car, defendant hid in an alley and then shot and killed the officer when the officer approached. Defendant argued in his post-conviction motion that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel. On appeal, the court found that defendant was not denied the effective assistance of counsel because: (1) trial counsel made a sound strategy choice to not utilize evidence of voluntary intoxication at the time of the offense; (2) trial counsel made a sound decision to not advance the defense of insanity; and (3) trial counsel was not required to voir dire the jury as to their perception of mental illness as counsel decided not to use an insanity defense. As to the writ for habeas relief, the court found that (1) the capital sentencing scheme was not unconstitutional; (2) defendant failed to show prejudice or error by appellate counsel; and (3) the supreme court did conduct a proportionality review of defendant's death sentence, and a proportionality finding was supported.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying postconviction relief was affirmed, and the petition for habeas relief was denied.

Advisory Opinion to the AG re: Authorizes Miami-Dade & Broward County Voters to Approve Slot Machines in Parimutuel Facilities


No. SC03-857


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


880 So. 2d 522; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 667; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 233



May 13, 2004, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Proponent attorney general requested that the court review a proposed amendment to the Florida Constitution that would permit two Florida counties to hold referenda on whether to permit slot machines in certain pari-mutuel facilities. Animal protection societies challenged the amendment.


OVERVIEW: The court was asked to review a proposed amendment to the Florida Constitution allowing two Florida counties to hold referenda on whether to allow slot machines in certain pari-mutuel facilities. The court found that its review was governed by Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3, which required that the amendment proposed should embrace one subject. The societies argued the proposed amendment violated the single-subject requirement. The court found the tax allocation provision in the proposed amendment did not violate the single-subject requirement. The court also found that voting on the slot machines did not affect the lottery provisions of the Florida Constitution under Fla. Const. art. X, §§ 7, 15, because the slot machines did not constitute a form of lottery. Finally, the ballot title and summary conformed with the legal requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161(1) (2003) in that it properly informed the voters of the chief purpose of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court approved the amendment, the ballot title, and the summary for placement on the ballot.

Douglas v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


878 So. 2d 1246; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 659; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 219



May 6, 2004, Decided

Rehearing denied by Douglas v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1149 (Fla., July 15, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Douglas v. Florida, 543 U.S. 1061, 125 S. Ct. 883, 160 L. Ed. 2d 790, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 611 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Douglas v. State, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 19 (Fla., Jan. 5, 2012)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which convicted him of sexual battery and first-degree murder, and which, after a jury recommended a sentence of death by a vote of 11-1 and after the trial judge found that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances, imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: The evidence established that defendant raped and beat the victim to death. Affirming, the court held that (1) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting autopsy photographs because they were relevant and not so inflammatory as to create undue prejudice; (2) substantial evidence supported the trial court's rejection of several mitigating circumstances because, even though there was testimony that defendant exhibited the mitigating qualities, it was not substantiated either by defendant's actions or by the testimony of those who had firsthand knowledge; (3) it was not an abuse of discretion to give little weight to the mitigating factors relating to defendant's abusive childhood; (4) the trial court's finding that the crime was heinous, atrocious, and cruel was supported by the evidence; (5) the death penalty was proportionate based on evidence that the victim was brutally beaten and remained conscious for at least part of the attack; and (6) Fla. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence of death.

Howell v. State


No. SC03-103


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


877 So. 2d 697; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 661; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 211



May 6, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Howell v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 995 (Fla., June 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Jefferson County, F. E. Steinmeyer, III, Judge - Case No. 92-22-CF.
Howell v. State, 707 So. 2d 674, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 143 (Fla., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of a motion for postconviction relief by the Circuit Court in and for Jefferson County (Florida). Defendant asserted his trial counsel was ineffective in declining to present a defense of intervening cause in the guilt phase and as nonstatutory mitigation in the penalty phase. Defendant also asserted that his sentence of death was unconstitutional. The convictions and death sentence had previously been affirmed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant wanted to kill a witness. He placed a bomb in a microwave oven and paid a driver to deliver the microwave to the witness. The driver thought the microwave contained drugs. Defendant rented a car for the driver to use. The driver, who had no license, was stopped for speeding. A dispatcher contacted defendant by phone to determine whether the rental car had been stolen and to tell him that it would be impounded. Defendant gave no warning regarding the bomb. A trooper was subsequently killed when he opened the microwave. Defendant's attorney rejected an "intervening cause" argument, despite his belief that the trooper violated policy in opening the package, as he thought such argument would have resulted in a certain death recommendation. The appellate court held that death was a clearly foreseeable result of defendant's act. Thus, the alleged policy violation would not have negated any of the elements of first-degree murder. The low probability of success, combined with the potential for alienating the jury by blaming the trooper for his own death, justified trial counsel's strategic decision. Constitutional challenges to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141 had previously been rejected.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief.

Globe v. State


No. SC02-39.


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA.


877 So. 2d 663; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 416; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 345



March 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: REVISED OPINION [**1] As Revised July 1, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Charles Globe v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 974 (Fla., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Columbia County,

E. Vernon Douglas, Judge - Case No. 00-897-CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Columbia County (Florida), convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with a co-defendant, killed another inmate. The state's highest court held that the trial court did not err when it denied defendant's motion to suppress his statements as his right to remain silent was scrupulously honored. Not only did four of the five factors weigh in favor of admissibility, but also, when defendant initially invoked his right to silence, he said only that he did not want to make a statement "at this time," leaving open the prospect of future questioning on the crime. Further, the totality of the circumstances demonstrated that defendant voluntarily waived his rights and was fully aware of the consequences of his decision. Also, there was no showing that the delay in defendant's initial appearance induced the confession. Additionally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's motion in limine, as the language used did not imply a mandatory death sentence. The sentence imposed was the result of a weighing of the aggravating and mitigating factors and it was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

586 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. SC01-2620.


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA.


873 So. 2d 1205; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 418; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 112



March 18, 2004.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Robinson, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 894 (Fla., May 13, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Robinson v. State, 151 So. 3d 1263, 2014 Fla. App. LEXIS 18147 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2014)
Dismissed by, Motion denied by, Request denied by Robinson v. Jones, 2016 Fla. LEXIS 315 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity

Fourth District - Case No. 4D00-253

(Broward County).
Robinson v. State, 804 So. 2d 451, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 15668 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court ruled that, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21(4)(c) (1998), defendant was a "sexual predator" because he had been convicted of kidnapping a minor that was not his child, even though there had been no sexual component to the crime. Defendant appealed; the District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed, declaring invalid the Florida Sexual Predators Act as applied to defendant's circumstances. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his companion stole a car; there was a baby in a car seat in the back seat. They later abandoned the car, with the baby still inside. Because defendant was convicted not only of carjacking, but of kidnapping a child that was not his, under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21(4)(c) (1998), the trial court had no choice but to find him a sexual predator, even though the State conceded that there was no sexual conduct involving the child. The district court of appeal held that the Act was overinclusive as applied to defendant and did not pass the rational relationship test. The supreme court affirmed, but for different reasons. Because of the stigma attached to sexual predator status, the life-long registration requirements, and the attendant adverse employment affects, the designation as a sexual predator was a deprivation of a protected liberty interest, triggering a substantive due process analysis. The supreme court held that as the predicate crimes had no sexual element and there was no sexual motive for them, the designation of defendant as a sexual predator based solely on his conviction for kidnapping a minor who was not his child violated his right to due process of law.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court of appeal was affirmed.

Baker v. State


Nos. SC02-775, SC02-1071 & SC02-1094


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


878 So. 2d 1236; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 314; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 413

PRIOR HISTORY: Three Cases Consolidated:

Original Proceedings - Habeas Corpus.
Brooks v. State, 636 So. 2d 518, 1994 Fla. App. LEXIS 2348 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Petitions for writ of habeas corpus dismissed as unauthorized.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates sought writs of habeas corpus, wherein they collaterally attacked their noncapital convictions for various crimes. The three petitions were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The inmates were each convicted of assorted crimes and each sought a writ of habeas corpus, based on issues regarding improper qualification or swearing in of prospective jurors, improper entry of a guilty plea, and a conflict of interest with trial counsel. The court indicated that the instant petitions were representative of many that were filed in the court, and that in the future, it would not continue to either transfer the petitions to lower courts for consideration as motions for postconviction relief or deny them on the merits or due to a procedural bar. Rather, the court concluded that the proper procedural maneuver would be to dismiss such petitions as unauthorized. In a thorough review of the history of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, the court noted the balance between the constitutional right to seek a writ of habeas corpus, pursuant to Fla. Const. art. I, § 13, and the institutional needs of the Florida courts system. Rather than continue to encourage misfiled applications to the court which were properly to be made under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 to the sentencing court, the court determined to dismiss unauthorized petitions.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petitions.

 

588 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Giorgetti


No. SC02-1812


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


868 So. 2d 512; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 308; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 95



March 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance.

Fourth District - Case No. 4D00-3594.

(Broward County).
Giorgetti v. State, 821 So. 2d 417, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 10065 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Revised certified question answered in affirmative. Decision approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of violating Florida's sexual offender registration statutes, Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435(4) and 944.607(9). The State subsequently appealed the judgment of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that reversed and remanded the trial court's decision, holding that the State was required to prove defendant's knowledge of the registration provisions of the statutes.


OVERVIEW: After defendant had served both his incarceration and parole time following a conviction for indecent assault, defendant moved, and was subsequently arrested when a police officer discovered defendant had not registered as a sex offender. Defendant pleaded not guilty to the charges, claiming he was not aware of the registration requirements, and he subsequently challenged the constitutionality of the sexual offender registration statutes based on the absence of a knowledge requirement. The trial court denied defendant's pretrial constitutional challenge. At trial the State asked for, and the trial court gave, a jury instruction explaining that the State was not required to prove that the statute had an element of knowledge or that defendant intended to violate the statute. In evaluating the language of the statutes, there was no such indication of legislative intent to dispense with mens rea. The public welfare offense rationale offered by the State did not apply to the sexual offender registration statutes. As such, due process required that the State demonstrate that defendant had knowledge of the requirements to register under the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and a new trial was ordered to be conducted.

 

589 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Cardenas v. State


No. SC02-1264, No. SC02-927


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


867 So. 2d 384; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 260; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 90



February 26, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases Consolidated: No. SC02-1264 - Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 1D00-3833; (Escambia County). No. SC02-927 - Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Fifth District - Case No. 5D00-1717; (Citrus County).
Cardenas v. State, 816 So. 2d 724, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 6122 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2002)
Bonine v. State, 811 So. 2d 863, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 4084 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two consolidated cases, the first in the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) and the other in the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), presented two questions concerning a jury instruction in prosecutions for driving or boating under the influence. The first issue was whether giving the standard jury instruction on the presumption of impairment was fundamental error and second, if preserved, whether the error was harmful per se.


OVERVIEW: One lower court of appeal concluded that giving the standard instruction on the presumption of impairment contrary to Miles was not fundamental error that could be raised initially on appeal. The other lower court of appeal determined that it was harmful error per se. The first case involved boating under the influence. The second case involved driving under the influence. In the first case, the trial court gave the standard jury instruction that provided two alternative methods in which to prove the crimes charged. It also gave the standard jury instruction on the presumptions of impairment contained in the implied consent law. The second court also instructed the jury on the presumption of impairment. The juries in both cases utilized a general verdict form in finding defendants guilty. The supreme court held that the improper instruction did not constitute fundamental error when the jury was instructed on either driving with an unlawful blood- or breath-alcohol level (DUBAL) or actual impairment, or both. Where the evidence of actual impairment was strong, the jury could choose to rely in part or whole on the presumption of impairment instruction.


OUTCOME: The conclusion that giving a standard instruction on the presumption of impairment was not fundamental error was approved. The holding that such an error was harmless solely because of overwhelming evidence of actual impairment was not approved. Thus, the decision in the second case was quashed and the matter was remanded for affirmance of defendant's conviction.

 

590 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Haire v. Fla. Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs.


Nos. SC03-446 & SC03-552


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


870 So. 2d 774; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 187; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 67



February 12, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Haire v. Fla. Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs., 2004 Fla. LEXIS 540 (Fla., Apr. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-2584 & 4D02-3315. (Broward County).
Fla. Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs. v. Haire, 836 So. 2d 1040, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 227 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Decision approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tree owners challenged the decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed a trial court's decision and expressly declared the Citrus Canker Law, Fla. Stat. ch. 581.184 (2003) constitutional under U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV and Fla. Const. art, I, § 9 and which held that it was permissible for a magistrate to issue a single warrant for multiple properties and to use an electronic signature.


OVERVIEW: The owners' citrus trees had been destroyed or were targeted for destruction by respondent, the Florida Department of Agriculture and Consumer Services, to prevent the spread of citrus canker. Affirming, the court held that: (1) the appellate court properly applied the reasonable relationship test because the state paid compensation for trees that were destroyed; (2) under the reasonable relationship test, the trial court improperly substituted its judgment for that of the legislature, which determined that the 1,900-feet eradication zone was justified by the best available science, and the Citrus Canker Law did not violate the owners' rights to substantive due process; (3) the lack of a pre-deprivation hearing did not deny the owners a meaningful opportunity to be heard on the propriety of the Department's removal order because summary eradication of the disease was warranted; and (4) pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 933, it was within the magistrate's discretion to decide both whether to issue a single warrant to search multiple properties based on a single application, and whether to use an electronic signature.


OUTCOME: The court approved the appellate court's decision, which declared the Citrus Canker Law constitutional and quashed the trial court's orders placing restrictions on the Department's ability to obtain search warrants.

 

591 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Children & Families v. Sun-Sentinel, Inc.


No. SC03-410


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


865 So. 2d 1278; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 161; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 55



February 5, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 19, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict Fourth District - Case No. 4D02-4466; (Palm Beach County).
Dep't of Children & Families v. Sun-Sentinel, Inc., 839 So. 2d 790, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 1841 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Confidential public records.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspaper sought access to certain public, but confidential, records maintained by respondent, the Department of Children and Families (DCF), pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 119.07(7)(a) (2002). Upon direct conflict with two cases from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), this matter followed.


OVERVIEW: At issue before the instant court was whether: (1) DCF waived its objection to personal jurisdiction when it simultaneously moved to transfer venue; (2) the newspaper was required to serve DCF with the petition; and (3) the circuit court erred in refusing to apply the home venue privilege. The district court held that DCF waived its objection by seeking a transfer of venue. The court also held that the circuit court did not err in refusing to apply the home venue privilege, even though none of the recognized exceptions to the privilege were satisfied. The instant court first held that a motion to transfer venue, filed simultaneously with an objection to personal jurisdiction, did not waive the jurisdictional objection. Second, Fla. Stat. ch. 119.07(7)(a) required formal service of process on DCF. Thus, the circuit court erred in denying DCF's motion to dismiss the petition for insufficient service of process and lack of personal jurisdiction. Finally, a fourth exception to the home venue privilege was created similar to the joint tortfeasor exception. Because the case fell within this new exception, the circuit court did not err in refusing to apply the home venue privilege.


OUTCOME: The judgment regarding the waiver of jurisdiction was disapproved. The judgment of the circuit court denying DCF's motion to dismiss for insufficient service of process and lack of personal jurisdiction was erroneous. Finally, the circuit court's judgment regarding the home venue privilege was not erroneous.

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by Robinson v. Crosby, 540 U.S. 1171, 157 L. Ed. 2d 1225, 124 S. Ct. 1197, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 1000 (U.S., Feb. 4, 2004).

P. 3.851 after he was convicted of various offenses, sentenced to death, and an active death warrant was signed. Defendant also filed a successive petition for a writ of habeas corpus, which was consolidated with the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction, death sentence, and the denial of his first postconviction motion for relief were previously affirmed on appeal. Sullivan v. Sapp


No. SC02-2490


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


866 So. 2d 28; 2004 Fla. LEXIS 5; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 15



January 15, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal--Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District--Case No. 1D02-450.
Sullivan v. Sapp, 829 So. 2d 951, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 15656 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2002).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant maternal grandmother, who had intervened in a collateral matter to a paternity determination and had sought visitation with a child, sought review of the judgment of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) which expressly declared Fla. OVERVIEW: The father was declared to be the natural father in a paternity action. A provision was included regarding income tax exemptions. However, the grandmother's issue of visitation was no longer the matter in litigation and her motion to intervene was properly denied. Fla. PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, William C. Johnson, Jr., Judge - Case No. CF91-06795-CFAES and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Guzman v. State, 721 So. 2d 1155, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1892 (Fla., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Postconviction relief denied; habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's petition for post-conviction relief, filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate appealed said order, and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate challenged the judgment entered and sought further relief. However, the instant court held that the post-conviction court's resolution of the Giglio claim failed to consider whether there was a reasonable likelihood that the false evidence regarding the payment could have affected that court's judgment. Nor did that court find that the State had demonstrated that the false evidence was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Second, the inmate was not entitled to relief on his Brady claim, as he failed to show that the State deprived him of evidence which it believed to be exculpatory. Likewise, there was no merit to the claim that the State committed a Brady violation by failing to disclose that the hair evidence had been destroyed. Further, the inmate failed to show that such was favorable to him. Because the inmate's counsel reasonably discounted the evidentiary value of the hair sample, he was not constitutionally ineffective. Third, the inmate's claims of misconduct were procedurally barred as they could have and should have been raised on direct appeal. Finally, the inmate failed to show he was entitled to habeas relief, and that his claims were ripe for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded on the third prong of the Giglio claim for post-conviction relief. Further, the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Davis v. State

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Randall G. McDonald, Judge - Case No. CF94-1248A1-XX and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.

DISPOSITION: Post-conviction relief denied; habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed his conviction and sentence of death by the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida) for the murder of an 11-year-old child. The Supreme Court of Florida had affirmed the conviction and death sentence. The inmate appealed a trial court order denying postconviction relief and petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus alleging ineffective assistance of appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: During the penalty phase, the inmate's trial counsel presented the testimony of 15 witnesses in mitigation. The supreme court determined that the inmate's untaped confession while in his holding cell should have been suppressed. However, the error was harmless as the inmate subsequently gave a taped statement after being Mirandized. The supreme court rejected the other issues raised by the inmate as without merit and affirmed the conviction and death sentence. The inmate's other assertions of ineffective trial counsel were without merit. Finally, the inmate's assertions of ineffective appellate counsel were also without merit, largely because alleged trial errors were not errors.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the denial of the inmate's postconviction motion and denied the petition for habeas corpus.

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Certificate of appealability granted Zakrzewski v. McDonough, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 46865 (N.D. Fla., June 28, 2006)
Post-conviction proceeding at Zakrzewski v. State, 13 So. 3d 1057, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 285 (Fla., Feb. 12, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Zakrzewski v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1283 (Fla., June 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Okaloosa County, G. Robert Barron, Judge - Case No. 94-01283-CF.
Zakrzewski v. State, 717 So. 2d 488, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1051 (Fla., June 11, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Okaloosa County Circuit Court (Florida) sentenced defendant to death for the murder of his wife and two children, which was affirmed on appeal. The court also denied defendant his request for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed this denial.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant's issues questioned whether: (1) his lawyers in the penalty phase provided ineffective assistance of counsel by failing to object to certain closing arguments; (2) his lawyers were ineffective for failing to move to suppress evidence; (3) his guilty pleas were voluntary; and (4) his death sentence was unconstitutional. The appeals court answered each in the negative. First, the trial court properly found that both of defendant's trial counsel were extremely experienced and utilized a defense strategy to forego any objection. Second, the search of defendant's home was justified under the exigent circumstances exception to the warrant requirement. Thus, suppression would have been denied. Third, defendant fully understood both the plea agreement and his discussions with counsel about the admissibility of contested photographs. Finally, the instant court had previously rejected post-conviction challenges to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141. Additionally, the prior violent felony or capital felony conviction aggravator exempted this case from the requirement of jury findings on any fact necessary to render a defendant eligible for the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The order denying relief was affirmed.

 

599 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Ault v. State


No. SC00-863


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


866 So. 2d 674; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1896; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 810



November 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 4, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Ault v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 223 (Fla., Feb. 4, 2004)
Appeal after remand at Ault v. State, 53 So. 3d 175, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 1631 (Fla., 2010)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Transferred by Ault v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 2474 (Fla., Aug. 8, 2014)
Post-conviction proceeding at Ault v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 509 (Fla., Mar. 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Marc H. Gold, Judge - Case No. 96-21248-CF10A.



DISPOSITION: Sentences vacated and convictions affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) convicted defendant of two counts of first-degree murder and imposed two death sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgments entered, first contending that he was entitled to suppression of his statements made following his arrest on an unrelated charge. The appeals court disagreed. Although he was in custody on said charge at the time he invoked his rights, he was not being interrogated, and no interrogation was imminent on the murder case. Thus, his invocation of rights only precluded the police from questioning him about the unrelated charge, not the murders. Second, defendant's claim relating to the dismissal of a potential juror was dispositive. The juror's response that she could put her personal feelings aside and be fair in the guilt and penalty phases even though she opposed the death penalty, satisfied the juror competency standard. Moreover, such error was not subject to harmless error analysis. Third, the aggravating circumstance that the murder was committed in the course of a felony aggravator was constitutional. Finally, if the sentences imposed for defendant's non-capital offenses could not have been lawfully imposed under the 1994 sentencing guidelines, then resentencing in accordance with those guidelines without departure was in order.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed, but the death sentences were vacated, and the matter was remanded for a new penalty phase proceeding before a new jury.

Armstrong v. State


Nos. SC01-1874 & SC02-1122


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


862 So. 2d 705; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1861; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 801



October 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Armstrong v. Crosby, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2254 (Fla., Dec. 19, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Florida v. Armstrong, 541 U.S. 1056, 124 S. Ct. 2161, 158 L. Ed. 2d 757, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3622 (2004)
Decision reached on appeal by Armstrong v. State, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 2255 (Fla., Sept. 22, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, James I. Cohn, Judge-Case No. 90-5417CF-B.
Armstrong v. State, 642 So. 2d 730, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1205 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) of first-degree murder, attempted murder of a law enforcement officer, and armed robbery. The trial court sentenced him to death for the murder conviction and to life imprisonment for the other convictions. He appealed the postconviction court's denial of his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion. He also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and an accomplice killed a police officer and wounded another police officer in a shooting during an armed robbery. The inmate made various allegations of error in his motion for postconviction relief and his petition for habeas corpus relief. The supreme court found that as to his postconviction relief claims (1) there was no merit to his guilt-phase claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel; (2) he failed to satisfy the Brady test, as he did not show a reasonable probability that the outcome of the proceedings would have been different had he been in possession of a witness's statements; and (3) the postconviction court correctly found that his claim that he was rendered effectively absent during a critical stage of the proceedings was procedurally barred. However, a resentencing was necessary on the basis of the invalidation of his prior felony conviction that was introduced at his penalty phase. As to his habeas petition, the supreme court found that he failed to show ineffective assistance of appellate counsel or that he was prejudiced by the absence of a part of the record on appeal.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed in part as to the issues relating solely to the guilt phase of the inmate's trial; however, the death sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing before a new jury on the first-degree murder conviction. The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.
